401 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Walker


1 CA-CR 06-0227


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


215 Ariz. 91; 158 P.3d 220; 2007 Ariz. App. LEXIS 74; 503 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 9



May 8, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR2004-135414-001 DT. The Honorable Warren J. Granville, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted him of possession of equipment and/or chemicals for the purpose of manufacturing a dangerous drug. Specifically, he challenged the denial of his motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: When officers arrived at a probationer's home to serve a probation arrest warrant, they conducted a cursory search of the home. The officers noticed a chemical-type odor coming from a large trunk-like box in the living room. They opened the trunk and found items consistent with manufacturing methamphetamine. A search warrant was obtained, and defendant, the probationer's boyfriend, was charged with several crimes. He was convicted after a motion to suppress evidence was denied. In affirming, the appellate court determined that defendant's search and seizure rights under the Fourth Amendment were not violated due to the probationary search. The probationer had a diminished expectation of privacy; therefore, it was proper to allow for warrantless searches as a condition of probation. Next, a probation search was authorized since there was a reasonable suspicion that the probationer, who was subject to a probation search, was engaged in criminal activity. The scope of such extended to property that the officers had a reasonable suspicion were owned, controlled, or possessed by the probationer. This evidence was properly seized against defendant because he lived at the residence.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

402 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Lincoln v. Holt


1 CA-SA 07-0052


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


215 Ariz. 21; 156 P.3d 438; 2007 Ariz. App. LEXIS 66; 502 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 25



April 26, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Lincoln v. Hon Holt/State ex rel. Thomas, 2007 Ariz. LEXIS 133 (Ariz., Oct. 30, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petition for Special Action from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR2006-009114-001 DT. The Honorable Cathy M. Holt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of an order from respondent, the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona), which denied his motion for a court-ordered deposition of a child's mother after petitioner was charged with abusing the child.


OVERVIEW: A three-year-old child was treated at a hospital for bruising around his eyes. Petitioner was indicted for one count of child abuse for allegedly choking or strangling the child. The State listed the child's mother as a material witness. She was the only witness that would testify that petitioner inflicted the injury. Counsel for petitioner requested an interview with the mother. The mother refused based on the Victims' Bill of Rights and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4433(H) (Supp. 2006). Petitioner's counsel moved for a court-ordered deposition of the mother. The trial court denied the motion. On appeal, the court held that § 13-4433(H) allowed a minor victim's parent or legal guardian who exercised victims' rights on behalf of the minor to also exercise all victims' rights specified in § 13-4433 on the parent or legal guardian's own behalf. That included the right to refuse an interview on the parent or legal guardian's own behalf, not just on behalf of the minor child. Further, § 13-4433(H) was a valid exercise of the authority granted to the legislature by the Victims' Bill of Rights under Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 2.1(D).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

403 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Lopez v. Cole


1 CA-CV 06-0477


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


214 Ariz. 536; 155 P.3d 1060; 2007 Ariz. App. LEXIS 58; 501 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 8



April 12, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 2001-020216. The Honorable F. Pendleton Gaines, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff guardian ad litem filed an action on plaintiff minor's behalf to recover for injuries and for the medical expenses. The suit alleged that defendant grandparents, defendant neighbors, and defendant mother were negligent. The Maricopa County Superior Court, Arizona, granted summary judgment to the grandparents. On remand, judgment was entered against the grandparents. The guardian ad litem appealed on behalf of the minor.


OVERVIEW: The grandparents' children cut a hole in the fence between their property and that of their neighbors, who owned a horse on the adjoining property. On the day of the incident, the mother went inside briefly and when she returned, she could not immediately locate the minor. She discovered that the minor had climbed through the hole and had been kicked in the head by the neighbors' horse. The issue on appeal was whether the claim for medical expenses in this case belonged to the minor's parents and was therefore barred by the two-year statute of limitations, or whether the minor could pursue the claim, and, if so, whether the statute of limitations was tolled pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-502. In sum, the minor urged that a new rule be crafted recognizing that if parents waived their claim to medical expenses by not bringing it within the two-year statutory period, the claim passed to the minor. In this case, the minor did not have a right to a claim for medical expenses unless his parents consented. Because there was no evidence that the minor's parents consented, he had no rights that could be abrogated. The minor could not recover for the cost of medical care he received.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's determination.

 

404 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Polanco v. Indus. Comm'n


2 CA-IC 2006-0025


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


214 Ariz. 489; 154 P.3d 391; 2007 Ariz. App. LEXIS 55; 500 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 8



March 29, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Polanco v. Ica/Pima County, 2007 Ariz. LEXIS 135 (Ariz., Oct. 30, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] SPECIAL ACTION-INDUSTRIAL COMMISSION. ICA Claim No. 20012780067. Insurer No. 20011041WW. Thomas A. Ireson, Administrative Law Judge.



DISPOSITION: AWARD AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee asserted a workers' compensation claim against respondent insurer, which was accepted for benefits. After an accident, the employee petitioned to reopen his claim. An administrative law judge (ALJ) denied the petition to reopen, but awarded additional supportive medical maintenance benefits. The employee brought a statutory special action against the insurer and respondent Industrial Commission of Arizona.


OVERVIEW: The employee injured his back, was awarded benefits, and underwent diskectomy surgery. The employee subsequently suffered an industrial motor vehicle accident in 2004 and had a spinal cord stimulator implanted. The ALJ determined that the employee had failed to demonstrate objective physical findings of a change in his condition as required by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1061(H). The employee argued that the objective physical findings requirement under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1061(H) was unconstitutional as applied to his case under Ariz. Const. art. XVIII, § 8. The court rejected the employee's argument because subjective pain was not an injury within the meaning of Ariz. Const. art. XVIII, § 8, and, therefore, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1061(H) did not unconstitutionally eliminate it as a type of compensable injury. The objective physical findings requirement of § 23-1061(H) did not address either legal or medical causation. That requirement instead made clear that subjective pain alone could not support a petition to reopen a claim. Rather, subjective pain had to directly relate to the degree of impairment resulting from an objective physical change.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award.

 

405 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Stewart v. Carroll


1 CA-CV 06-0240


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


214 Ariz. 480; 154 P.3d 382; 2007 Ariz. App. LEXIS 44; 499 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 27



March 13, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Stewart v. Carroll, 2007 Ariz. LEXIS 77 (Ariz., Sept. 25, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. LC2005-000880-001 DT. The Honorable Margaret H. Downie, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed a special action petition challenging the constitutionality of provisions of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 21-202 (Supp. 2006), allowing prospective jurors 75 and older to opt out of jury service and prohibiting the public disclosure of statements submitted by prospective jurors asking to be excused from service for mental or physical reasons. The Maricopa County Superior Court, Arizona, denied relief. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, who had been cited for violating various state criminal statutes, argued that the opt-out provision set out in § 21-202(C) for prospective jurors 75 and older, violated his Arizona constitutional rights to due process and a fair jury trial. The court concluded that § 21-202(C) did not violate the due process and fail-jury-trial provisions of the Arizona Constitution. Appellant presented no evidence that citizens 75 or over constituted a distinct group, such that allowing them to opt out of jury service would deprive a criminal defendant of the commonsense judgment of the community, would give rise to the appearance of unfairness, or would interfere with the responsibility and right all Americans share in ensuring the fair administration of justice. The court also concluded that the confidentiality provision set forth in § 21-202(B)(1)(c) did not violate the open courts requirement of Ariz. Const. art. II, § 11. The legislature's decision to maintain the confidentiality of medical statements submitted by prospective jurors did not infringe the constitutional requirement of public judicial proceedings; rather, it accommodated legitimate personal privacy rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

406 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Levens


1 CA-CR 05-0969


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


214 Ariz. 339; 152 P.3d 1222; 2007 Ariz. App. LEXIS 34; 498 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 8



February 20, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Levens, 2007 Ariz. LEXIS 117 (Ariz., Sept. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR2005-108790-001 DT. The Honorable Douglas L. Rayes, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A probation officer conducted a search of defendant's home and found four firearms. The officer sought to revoke defendant's probation, and defendant was separately charged with possession of firearms by a prohibited possessor. The State of Arizona appealed after the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) granted defendant's suppression motion and barred the evidence from being used at defendant's trial on the firearms possession charges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was required, as a condition of his probation, to submit to polygraph examinations as part of his post-conviction assessment and treatment program. During a pretest for a polygraph examination, defendant responded affirmatively to a question asking him if he had firearms in his home. The officer conducted the search after the examiner told him that defendant admitted that firearms were present in his home. At the suppression hearing, the superior court excluded evidence showing that defendant had received Miranda warnings prior to the pretest. It ruled that defendant's responses to the mandated polygraph examination were involuntary statements that could not be used against him, either to justify the search or to support the admission of the firearms evidence. The court found reversible error. The officer was not required to provide Miranda warnings because defendant was not in police custody during the examination. There was no evidence that defendant was threatened or otherwise compelled to answer the examiner's incriminating question. He had waived his U.S. Const. amend. V rights by failing to invoke his right against self-incrimination during the polygraph pretest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court's order granting defendant's suppression motion and remanded the case back for further proceedings consistent with its opinion.

Picaso v. Tucson Unified Sch. Dist.


2 CA-CV 2005-0174


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


214 Ariz. 462; 154 P.3d 364; 2007 Ariz. App. LEXIS 24; 497 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 5



February 13, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Picaso v. Tucson Unified Sch. Dist., 2007 Ariz. LEXIS 97 (Ariz., Sept. 25, 2007)
Vacated by Picaso v. Tucson Unified Sch. Dist., 2007 Ariz. LEXIS 139 (Ariz., Dec. 3, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. C20022430. Honorable Richard S. Fields, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother and appellant father brought a wrongful death action against appellee school district. The Superior Court of Pima County, Arizona, held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-807 applied and evidence of the mother's guilty plea to misdemeanor child abuse could be entered into evidence. The mother and the father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parents' 14-month-old child was struck and killed by a school bus. The mother entered a guilty plea to a misdemeanor child abuse charge for not noticing that the child had left the house unsupervised. The parents argued the trial court erred by applying Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-807, applying collateral estoppel (issue preclusion), and admitting evidence of the guilty plea. The appellate court held that when a criminal defendant entered a guilty plea, there was no actual litigation. In Arizona, actual litigation remained a necessary predicate to the application of issue preclusion, pursuant to supreme court authority. The trial court erred by ruling that the mother's guilty plea precluded her from contradicting any issues involved in the plea or explaining her reasons for entering the plea. As to the application of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-807, which the appellate court reviewed de novo, that statute only applied if a criminal defendant was a civil defendant in a subsequent suit. The trial court erred in applying the statute. Finally, Ariz. R. Evid. 403, allowing exclusion of evidence that would waste time or confuse the jury, could not justify the trial court's broad ruling.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the judgment, and the matter was remanded for proceedings consistent with the appellate court's decision.

State v. Ross


1 CA-CR 05-0200


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


214 Ariz. 280; 151 P.3d 1261; 2007 Ariz. App. LEXIS 12; 496 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 14



January 30, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 28, 2007.
Review denied by State v. Ross, 2007 Ariz. LEXIS 115 (Ariz., Sept. 25, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR2004-015337-001 DT. The Honorable Thomas O'Toole, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A grand jury indicted defendant for (1) conflict of interest in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 38-504(B); (2) conflict of interest by attempting to secure a valuable benefit in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 38-504(C) (2001); and (3) obstructing a criminal investigation in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2409 (2001). Defendant was convicted, before the Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, of violating § 38-504(C). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant served as a county assessor. Arizona enacted the Senior Property Valuation Protection Act, also known as Proposition 104. Proposition 104 was designed to protect low-income seniors from ever-rising property valuations. To obtain a tax freeze, a homeowner was required to submit an application with supporting documentation. Materials had indicated that this information would either be kept partially or totally confidential. Defendant took this information and provided it to a mortgage company to be used in a marketing campaign targeting seniors. On appeal, defendant argued that taking and using publicly available information from his own agency for his own business purposes could not be considered using his position to secure any valuable thing or valuable benefit that was of such character as to manifest a substantial and improper influence. The appellate court agreed. A criminal violation of § 38-504(C) had to be based on a duty applicable to the particular public officer with respect to his office. In this case, to the extent defendant had an obligation not to take the information, the obligation did not arise from being the assessor but from the public records law.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the conviction.

Doe v. Arpaio


1 CA-CV 05-0835


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


214 Ariz. 237; 150 P.3d 1258; 2007 Ariz. App. LEXIS 8; 28 A.L.R.6th 809; 496 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 36



January 23, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Request granted Doe v. Arpaio, 2007 Ariz. LEXIS 85 (Ariz., Sept. 25, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Arpaio v. Doe, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 2716 (U.S., Mar. 24, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 2004-009286. The Honorable Barry C. Schneider, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate sued defendant County and sheriff, challenging a prison policy that required a court order before transporting an inmate to receive an elective abortion. The Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) entered judgment in favor of the inmate and permanently enjoined the county from enforcing the policy insofar as it applied to an inmate seeking an abortion. The county timely appealed.


OVERVIEW: The policy represented an exaggerated response to the county's proffered penological concerns and was invalid insofar as it applied to transportation for abortion services. Specifically, there was no evidence that transporting an inmate for an elective abortion increased the risk of a security breach, the financial impact was minimal given the requirement that the inmate reimburse the county for security and transportation costs, and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-820.02(A)(2) (2003) exempted the county from liability for injuries caused by an escaped or escaping prisoner. Moreover, the policy did not help the county avoid violating Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 35-196.02 (2000) as the county expended no public funds for abortion procedures. Alternative means were not available as courts could effectively act as gatekeepers with the ability to overrule an inmate's choice to have an abortion. In addition, accommodating inmates' abortion rights had a de minimis financial impact on the county's jail facilities given that the inmate bore the expense. Finally, there was an alternative to the policy, i.e., administrative consideration of an inmate's request.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

State v. Mangum


2 CA-CR 2005-0384


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


214 Ariz. 165; 150 P.3d 252; 2007 Ariz. App. LEXIS 4; 495 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



January 12, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Mangum, 2007 Ariz. LEXIS 91 (Ariz., Sept. 25, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-20032388. Honorable Paul Tang, Judge, Honorable Charles S. Sabalos, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial before the Superior Court of Pima County, Arizona, defendant was convicted of possession of a deadly weapon by a prohibited possessor. The trial court suspended the imposition of sentence and placed defendant on probation for three years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The charge defendant faced was based solely on his having knowingly possessed a deadly weapon, while serving a term of probation on his misdemeanor domestic violence conviction. The justice court ultimately vacated the underlying conviction on constitutional grounds before this case went to trial. Defendant argued that a prior conviction, used as an element for a new offense, could not be satisfied by an underlying conviction that was constitutionally infirm. Defendant suggested that relief should be granted under Ariz. Const. art. II, § 4. The appellate court rejected that argument for two reasons. First, defendant failed to adequately develop the argument. Second, the one case defendant cited was inapposite, and pertinent Arizona case law refuted defendant's position. Defendant's status offense fell within Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3101(A)(6)(d), not Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3101(A)(6)(b). The appellate court agreed with the State that the prohibited possessor charge was essentially a status offense, and at the time of his arrest, defendant was bound by his as yet unchallenged guilty plea in justice court and by the probation imposed as a result of the plea.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction, suspension of imposition of sentence, and placement on probation were affirmed.

 

411 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Thomas v. Klein


1 CA-SA 06-0173


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


214 Ariz. 205; 150 P.3d 778; 2007 Ariz. App. LEXIS 3; 495 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 35



January 11, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 2005-011300-001 DT. The Honorable Andrew G. Klein, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State challenged a decision from respondent trial judge in the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona), who granted a motion to depose a victim in a criminal case.


OVERVIEW: Real party in interest defendant was charged with aggravated assault, but the indictment was later amended to designate the offense as a Class 1 misdemeanor. Defendant then sought to depose the victim, arguing that he had not committed a criminal offense for purposes of the Arizona Victims' Rights Implementation Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4401 (2001) et seq. The superior court ordered the deposition to proceed, and the State filed this special action proceeding. In vacating the superior court's decision, the appellate court determined that the amended definition of "criminal offense" under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4401(6) (2001) provided that the protections of the Arizona Victims' Bill of Rights, Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 2.1(A)(5) did not apply to certain persons. The Arizona Legislature's power to enact statutes was subject to any limitations imposed by a constitutional provision. It was not allowed to eliminate or reduce the rights otherwise guaranteed. As such, the amended definition of "criminal offense" unconstitutionally limited the categories of victims protected under Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 2.1(A)(5).


OUTCOME: The decision of the superior court was vacated, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

412 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Kromko v. Ariz. Bd. of Regents


1 CA-CV 04-0250


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


213 Ariz. 607; 146 P.3d 1016; 2006 Ariz. App. LEXIS 143; 491 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 8



November 14, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Kromko v. Ariz. Bd. of Regents/State, 2007 Ariz. LEXIS 35 (Ariz., Apr. 17, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 03-021650. The Honorable Rebecca A. Albrecht, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant university students sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona), which dismissed the students' complaint seeking declaratory and injunctive relief against appellees, the state legislature and the Arizona Board of Regents. The students alleged that a decision to raise tuition by almost 40% violated Ariz. Const. art. 11, §§ 6, 10. The trial court found that appellees were immune from suit.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court agreed that the legislature was immune but reversed the finding as to the Board. The plain language of Ariz. Const. art. 11, § 10 did not require the legislature to increase its appropriation to the university system or to keep tuition "as nearly free as possible." The implementing provision of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 15-1661 set the base amount for maintenance of universities. The legislature in setting the annual appropriation exercised its "power of the purse," a legislative function for which it was generally immune from judicial review. There was no indication in the complaint that the legislature did not minimally fund the university system as constitutionally required. However, the Board's authority to set tuition was not unlimited under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 15-1626(A)(5) and could violate Ariz. Const. art. 11, § 6, if the rate were found to be excessive or other than reasonable. Further, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-820.01 did not preclude actions for declaratory or injunctive relief. The court could not say as a matter of law that the complaint alleging a constitutional violation against the Board did not state a claim upon which relief could be granted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision dismissing the students' claims against the legislature but reversed the trial court's decision finding that the Board was immune. The court remanded the matter as to the Board.

 

413 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Thomas v. Talamante


1 CA-SA 06-0193


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


214 Ariz. 106; 149 P.3d 484; 2006 Ariz. App. LEXIS 144; 491 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 14



November 14, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State ex rel. Thomas v. Talamante, 2007 Ariz. LEXIS 39 (Ariz., Apr. 17, 2007)
Related proceeding at State v. Murray, 2009 Ariz. App. Unpub. LEXIS 105 (2009)
Related proceeding at State v. Murray, 2010 Ariz. App. Unpub. LEXIS 497 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Special Action from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR2005-110548-001 SE. The Honorable David M. Talamante, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the State of Arizona, sought a special action from a decision of respondent, a judge of the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona), contending that the trial court erred by precluding the State from introducing in its case-in-chief evidence of a prior conviction of real-party-in-interest (defendant) for a sexual offense in defendant's trial for violent sexual assault pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1423.


OVERVIEW: The State had filed an allegation of historical prior felony convictions pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604, indicating that defendant had a prior felony conviction for sexual assault. The trial court held that the evidence was a sentencing enhancement factor rather than an element of violent sexual assault and was prejudicial under Ariz. R. Evid. 403. The court accepted jurisdiction and vacated the trial court's ruling. The trial court improperly precluded the State from introducing evidence of the prior conviction. The court found that the text of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1423 and the legislative history plainly established the crime of violent sexual assault and that a historical prior felony conviction for a sexual offense was an element of that crime, rather than merely a sentence enhancement. Thus, Ariz. R. Crim. P. 19 had no application because the prior conviction was an element of the offense. The court rejected the argument that allowing the evidence was an unconstitutional encroachment on judicial rule-making authority under Ariz. R. Evid. 403 because the state supreme court had held that evidence establishing an element of the offense could not be kept from the jury.


OUTCOME: The court accepted jurisdiction and granted relief by vacating the trial court's ruling regarding the admissibility of a historical prior felony conviction.

 

414 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Olmstead


No. 1 CA-CR 05-1240


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


213 Ariz. 534; 145 P.3d 631; 2006 Ariz. App. LEXIS 129; 489 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 5



October 26, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Olmstead, 2007 Ariz. LEXIS 27 (Ariz., Mar. 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Coconino County. Cause No. CR2005-0271. The Honorable Danna D. Hendrix, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A grand jury indicted defendant on one count of aggravated assault and he was subsequently convicted. After the defendant agreed to stipulate to his two prior felony convictions, the State did not seek to establish aggravating factors. Although it found three mitigating factors, the Superior Court in Coconino County (Ariz.) court sentenced the defendant to the presumptive term in prison. The defendant made no objection, but timely appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant claimed the lower court erred in failing to impose a mitigated sentence when it found mitigating but not aggravating factors under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-702(D) and that the state's sentencing scheme was unconstitutional. The appellate court held that the fact that the lower court found only mitigating factors and still imposed the presumptive sentence was of no moment unless, in evaluating the amount and substance of the mitigating factors, it abused its considerable discretion in doing so. There was no such abuse of discretion in this case. Although the court was required by § 13-702(D)(2) to consider the defendant's impaired capacity to appreciate the wrongfulness of his actions and to conform his conduct to the law, it was permitted to find that a presumptive term was nevertheless appropriate. The lower court considered the defendant's individual circumstances and imposed a sentence well within its discretion based on the crime and the defendant's criminal history. The defendant failed to explain how § 13-702(D) violated due process, and the appellate court was unable to envision why it would, so it declined to find Arizona's sentencing scheme unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The appellate court upheld the conviction and sentence imposed by the lower court.

 

415 of 1194 DOCUMENTS



Northwest Fire Dist. v. U.S. Home of Ariz. Constr. Co.


2 CA-CV 2006-0061


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


213 Ariz. 489; 143 P.3d 1030; 2006 Ariz. App. LEXIS 116; 487 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 14



September 29, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Northwest Fire Dist. v. US Home of AZ, 2007 Ariz. LEXIS 34 (Ariz., Apr. 17, 2007)
Vacated by Northwest Fire Dist. v. U.S. Home of Ariz. Constr. Co., 2007 Ariz. LEXIS 67 (Ariz., June 29, 2007)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant fire district adopted a resolution to impose a facilities benefit assessment on homes not yet constructed. Appellee construction company refused to pay the assessments on homes they were building, and the district brought an action to force the company to pay the assessment. The Superior Court of Pima County, Arizona, granted summary judgment in favor of the company. The district appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the fire district contended summary judgment in favor of the construction company was improper. The appellate court agreed, finding first that the district properly characterized its facilities benefit assessment as a fee to help pay for the costs of developing facilities from which to provide services to new building construction areas. Whether such assessments were similar in nature to development fees or not, the legislature intended to authorize those assessments when it promulgated Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 48-805(B)(14). Because the legislature specifically considered the scope of § 48-805(B)(14) and did not exclude owners in the process of constructing a home, the appellate court rejected the company's contention that the legislature could not have intended to authorize the district to assess fees against it. Further, the assessment was not a tax as it would not be used to benefit the entire community but, rather, to develop facilities or other resources designed to benefit both those in the process of building homes and those who eventually purchased those homes. Thus, it would be used for the regulation or benefit of the parties upon whom the assessment was imposed.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.


 

416 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Nordstrom v. Cruikshank


2 CA-SA 2006-0056


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


213 Ariz. 434; 142 P.3d 1247; 2006 Ariz. App. LEXIS 109; 486 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 15



September 14, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] SPECIAL ACTION PROCEEDING. Pima County. Cause No. CR-55947.
State v. Nordstrom, 206 Ariz. 242, 77 P.3d 40, 2003 Ariz. LEXIS 126 (Ariz., 2003)



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a pro se memorandum, which was later adopted by appointed counsel, alleging that he was improperly resentenced by respondent judge following appeal of his first-degree murder conviction. The real party in interest, the State, responded. Jurisdiction was granted.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of first degree murder and other offenses. Defendant maintained that, based on Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-703.01 and Ariz. R. Crim. P. 19.1(c), he was entitled to a full and fair aggravation resentencing proceeding. The State asserted that, because Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-703(F)(1) factor was exempt from certain requirements and because the inmate had conceded in his appeal that a resentencing on the (F)(1) factor was not required, the jury did not need to determine whether any aggravating circumstances existed. One factor, the State argued, rendered the inmate death eligible, although a jury was required to impose the death penalty in a felony-murder matter. Arizona's amended statutes required the trier of fact to find whether any aggravating circumstances alleged under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-703(F) existed and whether to impose the death penalty. Nothing in the new statutory scheme permitted a trial judge to direct a verdict against a defendant on alleged aggravating circumstances based on evidence presented at trial. The appellate court found that the judge proceeded or was threatening to proceed without or in excess of jurisdiction or legal authority.


OUTCOME: Special action relief was granted.

 

417 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Garcia v. Browning


2 CA-SA 2006-0040


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


213 Ariz. 598; 146 P.3d 1007; 2006 Ariz. App. LEXIS 104; 486 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 10



September 5, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Reversed by, Remanded by Garcia v. Browning, 214 Ariz. 250, 151 P.3d 533, 2007 Ariz. LEXIS 15 (Ariz., 2007)
Subsequent appeal at, Remanded by State v. Garcia, 2009 Ariz. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1677 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: SPECIAL ACTION PROCEEDING. Pima County. Cause No. CR-20044702.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a special action, petitioner presented the issue whether Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-205 (2006), Arizona's statute on affirmative defenses, enacted as an emergency measure pursuant to Ariz. Const. art. IV, pt. 1, § 1(3), applied to criminal defendants such as petitioner, who allegedly committed first-degree murder before the effective date of the statute but whose case was yet to be tried.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was charged in 2004. In accordance with the version of § 13-205 then in effect, justification defenses were affirmative defenses that a defendant had to prove by a preponderance of the evidence. In 2006, the legislature amended the language of § 13-205 to exclude justification defenses from among the affirmative defenses that could be raised in a criminal action. Respondent judge denied petitioner's motion to instruct the jury in accordance with the current version of the statute. On review, the court first stated that special action jurisdiction was appropriate. It then determined that the legislature intended the statute to apply to pending cases that had not yet gone to trial. Although the court viewed that as a prospective application of the statute, even assuming it could be construed retroactively when applied to defendants who committed offenses before the amendment's effective date, the court found no constitutional or statutory impediment to such an application. Therefore, the court held that § 13-205 applied to defendants like petitioner who allegedly committed offenses before the effective date of the amendment but who had not yet been tried.


OUTCOME: The court accepted special action jurisdiction and granted relief by reversing that portion of the judge's order that essentially found § 13-205 inapplicable.

State ex rel. Thomas v. Rayes


1 CA-SA 06-0006


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


213 Ariz. 326; 141 P.3d 806; 2006 Ariz. App. LEXIS 92; 484 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 30



August 15, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State ex rel. Thomas v. Rayes, 2007 Ariz. LEXIS 2 (Ariz., Jan. 9, 2007)
Vacated by, Remanded by State ex rel. Thomas v. Rayes, 153 P.3d 1040, 2007 Ariz. LEXIS 32 (Ariz., Mar. 20, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Special Action from the Maricopa County Superior Court. Cause Nos. CR 2004-012417-001 DT, CR 2005-119508-001 DT. The Honorable Douglas L. Rayes, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Maricopa County Attorney sought special action review of an order of the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona) directing it to reinstate an expired plea offer after defense counsel failed to communicate it to defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with armed robbery and theft of means of transportation. On August 25, 2005 the county attorney mailed defense counsel proposed plea agreements, however, defense counsel did not discover them in the file until three months later at a trial management conference, after the offer had expired. On review of the trial court's order requiring the county attorney to reinstate the plea offers, the court held that defendant was deprived of effective assistance of counsel when she failed to communicate the plea offers to him. However, the trial court exceeded its authority and violated separation of powers principles under Ariz. Const. art. III when it compelled the county attorney to reinstate the expired plea offer in reliance on the Donald decision. The court held that the proper remedy was to direct the parties to return to the plea negotiation stage.

Town of Gilbert v. Maricopa County


No. 1 CA-CV 06-0309


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


213 Ariz. 241; 141 P.3d 416; 2006 Ariz. App. LEXIS 94; 484 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 27



August 15, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 2006-004754. The Honorable Colin F. Campbell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, granted judgment in favor of appellee town by finding that House Bill 2145 (HB 2145), 2006 Ariz. Sess. Laws ch. 2, § 4, was unconstitutional. Appellant county island residents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ruled that the legislation, which allowed the county island residents to create a county island fire district to obtain fire and emergency services, violated Ariz. Const. art. 4, pt. 2, § 19, and granted the town injunctive relief. The residents argued that HB 2145 did not violate the Arizona Constitution. The appellate court noted that the town had standing to challenge the constitutionality of the legislation because if the fire district could not secure a private provider, the town remained responsible for providing the services. There was clearly a legitimate governmental objective - to provide fire and emergency services to the county island residents. The population classification was rationally related to the legislative's objective of providing fire and emergency services to those in need. The legislature failed to include the county island residents of other towns who were similarly situated but did not have the ability to create their own county island fire district. The remote possibility of only one other entity being able to enter the class in the next 19 years was insufficient to satisfy the third prong of elasticity.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Am. Fedn. & Mun. Emples., AFL-CIO, Local 2384 v. City of Phoenix


1 CA-CV 04-0766


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


213 Ariz. 358; 142 P.3d 234; 2006 Ariz. App. LEXIS 95; 180 L.R.R.M. 2325; 484 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 9



August 15, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by AFL-CIO v. City of Pheonix, 2007 Ariz. LEXIS 6 (Ariz., Jan. 10, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV2002-011886. The Honorable F. Pendleton Gaines, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, granted judgment in favor of appellee city by finding that appellant union's proposed mandatory deductions from non-union workers' wages, or "fair share" proposals, were illegal under Arizona state law. The union appealed; the city cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The union argued that the superior court erred in finding that its "fair share" proposals were illegal under Arizona law; violated the city's "meet and confer" ordinance; and, even if legal, were a permissive rather than mandatory subject of collective bargaining. The appellate court determined that the clear intent of the electorate of Arizona in enacting Ariz. Const. art. 25 and Arizona's "right to work" laws was to ensure the freedom of workers to choose whether to join and participate in a union. Allowing the proposed "fair share" fee would be contrary to that intent as it would render meaningless the distinction between union membership and non-membership. The fact that the union's proposed "fair share" fee may be less than the amount of full union dues was a distinction without a difference; it was the compulsion and not the amount that was important. Because the "fair share" proposals were illegal, the appellate court did not need to decide the other issues raised by the union or by the city in its cross-appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Curtis v. Richardson


1 CA-CV 04-0827


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


212 Ariz. 308; 131 P.3d 480; 2006 Ariz. App. LEXIS 40; 475 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 21



March 23, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Curtis v. Richardson, 2006 Ariz. LEXIS 86 (Ariz., June 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. LC2003-000893-001DT. The Honorable Michael D. Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicant challenged a decision from the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona), which affirmed appellee state agency's decision to deny him a real estate sales license.


OVERVIEW: The applicant unsuccessfully sought a real estate sales license. A hearing was conducted, but the decision was upheld, and this was affirmed on review. The applicant then filed an appeal. On review, the appellate court determined that the superior court did not abuse its discretion by denying the motion to change venue under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-406 (2003). The convenience of witnesses was not an issue because the applicant was not entitled to a trial de novo. A denial under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 32-2153(B)(2) (Supp. 2005) was proper because the applicant's drug/alcohol crimes were reasonably related to the function of a real estate salesman, and they indicated a lack of good character under § 32-2153(B)(7). Finally, the reference to good character was also not impermissibly vague.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

State v. Freitag


1 CA-CR 04-0770


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


212 Ariz. 269; 130 P.3d 544; 2006 Ariz. App. LEXIS 31; 473 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 5



March 14, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected, May 2, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. LC2004-000354-001 DT. The Honorable Michael D. Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in Maricopa County that affirmed his conviction for soliciting an act of prostitution in violation of Phoenix, Ariz., City Code § 23-52(A)(2), and the municipal court's assessment of a fee to appeal the conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed the city's prostitution ordinance, Phoenix, Ariz., City Code § 23-52(A)(2), violated his fundamental constitutional right to engage in adult consensual sexual conduct in light of the United States Supreme Court's holding in Lawrence v. Texas, 539 U.S. 558, 156 L. Ed. 2d 508 (2003), and that the appellate filing fees imposed by the municipal court violated the rights of the accused guaranteed by Ariz. Const. art. II, § 24. The court held that the prostitution ordinance was constitutional because the liberty interest accorded to homosexuals in Lawrence did not extend to all private consensual sexual activity, and the Supreme Court had expressly stated that its holding did not reach other forms of sexual activity, including public conduct and prostitution. The court also found that Arizona courts had never recognized any constitutionally protected fundamental liberty or privacy interest in engaging in commercial sexual activity, even in private. The court held that the municipal court's assessment of the fee violated Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 22-373 (2002) and Ariz. Const. art. II, § 24, which prohibited the collection of a fee from a defendant to pursue a criminal appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court decision affirming defendant's conviction and sentence for soliciting an act of prostitution in violation of the city's prostitution ordinance and held that the city's ordinance was constitutional. However, the court held that the municipal court's assessment of fees to appeal a criminal conviction was not legal, and directed the court to refund the fees to defendant.

COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. C20003514. Honorable Carmine Cornelio, Judge.

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, property owners, challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee county in the owners' suit alleging that the county violated their constitutional due process rights, and the jurisdictional requirements and notice and hearing provisions in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 11-829 and Pima, Ariz., County Code §§ 18.91.060 and 18.91.060(B)(1).

Mutschler v. City of Phoenix


1 CA-CV 04-0203


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


212 Ariz. 160; 129 P.3d 71; 2006 Ariz. App. LEXIS 11; 471 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 5



February 14, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Mutschler v. City of Phoenix, 2006 Ariz. LEXIS 80 (Ariz., June 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV-2003-017925. The Honorable Michael A. Yarnell, Retired Judge.
State v. Mutschler, 204 Ariz. 520, 65 P.3d 469, 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 51 (Ariz. Ct. App., 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, granted judgment in favor of appellee city granting the city's motion to dismiss appellant business owners' regulatory taking claim. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court determined that the owners failed to refute the city's plainly legitimate justification for the city ordinance that made the operation of a live sex act business illegal in the city. The city claimed that its regulatory prohibition of live sex act clubs as public nuisances was not a constitutional taking of property for which the owners were entitled to receive just compensation. The appellate court agreed with the city that the trial court should have ruled on the city's nuisance exception defense as a threshold matter before reaching the Penn Central analysis. The conduct proscribed by Phoenix, Ariz., Ordinance No. G-4145 (Ordinance) could have been prohibited as a common-law public nuisance and a public health hazard. Because the Ordinance did not proscribe a productive use that was previously permissible under relevant nuisance laws, live sex acts fell within the nuisance exception to the Takings Clause. Although the city did license sexually oriented businesses, the owners would not have qualified because that license applied only to adult arcades, cabarets, adult motels and adult theaters.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


211 Ariz. 576; 125 P.3d 396; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 167; 467 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 26



December 22, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV2004-015153. The Honorable Michael A. Yarnell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant political committee filed a special action in the Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, asking the trial court to order appellee city to transmit its referendum petition regarding municipal ordinances setting rates charged for city-owned utility services for voter approval at the next city election. The trial court considered cross-motions for summary judgment and granted judgment to the city. The political committee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city had adopted four ordinances that adjusted its utility rates. The political committee filed an application for a referendum petition to refer the ordinances for voter approval. The trial court held that utility rate making was an administrative act that was not subject to referendum. The political committee argued that the ordinances were legislative acts that were referable because the city passed them to implement a general tax increase, that the city's charter made the referendum applicable to increased utility rates, and that other states had found that setting utility rates was a legislative action subject to the referendum power. The appellate court noted that the city's use of revenues from its utility services to offset other costs of governing did not automatically convert utility rates into a tax and that the city's charter empowered it to enact ordinances to regulate rates charged by public utilities and to fix rates for city-owned utilities. The appellate court held that there were no Arizona statutory or constitutional provisions which conflicted with deciding that municipal rate increases were administrative acts that were not subject to referendum.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Jennifer G. v. Ariz. Dep't of Econ. Sec.


2 CA-JV 2004-0095


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


211 Ariz. 450; 123 P.3d 186; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 162



November 29, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF COCHISE COUNTY. Cause No. MD200300063. Honorable Charles A. Irwin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Granting a motion for summary judgment filed by appellee Arizona Department of Economic Security (ADES), the Superior Court of Cochise County (Arizona), sitting as a juvenile court, severed appellant mother's parental rights pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-533(B)(3) on the grounds of chronic substance abuse and the duration of the children's court-ordered, out-of-home placement pursuant to § 8-533(B)(8)(a). The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued that the juvenile court granted summary judgment based on erroneous factual findings and legal conclusions. ADES's own documents in support of summary judgment invited the court to make credibility determinations and established that the parties' versions of material facts differed. Despite deficiencies in form, the appellate court found that the mother's opposition, when coupled with questions of fact raised by some of ADES's own documents, sufficiently demonstrated the existence of genuine, material factual disputes, and the appellate court disagreed with the juvenile court's apparent conclusion that the "quantum of evidence" was so slight as to justify denying the mother a trial. Though the mother might have been unlikely to prevail at trial, ADES was not entitled to summary judgment because material issues of fact could not be resolved without credibility determinations and weighing of evidence, matters peculiarly and exclusively for a trier of fact. A reasonable trier of fact could have determined that ADES failed to prove by clear and convincing evidence that grounds existed to terminate the mother's parental rights pursuant to § 8-533(B)(3) or (B)(8)(a).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed. The case was remanded.

 

430 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Jeter v. Mayo Clinic Ariz.


1 CA-CV 04-0048


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


211 Ariz. 386; 121 P.3d 1256; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 153; 467 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 5



October 27, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 2003-011775. The Honorable Michael J. O'Melia, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a husband and wife who were patients at a fertility clinic, appealed a decision of the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona), which dismissed their lawsuit against defendant fertility clinic in the couple's action for the alleged negligent destruction of loss of five of the couple's frozen human pre-implantation embryos or pre-embryos, which the clinic agreed to cryopreserve and store.


OVERVIEW: A physician at the clinic harvested eggs from the wife and fertilized them with the husband's sperm. When plaintiffs had the pre-embryos transferred to another clinic, some were missing. The trial court held that plaintiffs failed to state a claim. The court affirmed the dismissal on the wrongful death claim under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-611 because the absence of this prerequisite to "personhood" supported a conclusion that pre-implantation fertilized human eggs were not "persons" for purposes of § 12-611. The court declined to expand the definition of "viability" to a point of "potential viability." Such a decision was best left to elected representatives subject to constitutional restraints. However, the court held that plaintiffs could sue for the negligent loss of their pre-embryos and that it was premature for the superior court to hold that the medical malpractice act barred the claim for breach of fiduciary duty. The act did not shield health care providers from all other negligence actions. If the claim was grounded in the clinic's negligent storage by non-health care personnel, it was arguably not a medical malpractice action under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-562(A).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's dismissal of the wrongful death claim. The court reversed the dismissal of the claim for negligent loss or destruction of the pre-embryos, breach of fiduciary duty and breach of a bailment contract.

 

431 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


In re Manny


2 CA-JV 2005-0001


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


211 Ariz. 301; 120 P.3d 1111; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 140; 463 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



October 18, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. 165513-01. Honorable Michael O. Miller, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Pima County, Arizona, held appellant mother in contempt for violating the court's prior probation order relating to her responsibilities as a juvenile adjudicated delinquent's custodian. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued that the juvenile court erred in sentencing her under the general contempt provisions in Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 12-861 through 12-865 rather than the specific juvenile contempt provisions of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-234. The appellate court concluded that the legislature did not intend to permit juvenile courts to employ the contempt sanctions in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-863 when addressing the willful violation of court orders issued pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-234. The legislature intended to alter the maximum punishment available for the contempt addressed in § 8-234 from that addressed in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-863. Section 8-234 was the more specific of the two provisions. It created the duty that the mother breached and authorized the court's order that the mother later violated. The legislature did not intend to provide superior courts the option of choosing between the two statutes. The appellate court's conclusion that the juvenile court erred by not proceeding under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-234 rendered any deficiencies in trial counsel's understanding of his client's rights pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 12-861 through 12-865 irrelevant and not prejudicial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded with instructions to resentence the mother under the appropriate statute.

 

432 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Ariz. Minority Coalition for Fair Redistricting v. Ariz. Indep. Redistricting Comm'n


1 CA-CV 04-0061


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


211 Ariz. 337; 121 P.3d 843; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 141; 464 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 4



October 21, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 2002-004380; CV02-004882 (Consolidated). The Honorable Kenneth Fields.
Ariz. Indep. Redistricting Comm'n v. Fields, 206 Ariz. 130, 75 P.3d 1088, 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 150 (Ariz. Ct. App., 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a redistricting commission, a group, and several intervenors, challenged a decision of the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona), which ordered the commission to formulate various definitions and standards after finding that a legislative plan did not sufficiently favor competitive voting districts in an action filed by appellees, a coalition state senators and others (coalition), challenging the plan.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether the trial court correctly ruled on constitutional challenges to new voting districts. The trial court utilized the strict scrutiny standard in deciding the equal protection challenges. The court held that there had been no unconstitutional identification of or discrimination against a suspect class warranting strict scrutiny review because the redistricting plans did not impose "severe" restrictions that substantially burdened the right to vote. Further, the coalition did not demonstrate that equal protection principles demanded definitions to prevent the commission from discriminating against some voters. The trial court also erred by ruling that creation of competitive districts was no less important than other goals in Ariz. Const. art. IV, pt. 2, § 1(14)(B) - (E) and that the commission erred in treating competitiveness as a subordinate goal. Also, mere knowledge of the specific residence of an incumbent, without the use of such knowledge to draw boundary lines, could not render a plan unconstitutional. Moreover, it was error to rule that the act of designating a consultant as an expert witness permanently waived the legislative privilege.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that portion of the judgment that invalidated the redistricting plan and ordered the commission to construct a new plan. The court affirmed the portion of the judgment granting summary judgment against a Native-American nation.

Hourani v. Benson Hosp.


2 CA-CV 2004-0155


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


211 Ariz. 427; 122 P.3d 6; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 137



September 27, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Hourani v. Benson Hosp., 2006 Ariz. LEXIS 51 (Ariz., Apr. 20, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF COCHISE COUNTY. Cause No. CV200200261. Honorable Wallace R. Hoggatt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; VACATED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Cochise County (Arizona) that denied the hospital's motion and granted appellee doctor's motion for summary judgment in his appeal of a decision of the hospital's Governing Board that accepted the recommendation of the Appellate Review Committee (ARC) and Medical Staff Executive Committee (MSEC) to revoke the doctor's hospital privileges based on the quality of care.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the doctor was entitled to injunctive relief because there were four procedural defects in the hospital's revocation proceeding and there were no issues of material fact as to the violations. The hospital argued that the trial court was required by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 36-445.02(B) to affirm the decision revoking the doctor's privileges, despite procedural errors, because it was based on substantial evidence. The court rejected the hospital's argument and concluded that § 36-445.02(B) permitted the doctor to bring an action for injunctive relief seeking to correct an erroneous decision or procedure. However the court held that the trial court erred in granting the doctor's motion for summary judgment because there were questions of fact as to whether procedural defects occurred. The court noted that there was no requirement that the hearing officer make recommendations, that the doctor failed to establish bias on the part of an ARC member or that his dual role on the MSEC and ARC constituted an automatic due process violation, and that the bylaws did not prohibit an ARC member from serving on both the MSEC and the Governing Board.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the hospital's motion for summary judgment, but reversed the grant of the doctor's motion for summary judgment on the grounds that factual issues precluded summary judgment. The court remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

State ex rel. Thomas v. Foreman


No. 1 CA-SA 05-0001


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


211 Ariz. 153; 118 P.3d 1117; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 109



September 1, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State ex rel. Thomas v. Foreman, 2006 Ariz. LEXIS 39 (Ariz., Mar. 14, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Special Action from the Maricopa County Superior Court. Cause No. CR 2002-007255. The Honorable John Foreman, Judge.
Phillips v. Araneta, 208 Ariz. 280, 93 P.3d 480, 2004 Ariz. LEXIS 70 (Ariz., 2004)



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Arizona filed a special action to challenge the judgment of the Maricopa County Superior Court, Arizona, declaring that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4426.01 (Supp. 2004) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for first-degree murder and sexual assault. The State filed notice that it would request the death penalty, and indicated that it might offer testimony of the victim's representative during any sentencing aggravation and penalty phases. Defendant unsuccessfully moved to preclude introduction of victim impact evidence, and requested the trial court to declare Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4426.01 unconstitutional. The trial court agreed and found that the statute conflicted with the Sixth, Eighth, and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution. The appellate court ruled that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4426.01 was facially constitutional, and it was premature to evaluate the application of the statute to the facts. The statute afforded the victim's representative a right to present an impact statement to rebut any mitigation evidence at any sentencing penalty phase without disclosing that statement. Defendant did not make any showing that victim impact information existed, or that it would be necessary during the trial or in any sentencing aggravation phase. The trial court erred in determining that the statute was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Jurisdiction was accepted, and the State was granted relief.

436 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Linda V. v. Ariz. Dep't of Econ. Sec.


1 CA-JV 04-0180


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


211 Ariz. 76; 117 P.3d 795; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 91; 458 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 16



August 9, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. JD 12929. The Honorable Pamela J. Franks, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) terminated appellant mother's parental rights to her child after her older child had been abused and murdered by the mother's boyfriend. The court impliedly adopted the interpretation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-533(B)(2) that justified termination if "a child" was abused or neglected by the parent or another and the parent knew or should have known about the abuse or neglect. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued that the department of economic security did not prove by clear and convincing evidence that she abused her daughter and that her boyfriend's murder of her other child should not have been considered. She also argued that the court violated her fundamental rights as a parent. The mother contended that because she did not abuse or neglect her other child, the juvenile court erred in basing its termination order on § 8-533(B)(2). The deceased child was fatally abused, and the younger child was removed because of that abuse; thus the appellate court focused on whether "a child" in the statute meant "the child" who was abused or "another child of the parent" who was not abused. Based on the statutory language and context the court held that § 8-533(B)(2) could mean that parents who abused or neglected their children, or who permitted another person to abuse or neglect their children, could have their parental rights to their other children terminated even though there was no evidence that the other children were abused or neglected. That was the very fact situation that prompted the legislature to change the statute. Thus, statutory grounds existed for termination.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Febles


1 CA-CR 03-0827 PRPC


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


210 Ariz. 589; 115 P.3d 629; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 86; 455 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



July 5, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Febles, 2006 Ariz. LEXIS 53 (Ariz., Apr. 20, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 1996-094189. The Honorable Linda A. Akers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVIEW GRANTED; RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged a judgment of the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) denying his petition for post-conviction relief from his conviction of aggravated assault and first-degree burglary and his concurrent aggravated prison terms of 15 and 21 years, denying his supplemental petition alleging a violation of his Sixth Amendment right to a jury trial and ineffective assistance of counsel, and denying his request for a rehearing.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimed his Sixth Amendment right to a jury trial was violated when the trial court imposed aggravated sentences based on facts not proven to a jury in violation of the rule announced in Apprendi v. New Jersey and Blakely v. Washington. Petitioner also claimed his appellate counsel was ineffective for failing to raise an Apprendi claim on direct appeal. Petitioner argued that he was entitled to relief because Blakely was retroactive to the date that Apprendi was decided and his convictions and sentences were not final at that time. On review, the court held that Blakely did not apply retroactively because it was a new rule of criminal procedure and did not fall within the exceptions to the rule of non-retroactivity; thus, it applied only to cases not yet final on direct review when it was decided. The court rejected the ineffective assistance of counsel claim because petitioner's aggravated sentences did not exceed the statutory maximum; thus, Apprendi did not apply and the outcome of petitioner's appeal would not have changed if the Apprendi claim had been raised.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's request for relief in both the original and supplemental petitions for review.

State v. Brown


2 CA-SA 2005-0011


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


210 Ariz. 534; 115 P.3d 128; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 77; 454 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 21



June 22, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, in part, Review denied by, in part State v. Brown, 2006 Ariz. LEXIS 10 (Ariz., Jan. 4, 2006)
Affirmed by, in part, Remanded by State v. Brown, 2006 Ariz. LEXIS 25 (Ariz., Mar. 16, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] SPECIAL ACTION PROCEEDING. Santa Cruz County Cause No. CR-01-199.
State v. Brown, 205 Ariz. 325, 70 P.3d 454, 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 106 (Ariz. Ct. App., 2003)



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a special action proceeding, petitioner State of Arizona contended that respondent judge of the Superior Court of the State of Arizona, in and for the County of Santa Cruz, abused his discretion by finding that statements made by real party in interest criminal defendant in establishing his guilty plea to reckless manslaughter were not admissions of facts for purposes of the U.S. Supreme Court's decision in Blakely v. Washington.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot and killed his mother and shot his father and brother, injuring them. Pursuant to a plea agreement, he pled guilty to reckless manslaughter in exchange for the State's dismissal of the remaining charges. Defendant established the factual basis for the plea at the change-of-plea hearing, describing what had occurred the night of the shootings. The judge deferred accepting the plea until sentencing. The State then alleged aggravating circumstances, but the judge found Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 13-702 and 13-702.01 unconstitutional insofar as they permitted judges to impose a prison term based on facts in aggravation found by a judge rather than a jury. The state sought special action relief. The court concluded that the judge did not abuse his discretion in finding that statements defendant made during the change-of-plea colloquy were not admissions of fact for purposes of Blakely, adding that defendant did not knowingly, voluntarily, and intelligently waive his right to a jury trial on the aggravating circumstances. The court found that the judge erred in ruling that the State could not prove to a jury beyond a reasonable doubt the aggravating circumstances it alleged.


OUTCOME: The court accepted jurisdiction and granted relief in part by vacating the part of the judge's ruling that determined that the State could not prove to a jury beyond a reasonable doubt the aggravating circumstances it alleged. The court ruled that a judge had the authority to conduct such a trial, and the sentencing statutes could be applied in a constitutional manner.

Fragoso v. Fell


2 CA-SA 2005-0001


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


210 Ariz. 427; 111 P.3d 1027; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 64; 451 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 39



May 10, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Motion granted by Fragoso v. Hon. Fell/State of Ariz., 2005 Ariz. LEXIS 91 (Ariz., Sept. 27, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Pima County Cause No. CR-20042912.



DISPOSITION: RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent judge, in the underlying proceeding, imposed a "cash-only" restriction on a pretrial release bond. Petitioner, a defendant in the underlying proceeding, sought special action relief. Jurisdiction over the special action was accepted.


OVERVIEW: The trial judge initially set bail at $ 250,000, to be paid in cash; the trial court later reduced bail to $ 50,000, to be paid in cash. Petitioner's motion to modify was denied. In his request for special action relief, petitioner argued that Ariz. Const. art. II, § 22, Ariz. R. Crim. P. 7.2, and Ariz. R. Crim. P. 7.3 prohibited "cash-only" conditions of bail. The appellate court rejected this argument; it held that Arizona law did not prohibit a "cash-only" condition on bail. The appellate court, in its analysis, first addressed the meaning and scope of the pertinent Arizona statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3967, and rules 7.2 and 7.3. The appellate court determined the statute was clear and definitive, expressly authorizing a trial court to impose a deposit of cash as a required condition of bail. The rule of lenity did not apply because the statute was not ambiguous. Turning next to the constitutional argument, the appellate court noted that there was no basis for concluding that the drafters of the state's constitution intended to foreclose a cash-only restriction. The judge acted within his legal authority in denying the motion to set a secured appearance bond.


OUTCOME: The appellate court denied the requested relief.

Naslund v. Indus. Comm'n of Ariz.


1 CA-IC 02-0084


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


210 Ariz. 262; 110 P.3d 363; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 57; 450 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 18



April 21, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Naslund v. Ica/Maricopa Co/Tristar, 2005 Ariz. LEXIS 115 (Ariz., Oct. 24, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Special Action--Industrial Commission. ICA CLAIM NO. 94231-5804-49. CARRIER NO. 94C0045. Administrative Law Judge Michael A. Mosesso.



DISPOSITION: AWARD SET ASIDE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee sought review of a decision by respondent, the Industrial Commission of Arizona (ICA), that denied the employee's claim for temporary partial disability (TPD) benefits. The employee's TPD compensation benefit was reduced to zero due to the application of an amendment to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1044(A) that required that 50 percent of retirement benefits received during the period of TPD be considered as wages able to be earned.


OVERVIEW: Prior to the amendment to § 23-1044(A), the employee was forced to retire because of a work-related injury. After the amendment was enacted, the employee became eligible for TPD benefits, but the amendment reduced the employee's benefit to zero. Because the employee did not have a vested right to TPD benefits prior to the amendment, the court rejected the employee's contention that the amendment was erroneously applied retroactively. The court also determined that the amendment did not waive or assign workers' compensation benefits in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 23-1025(A) or 23-1068(A) (Supp. 2004). The court concluded that the amendment to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1044(A) violated Ariz. Const. art. XVIII, § 8 and was therefore void because the amendment reduced the amount of compensation to which the employee would have otherwise been entitled and the amendment was not approved by Arizona voters. Because the ICA decision was based on the application of the unconstitutional amendment, the ICA award was set aside.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the ICA award that denied TPD benefits to the employee.
