State v. Aleman


2 CA-CR 2003-0075


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


210 Ariz. 232; 109 P.3d 571; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 52; 449 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



April 4, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PINAL COUNTY. Cause No. 2000026839. Honorable Gilberto V. Figueroa, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of Pinal County (Arizona) of two counts of second-degree murder, four counts of aggravated assault, and three counts of aggravated driving while under the influence of an intoxicant (DUI). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erroneously denied his pretrial motion to suppress evidence of blood test results. The court of appeals disagreed. In addition to observing open beer containers in and around defendant's car, emergency personnel who attended to him at the scene told police they had detected the odor of intoxicants on his breath. Moreover, the "distinct strong odor" of alcohol emanating from defendant's position in the driver's seat became even stronger when he attempted to speak to the deceased front-seat passenger. The accident occurred in broad daylight when defendant crossed the centerline and collided head-on with the oncoming van. The record reflected no circumstances other than defendant's impairment to explain the collision. Therefore, the officer had probable cause to believe that defendant had been driving under the influence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

442 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Poshka


2 CA-CR 2003-0123


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


210 Ariz. 218; 109 P.3d 113; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 50; 448 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



April 1, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Tyla Naureen Poshka, 2005 Ariz. LEXIS 120 (Ariz., Nov. 29, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-20022605. Honorable Kenneth Lee, Judge, Honorable Paul E. Tang, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Pima County, Arizona, convicted defendant of aggravated driving under the influence of alcohol (DUI) with a suspended or revoked driver's license and one count of aggravated driving with a blood alcohol concentration (BAC) of .08 or more with a suspended or revoked driver's license. The trial court suspended the imposition of sentence and imposed concurrent, five-year terms of probation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1381 was unconstitutional and violated her due process rights. The appellate court noted that because the statute provided fair notice of what constituted a punishable BAC level, it should not be declared void for vagueness simply because it might be difficult for the public to determine how far they could go before they were in actual violation. While results from a test administered after a significant period of time or which were subject to other factors creating scientific inaccuracy may inject evidentiary problems, those were matters for the fact finder to resolve. The statute's terms were unambiguous and precise in identifying the prohibited conduct --having a BAC of .08 or higher within two hours of driving a vehicle. Defendant lacked standing to bring an overbreadth claim as she did not allege that the statute substantially infringed upon protected First Amendment freedoms or that she was a member of a class of innocent defendants. Elimination of the affirmative defense provision did not render it unconstitutional as the State was not relieved from proving that defendant's BAC was .08 or greater within two hours of driving.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

443 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Lamparella v. Lamparella (In re Estate of Lamparella)


1 CA-CV 04-0124


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


210 Ariz. 246; 109 P.3d 959; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 46; 454 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



March 29, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. PB 02-090096. The Honorable Lindsay Best Ellis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner life insurance company filed a petition with the probate court to deposit disputed annuity policy benefits with the probate court. Appellant wife and appellee husband's estate filed competing claims for the annuity proceeds. The estate eventually moved for summary judgment. The Maricopa County Superior Court, Arizona, ruled in favor of the estate, but it denied the estate's attorney fee request. The parties cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The husband applied for an annuity, which named the wife as the beneficiary. Three years later, the wife filed a pro per petition for marital dissolution. The couple jointly filled out a section describing community property and debts. The annuity policy, however, was not addressed. The wife attempted to argue that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 14-2804(A) (1995) was inapplicable because the husband had made an affirmative decision to retain her as the policy's beneficiary by not removing her as the beneficiary after entry of the dissolution decree. She also asserted that she was entitled to a community property share of the proceeds pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 25-318(B) (Supp. 2004). The policy was not omitted property under § 25-318(B). Section 25-318(B) did not apply when a decree effectuated an explicit property settlement agreement that disposed of all of the parties' marital assets. Also, the automatic revocation mandated by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 14-2804 (1995) could not be avoided by spousal inaction. Pursuant to § 14-2804, the husband's designation of the wife as the beneficiary under the annuity policy was automatically revoked upon entry of the dissolution decree.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the probate court's decision awarding the annuity proceeds to the husband's estate. The appellate court also affirmed the probate court's decision denying the estate's request for fees, but the appellate court reversed the probate court's decision denying court costs.

State v. Storholm

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 2003-008591-001 DT. The Honorable M. Jean Hoag, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted him of both aggravated driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor (DUI) and aggravated driving with an alcohol concentration of .08 or more in his body within two hours of driving a motor vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated DUI and aggravated driving with an alcohol concentration of .08 or more in his body within two hours of driving a motor vehicle. The trial court placed defendant on probation for two years on each count, to run concurrently. The trial court also sentenced defendant to four months of incarceration as a condition of probation on the first count. On appeal, defendant asserted that due process required law enforcement to provide DUI suspects their own breath samples for independent testing. Moreover, the record failed to show that defendant even attempted to obtain independent testing of his breath. Thus, the practical difficulty that defendant identified in obtaining an independent breath sample failed to create a due process violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

Griffith Energy, L.L.C. v. Ariz. Dep't of Revenue


1 CA-TX 04-0007


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T


210 Ariz. 132; 108 P.3d 282; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 43; 448 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 25



March 22, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT FOR PUBLICATION - RULE 28, ARIZONA RULES OF CIVIL APPELLATE PROCEDURE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Changed to Opinion By Order Filed March 18, 2005.
Companion case at Duke Energy Arlington Valley, LLC v. Ariz. Dep't of Revenue, 2008 Ariz. App. LEXIS 110 (Ariz. Ct. App., July 15, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Arizona Tax Court. Cause No. TX 03-000002. The Honorable Paul A. Katz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Tax Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed a judgment of the Arizona Tax Court that granted summary judgment in favor of defendant Arizona Department of Revenue (ADOR) and upheld the ADOR's adoption, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-14156(3) (Supp. 2004), of a 25-year valuation table for depreciating personal property at electric generation plants, and that denied the taxpayer's post-trial motion. The taxpayer owned an electric generation plant.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer argued that the ADOR should have adopted a 15-year valuation table for depreciating personal property rather than the 25-year table adopted by the ADOR. The tax court found that the ADOR did not act arbitrarily in adopting the 25-year table. On appeal, the taxpayer argued that the tax court erred by applying the arbitrary standard of review rather than a de novo standard of review. The court held that the tax court did not err by employing the arbitrary standard of review. The court noted that a valuation challenge could encompass a claim under the "obsolescence provision," Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-14156(A)(4), which would have required the de novo standard of review but that the taxpayer did not raise any issues to the tax court concerning the obsolescence provision. Rather, the only issue raised by the taxpayer was the ADOR's adoption of the 25-year table. The court found that the record reflected that ADOR selected the 25-year table based on a rational basis and after due investigation and that the taxpayer presented no evidence contesting that the ADOR engaged in the investigation or disputing that the selection of the 25-year table had a rational basis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the tax court judgment.

 

446 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


In re Daniel A.


1 CA-JV 04-0181


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


210 Ariz. 162; 108 P.3d 941; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 40; 447 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 5



March 15, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. JV 531242. The Honorable M. Jean Hoag, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile admitted to attempted unlawful use of means of transportation, unlawful use of means of transportation, simple assault, and probation violations. The Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona entered a disposition committing appellant to the Arizona Department of Juvenile Corrections (ADJC) for a minimum of six months. Appellant challenged the disposition.


OVERVIEW: Prior to disposition in this matter, appellant had a number of referrals to juvenile court for various offenses with a range of offense levels. The juvenile court not only ordered commitment, but directed appellant to attend school, and it also ordered appellant to attend programs for substance abuse and anger management. Appellant submitted two contentions on appeal: (1) the disposition was unlawful; and (2) the commitment violated his constitutional right to be free from cruel and unusual punishment. Appellant contended that the juvenile court's error in attempting to direct ADJC as to the terms of confinement required the appellate court to vacate the entire disposition. The appellate court agreed that the juvenile court could not direct the ADJC to provide specific services to a juvenile during commitment. This error did not, however, invariably require that the commitment decision be vacated. The juvenile court clearly stated that the only option for appellant was commitment, a determination supported by the record. The defect in the disposition was remedied by deleting the directions.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the juvenile court's disposition, as modified.

 

447 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Estrada


1 CA-CR 03-0914


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


210 Ariz. 111; 108 P.3d 261; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 38; 446 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 30



March 4, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Amended by Order filed March 10, 2005.
Review denied by State v. Estrada, 2005 Ariz. LEXIS 98 (Ariz., Sept. 27, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 2003-012565-001 DT. The Honorable Eileen Willett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of burglary in the third degree and possession of burglary tools. The Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, sentenced him to aggravated prison terms of 11 years and 4 years, respectively, to be served concurrently. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Before imposing defendant's sentence, the trial court found four aggravating circumstances, including defendant's history of prior felony convictions, and one mitigating circumstance. Defendant argued that the judicial determination of aggravating circumstances denied him the Sixth Amendment's jury-trial guarantee. Because several of defendant's convictions occurred within 10 years preceding the date of his current offenses, the trial court was required, under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-702(C)(11) (2001), to consider them as aggravating factors, which exposed him to maximum sentences of 12 and 4.5 years, respectively, based solely on the facts reflected in the jury verdicts. Because the sentences imposed by the trial court did not exceed these maximums, the three additional aggravating factors were not facts legally essential to the punishment; thus, defendant had no legal right to have a jury determine their existence. Hence, the trial court did not violate defendant's jury-trial guarantee when it considered additional aggravating factors not found by the jury, weighed them against the sole mitigating circumstance, and imposed aggravated sentences within the authorized ranges.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentences were affirmed.

Grand Canyon Trust v. Ariz. Corp. Comm'n


1 CA-CV 04-0079


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


210 Ariz. 30; 107 P.3d 356; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 20; 446 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 20



February 22, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Grand Canyon Trust v. Ariz. Corp. Comm'n, 2005 Ariz. LEXIS 72 (Ariz., June 28, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 03-000436. The Honorable Ruth Harris Hilliard, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff nonprofit organizations appealed from the decision of the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona), affirming a decision of defendant, the Arizona Corporation Commission, authorizing the construction of a fourth coal-powered electric generating unit at intervenor power company's generating station.


OVERVIEW: Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 40-360.07(B) required the Commission, upon a challenge to a decision of the Siting Committee concerning a certificate of environmental compatibility, to balance, in the broad public interest, the need for an adequate, economical, and reliable supply of electric power with the desire to minimize the effect on the environment and the ecology of Arizona. However, that balancing was not required in every case. It was only required when a party requested that the Commission review the Siting Committee's written decision concerning a certificate of environmental compatibility (CEC) within 15 days of its issuance. However, even if the statute did not require that the balancing occur in the present case, one of the conditions placed in the CEC itself did require the statutory balancing. But, the appellate court found that the testimony introduced at the Commission hearing constituted substantial evidence of the need for the power from the fourth unit when balanced with the desire to minimize the environmental and ecological costs to Arizona. Thus, the Commission's decision authorizing the construction of the fourth unit was not erroneous.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

449 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Goddard v. Gravano


1 CA-CV 03-512, 1 CA-CV 03-822 (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


210 Ariz. 101; 108 P.3d 251; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 19; 445 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



February 17, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 00-007692. The Honorable Mark R. Santana, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, the State of Arizona, filed an in personam and in rem civil forfeiture suit against appellant property owner pursuant to the Arizona Racketeering Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2314, and the Arizona Forfeiture Reform Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 13-4301 to -4315 (1999) The Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, granted a partial summary judgment and awarded attorneys' fees and costs for the State. The property owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owner moved to Arizona, where she bought a home and a restaurant. Although the property owner claimed that she had divorced her husband, the State maintained that they were still married. The property owner was functioning as a drug enterprise's banker. The complaint alleged that the property owner participated in the transfer of an organized crime family's proceeds to Arizona. The property owner claimed that the forfeiture proceedings at issue violated the Double Jeopardy Clause, U.S. Const. amend. V. The appellate court determined that the forfeiture statutes were civil in nature, not criminal. Moreover, because the forfeiture was foreseeable, it was not a violation of the Excessive Fines Clause. The double jeopardy provision of Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 10 was interpreted in a parallel manner to its federal counterpart. The appellate court further concluded that Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 16 was not violated because the forfeiture was triggered only by racketeering conduct as defined in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2301(D)(4). Finally, the award of attorneys' fees and costs was based upon the actual expenditure of government resources; therefore, it was not punishment.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the superior court's judgment.

Martin v. Schroeder


2 CA-CV 2004-0092


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which denied his motion for summary judgment and awarded summary judgment to defendant parents in a negligence action.


OVERVIEW: Because the parents' son, a security guard, was not 21 years old, and could not legally purchase a handgun himself, he asked the parents to purchase a gun for him so that he could receive an increase in pay. The mother purchased a gun for him. Despite the son's use of marijuana in the past, the mother believed that he was no longer using marijuana. Later, plaintiff and the son were smoking marijuana and the son accidentally shot plaintiff in the head. Plaintiff sued the parents, alleging they were liable for his injuries because they purchased the gun that was used in the shooting and had given it to the son, knowing he was a drug abuser. The trial court denied plaintiff's motion for summary judgment and granted the parents' motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court found that plaintiff failed to raise a genuine issue of material fact concerning whether the parents knew or should have known the son was using marijuana when they purchased the gun. Plaintiff also failed to show that, at the time the parents gave the son the gun, they knew or had any reason to believe that he was an "unlawful user" within the meaning of 18 U.S.C.S. § 922.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

Baker v. Ariz. Dep't of Revenue


1 CA-TX 03-0006


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T


209 Ariz. 561; 105 P.3d 1180; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 14; 446 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



February 3, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected March 4, 2005.
Review denied by Baker v. ADOR, 2005 Ariz. LEXIS 113 (Ariz., Oct. 24, 2005).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Arizona Tax Court. Cause No. TX 02-000118. The Honorable Paul A. Katz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers requested additional tax credits that would have been available under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 43-1086 (repealed 2004). A hearing officer of defendant Arizona Department of Revenue (ADOR) denied the claim, the ADOR's director sustained the denial, and the taxpayers appealed. The Arizona Tax Court granted summary judgment for ADOR. The taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: 2000 Ariz. Sess. Laws ch. 405 created enhanced tax credits and other benefits for persons who owned vehicles powered by alternative fuel. Taxpayers could obtain a new 100 percent tax credit for the cost of alternative fuel vehicle (AFV) conversions plus additional credits. Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 43-1086 was amended to allow a minimum $ 30,000 tax credit for the conversion of a vehicle over 12,000 pounds in weight. The taxpayers ultimately bought four used motor homes for conversion. Unforeseen costs to the state, however, forced a moratorium on the program. Nevertheless, the taxpayers filed their income tax return and received the full cash value of those tax credits. They later amended their return to request additional credits. The appellate court noted that the taxpayers failed to prove: (1) the existence of a contract, and (2) an unconstitutional impairment of that contract. The enactment of the statutes did not create a contract. Further, no due process violation occurred because the tax provisions did not create vested rights. The later version of the law, however, did allow recovery of 100 percent of costs, and it allowed the taxpayers to retain profits.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Alvarez


2 CA-CR 2002-0084


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


210 Ariz. 24; 107 P.3d 350; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 39; 447 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 29



January 24, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Redesignated as Opinion by Order date March 9, 2005.
Review granted by, in part State v. Alvarez, 2005 Ariz. LEXIS 127 (Ariz., Nov. 29, 2005)
Remanded by State v. Alvarez, 2006 Ariz. LEXIS 96 (Ariz., July 10, 2006)
Modified by, On remand at State v. Alvarez, 143 P.3d 668, 2006 Ariz. App. LEXIS 115 (Ariz. Ct. App., 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-20013408. Honorable Howard Fell, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of Pima County, Arizona, of felony murder and aggravated robbery. He appealed, arguing, inter alia, that admission of a hearsay statement by the victim violated his confrontation rights under Crawford.


OVERVIEW: Defendant said his two companions pulled a man out of his rental car and beat him; defendant and the companions drove off in the car. Before dying of his injuries, the victim told police he had been assaulted by three men who stole his car. Defendant and two other men were seen in rental car. Blood was found on defendant's shoe, on the companion's clothes, and on concrete blocks found at the murder scene. The appellate court held that, as the evidence had been sufficient to convict defendant of the crimes, the trial court properly denied his motion for a judgment of acquittal. Instructions concerning reasonable doubt and the elements of felony murder were proper. As the victim had been staggering, bleeding, slipping in and out of consciousness, and asking for medical help, the trial court properly found that he had been under the stress of a startling event; his statement was thus admissible under Ariz. R. Evid. 803(2) as an excited utterance. Since police did not know a crime had been committed when they questioned the victim, his statement was non-testimonial hearsay outside the scope of Crawford and its admission did not violate defendant's Sixth Amendment confrontation rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Cook v. Cook


1-CA-CV 03-0727


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


209 Ariz. 487; 104 P.3d 857; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 6; 444 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 23



January 13, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Cook v. Cook, 2005 Ariz. LEXIS 93 (Ariz., Sept. 27, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Yuma County. Cause No. SC1400DR09700015. The Honorable Kirby D. Kongable, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in Yuma County (Arizona), which entered a decree of dissolution of his marriage to appellee wife. Appellant and appellee were first cousins and appellant contested the trial court's jurisdiction alleging that there was no valid marriage.


OVERVIEW: The parties were married in Virginia and at the time marriage between first cousins was valid in Virginia. The parties moved to Arizona where marriage between first cousins was void per Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 25-101. However when they moved to Arizona, the law also provided that marriages valid by the laws of the place where contracted were valid in Arizona per Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 25-112(A). Later, § 25.112(A) was amended to add a phrase excepting marriages that were void and prohibited by Ariz. Code § 25-101. The court held that under a conflict-of-law analysis of whether the out-of-state marriage was valid in Arizona did not apply Virginia law. If the plain language of the amendment were applied the legislation had a retroactive effect on the marriage. The court held that marriage was a substantive right and appellee's right to have her marriage recognized had "vested." Had the legislature chosen to nullify existing marriages (thus having the retroactive effect described) it could have expressly stated so.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

State v. Timmons


2 CA-CR 2004-0058


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


209 Ariz. 403; 103 P.3d 315; 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 1; 442 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 33



January 7, 2005, Decided


NOTICE:

THIS DOCUMENT WAS VACATED BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, in part, Review denied by, in part, Remanded by State v. Timmons, 2005 Ariz. LEXIS 100 (Ariz., Sept. 27, 2005)
Vacated by, On remand at State v. Timmons, 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 146 (Ariz. Ct. App., Oct. 27, 2005)
Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at State v. Timmons, 2005 Ariz. App. Unpub. LEXIS 429 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-20031946. Honorable Howard Fell, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: Timmons's convictions and presumptive sentences affirmed; aggravated sentences vacated. Care remanded to trial court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Pima County, Arizona, convicted defendant of armed robbery, aggravated robbery, six counts of kidnapping, and six counts of aggravated assault, and sentenced him to a combination of consecutive and concurrent, presumptive and aggravated prison terms totaling 30.5 years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended, inter alia, that the trial court violated Blakely by aggravating his sentences using factors not found by the jury. The appellate court agreed, finding that without additional findings of fact, the presumptive sentences for the aggravated robbery and dangerous nature, armed robbery convictions were 3.5 years and 10.5 years, not the aggravated sentences of 7 and 20 years the trial court imposed. The aggravated sentences, therefore, violated Blakely. Further, the appellate court could not say that a jury would have found the same aggravating factors as the trial court. The trial court's finding of "significant emotional harm to multiple victims" was an inherently subjective determination, and, of the five aggravating factors found, only three were among the aggravators listed in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-702(C). The appellate court could not conclude that the Blakely error was harmless and did not contribute to the sentences, particularly because, in addition to relying on the presence of accomplices, the trial court also weighed four additional aggravating factors not found beyond a reasonable doubt by the jury.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and presumptive sentences were affirmed, but his aggravated sentences were vacated and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

State v. Gomez


1 CA-CR 03-1050


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


209 Ariz. 372; 102 P.3d 992; 2004 Ariz. App. LEXIS 186; 441 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



December 21, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Gomez, 2005 Ariz. LEXIS 62 (Ariz., May 24, 2005)
Vacated by, Remanded by State v. Gomez, 2006 Ariz. LEXIS 17 (Ariz., Feb. 8, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR-2003-012719-001 DT. The Honorable Eileen S. Willett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed; sentences vacated. Remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) convicted defendant on charges of possession of methamphetamine and possession of marijuana. She appealed her sentences.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ruled defendant was ineligible for probation under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-901.01 (Supp. 2003) because she had been previously indicted for manslaughter, based on § 13-901.01(B). Defendant was never tried on the charge. There was no ambiguity in § 13-901.01(B) that would permit the "indicted for" language to be applied solely to existing indictments. The use of the past tense "has been" as a modifier for the phrase "convicted of or indicted for" indicated a clear intent to include all prior convictions or indictments for a violent crime as disqualifying a person from the scope of § 13-901.01. This statute could not constitutionally permit the fact of an indictment to serve as a disqualifying or enhancement factor for purposes of sentencing. The portion of § 13-901.01(B) that disqualified an otherwise eligible defendant from mandatory probation for a drug offense based solely on a finding that she had been indicted for a violent crime was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed; however, her prison sentences were vacated and the case was remanded for a new disposition consistent with the court's opinion.

State v. Berger


1 CA-CR 03-0243


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


209 Ariz. 386; 103 P.3d 298; 2004 Ariz. App. LEXIS 182; 441 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 29



December 14, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, Motion to strike denied by, Request denied by State v. Berger, 2006 Ariz. LEXIS 11 (Ariz., Jan. 4, 2006)
Vacated by, in part, Affirmed by, in part, En banc State v. Berger, 212 Ariz. 473, 134 P.3d 378, 2006 Ariz. LEXIS 58 (Ariz., May 10, 2006)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Petition granted by State v. Berger, 2017 Ariz. App. Unpub. LEXIS 972 (July 20, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa. County Cause No. CR 2002-013657. The Honorable Ruth Harris Hilliard, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, Maricopa County (Arizona), convicted and sentenced defendant for 20 counts of sexual exploitation of a minor younger than 15 years of age, in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3553(A) (Supp. 2004), based on his possession of child pornography. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Each offense was a class 2 felony and dangerous crime against children punishable by a prison term of 10 to 24 years without the possibility of probation, early release, or pardon, and each sentence had to be served consecutively, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3553(C). Defendant was sentenced to the minimum and mitigated sentence, 20 consecutive 10-year terms of imprisonment. The legislature's designation of possession of child pornography as a more serious offense than the act of indecent exposure and its refusal to distinguish between commercial and non-commercial sexual exploitation of minors was rationally related to furthering the State's interest in protecting children. Defendant's constitutional guarantees of equal protection were not violated. Defendant claimed his sentence was disproportionate, because he was convicted of possessing child pornography, not of producing or selling it. But he supported the industry, as he provided an economic motive for its creation and continuation. There was no inference of gross disproportionality in his sentence. The federal and state constitutional prohibitions against cruel and unusual punishment were not violated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Leopoldo L.


1 CA-JV 04-0074


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


209 Ariz. 249; 99 P.3d 578; 2004 Ariz. App. LEXIS 152; 437 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 32



October 21, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. JV 535391. The Honorable Silvia R. Arellano, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona), which required him to submit to DNA testing. Defendant claimed that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-610(O)(1) (Supp. 2003), which authorized DNA testing of juveniles adjudicated delinquent for sexual offenses, did not apply to attempted sexual offenses and that the ordered test violated his constitutional right to privacy under the Fourth Amendment and Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 8.


OVERVIEW: Defendant admitted to committing attempted public indecency to a minor, in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 13-1001 and 1403(B), and the juvenile court adjudicated him delinquent of the admitted charge, placed him on probation, and ordered him to submit to DNA testing pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-610(O)(1) (Supp. 2003). Defendant argued that the word "attempt," as used in § 13-610(O)(1), only applied to homicide offenses and did not apply to the remaining offenses listed within § 13-610(O)(1). The court held that § 13-610(O)(1) mandated DNA testing of a juvenile adjudicated delinquent for attempting to commit any offense listed in that subsection, including a felony sexual offense listed in Ariz. Rev. Stat. ch. 14. The court rejected defendant's argument that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-610 was unconstitutional as applied to him because the DNA testing required by § 13-610 served the government's special needs to identify perpetrators of past and future crimes and to deter a known class of offenders from re-offending. The primary purpose of § 13-610 was not simply the advancement of a generalized interest in law enforcement without individualized suspicion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

Komalestewa v. Indus. Comm'n

COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D

OVERVIEW: The employee crawled under a conveyor belt, and his right arm became caught, resulting in serious injury. Witnesses testified that the employee did not appear intoxicated that morning, but an expert testified that the employee's blood alcohol content at the time of the accident was 0.176. On appeal, the employee argued that the ALJ erred by determining that the employee's use of alcohol rendered his claim noncompensable pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1021(C) (amended 1996). The employee denied that intoxication more than slightly contributed to his work-related injury; however, there was sufficient evidence presented to support the ALJ's finding. Arizona-American Water Co. v. Ariz. Corp. Comm'n


1 CA-CC 03-0001


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


209 Ariz. 189; 98 P.3d 624; 2004 Ariz. App. LEXIS 146; 437 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



October 5, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Arizona Corporation Commission. Docket Nos. W-01303A-0983.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant water company challenged a decision of appellee Arizona Corporation Commission that denied its application for rehearing seeking review of the conditions imposed by the Commission on a proposed merger between the water company's parent company and a foreign corporation. The water company had sought a declaration that the Commission's Affiliated Interests Rules, Ariz. Admin. Comp. R. 14-2-801 to 14-2-806, did not apply to the merger.


OVERVIEW: The water company appealed the Commission's decision that imposed conditions on the proposed merger. The court noted that pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 40-254 (2001) the Legislature had given the superior court direct jurisdiction over all appeals from Commission orders except for a single class of appeals, which involved public service corporations and related to rate making or rate design as provided by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 40-254.01(A). The court concluded that it lacked jurisdiction because the Commission's order and the conditions it contained did not constitute rate-making or rate-design. The court noted that process of rate-making and/or rate-design had been characterized as one in which the Commission set rates and determined fair value of property and reasonable rates of return. The court concluded that the Commission's order and conditions did not set rates or determine the fair value of the water company's property or a reasonable rate of return on that property. The court rejected the argument that a Commission order could be directly appealed to the court as related to "rate making or rate design" merely because it affected rates.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that it lacked jurisdiction and dismissed the appeal.

Ariz. State Democratic Party v. State


1 CA-CV 02-0180


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


209 Ariz. 103; 98 P.3d 214; 2004 Ariz. App. LEXIS 145; 435 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 23



September 30, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Ariz. State Democratic Party v. State, 2005 Ariz. LEXIS 11 (Ariz., Feb. 8, 2005)
Vacated by Ariz. State Democratic Party v. State, 115 P.3d 121, 2005 Ariz. LEXIS 78 (Ariz., July 12, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 00-011655. The Honorable Roland J. Steinle, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, denied appellant political party's motion for summary judgment and granted it in favor of appellee State, finding that the party had violated Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 16-919 (Supp. 2003) by soliciting and accepting donations from corporations and labor unions to pay its operating expenses. The party appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court had to determine whether monies given to a political party by a corporation for operating expenses fell within the constitutional prohibition of Ariz. Const. art. 14, § 18. The phrase "influencing any election" could be reasonably construed in differing ways, and the monies contributed by corporations to political parties for operating expenses were not necessarily prohibited by the constitution. Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 16-919 and 16-920 allowed labor organizations and corporations to spend money on non-partisan activities aimed at their own members, stockholders, and families. Monies contributed to the party were partisan and not limited to shareholders, members, or their families. Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 16-901(5)(b)(v) provided for the exclusion of payments by a political party, not monies contributed to a political party. The legislature intended to preclude corporations and labor unions from utilizing treasury monies for contributions to political parties. The federal and Arizona's right to "freely speak" did not infringe upon the legislature's ability to completely ban corporate and labor contributions to parties whether designated for operating expenses or not.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

461 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fell


2 CA-SA 2004-0057


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


209 Ariz. 77; 97 P.3d 902; 2004 Ariz. App. LEXIS 137; 435 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 67



September 23, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 28, 2004.
Review granted by State v. Fell, 2005 Ariz. LEXIS 25 (Ariz., Mar. 22, 2005)
Affirmed by, Remanded by State v. Fell, 210 Ariz. 554, 115 P.3d 594, 2005 Ariz. LEXIS 73 (Ariz., 2005)
Subsequent appeal at State v. Sanders, 2006 Ariz. App. Unpub. LEXIS 248 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: SPECIAL ACTION PROCEEDING Pima County. Cause No. CR-20002900.



DISPOSITION: RELIEF GRANTED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Real party in interest defendant was convicted of sexual assault, sexual abuse, kidnapping, second-degree burglary, and first-degree murder in the Pima County Court (Arizona). As petitioner State was not seeking the death penalty, the sentencing options were life in prison or life with the possibility of parole after 25 years. Before sentencing, respondent judge entered orders resulting in the State's petitioning for special action relief.


OVERVIEW: The sentencing judge found the U.S. Supreme Court's decision in Blakely v. Washington applied to defendant's sentencing and concluded that before he could impose life on the murder charge, the State had to prove beyond a reasonable doubt the aggravating circumstances alleged. The appellate court was presented with two issues: whether Blakely required a jury to find beyond a reasonable doubt that certain aggravating circumstances existed before an Arizona trial judge could sentence a first-degree murder defendant to life rather than life with the possibility of parole and whether Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-703.01(Q), which required judges to consider the aggravating circumstances in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-702 in choosing between those sentencing alternatives, applied retroactively to offenses committed before the statute's effective date. The appellate court denied relief on the latter question and affirmed the judge's orders that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-703.01(Q) could not be applied retroactively. Because there was no presumptive or aggravated prison term for first-degree murder Blakely did not apply, and defendant was not entitled to a jury trial on the aggravating circumstances.


OUTCOME: The appellate court granted partial relief by vacating those portions of the judge's orders compelling the State to prove and a jury to find beyond a reasonable doubt the aggravating factors alleged in the State's notice. The judge was directed to conduct sentencing proceedings consistent with the opinion and the Arizona Supreme Court's decision in Viramontes.

State v. Chavez


2 CA-CR 2002-0202


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


208 Ariz. 606; 96 P.3d 1093; 2004 Ariz. App. LEXIS 130; 434 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



September 14, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Chavez, 2005 Ariz. LEXIS 58 (Ariz., May 24, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-20000140. Honorable Paul S. Banales, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, Pima County (Arizona) convicted defendant of four felony counts of aggravated driving under the influence of intoxicants (DUI) based alternately on his revoked driver's license and his two prior DUI convictions. The trial court placed him on five years' probation and imposed four months' imprisonment as a condition of his probation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant claimed the trial court should have granted his pretrial motion to dismiss the charges or alternatively to suppress evidence, based on what he alleged was an improper citizen's arrest under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3884(1). In denying defendant's motion to suppress, the trial court ruled that the ranger had authority to stop and detain defendant's vehicle, not in his official capacity as a ranger, but as a private citizen. The court held defendant's erratic and dangerous driving constituted a breach of the peace for purposes of § 13-3884. Because the ranger's actions in stopping and detaining defendant were those of a private citizen, the Fourth Amendment's requirement of probable cause was not implicated. Even if the citizen's arrest had been unlawful, the evidence would not have been suppressed. The exclusionary rule did not apply to the actions of private citizens. Driving a vehicle while intoxicated constituted a misdemeanor amounting to a breach of the peace within the meaning of § 13-3884(1) and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's motion to dismiss or to suppress.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Cons


2 CA-CR 2002-0333


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


208 Ariz. 409; 94 P.3d 609; 2004 Ariz. App. LEXIS 107; 430 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 63



July 22, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PINAL COUNTY. Cause No. CR-200200170. Honorable Kelly Marie Robertson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with a forgery. The State alleged defendant had two prior felony convictions. A jury, before the Superior Court of Pinal County, Arizona, convicted defendant. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant contended that the trial court committed reversible error by permitting the amendment of the allegation of prior felony convictions. Nevertheless, nothing in the record showed that defendant objected to the amendment. Reviewing for fundamental error, the appellate court concluded that the claim was meritless. Defendant also contended that the State was required to prove the prior convictions beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court determined, however, that a heightened burden of proof was not applicable. Prior convictions for sentence enhancement need only be established by clear and convincing evidence. Turning to the sufficiency of the evidence, the appellate court noted that, to prove a prior conviction, the State must submit positive identification establishing that the accused was the same person who previously was convicted, as well as evidence of the conviction itself. That was done here. Defendant objected to the admission of the documents on the ground that, inter alia, the State failed to show that the convictions were final. The appellate court rejected this argument as summarily waived.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the conviction and the sentence.

State v. McDermott


1 CA-CR 03-0683


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


208 Ariz. 332; 93 P.3d 532; 2004 Ariz. App. LEXIS 102; 429 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 11



July 8, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. LC 2002-000633. The Honorable Michael D. Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in municipal court with violating Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3102(A)(1) (2001), the prohibition against carrying a concealed weapon on one's person without a permit. The municipal court granted defendant's moved to dismiss, and the City appealed. The Maricopa County Superior Court, Arizona, reversed and remanded, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Two officers stopped defendant for speeding. As one of the officers approached defendant's truck, defendant stepped out wearing a fanny pack around his waist. After talking with the officer, defendant removed the pack and placed it in the bed of the truck. When the officer moved the pack, he felt what proved to be a handgun. Defendant argued that his conduct was lawful because a fanny pack fell within the luggage exception in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3102(F) (2001). The municipal court found that a fanny pack was not luggage but that the word "luggage" as used in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3102(F) was unconstitutionally vague. The superior court found that the municipal court erred in determining that the statute was unconstitutionally vague. The appellate court ruled that a fanny pack was different from luggage for the purpose of applying the exemption from punishment for carrying a concealed weapon pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3102(F). Also, the use of the word "luggage" did not render the statute unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The superior court's reversal of the municipal court's order granting defendant' motion to dismiss was affirmed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Bennett v. Brownlow


1 CA-CV 03-0233


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


208 Ariz. 79; 90 P.3d 1245; 2004 Ariz. App. LEXIS 72; 428 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 43



June 1, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Amended by Order filed June 16, 2004.
Review granted by Bennett v. Brownlow, 2005 Ariz. LEXIS 2 (Ariz., Jan. 4, 2005)
Vacated by, Remanded by, En banc Bennett v. Brownlow, 211 Ariz. 193, 119 P.3d 460, 2005 Ariz. LEXIS 85 (Ariz., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Yavapai County. Cause No. CV 01-0567. The Honorable Kenneth L. Fields, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, festival owner/organizer and her husband, appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in Yavapai County (Arizona) that granted summary judgment for defendant county in the organizer's action which asserted both federal and state claims against the county based on a county ordinance that required event sponsors to be nonprofit organizations.


OVERVIEW: The organizer had been permitted to sponsor an art and craft festival at a county courthouse plaza until 2000, when the county adopted an ordinance that required event sponsors to be nonprofit organizations. The organizer filed suit claiming the ordinance violated the First Amendment, as well as Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 6. She argued that the courthouse plaza was a traditional public forum and the presentation and sale of arts and crafts at the festival was expressive conduct entitled to constitutional protection. The trial court entered judgment for the county. On appeal, the court reversed. The court found that because the ordinance was not content-based, it did not need to be narrowly tailored to serve a compelling state interest, but needed to be narrowly tailored to serve a significant government interest. The court concluded that avoiding competition with local merchants was a valid purpose, but the ordinance's limitation of event sponsors to non-profit organizations was neither significantly related to that purpose nor narrowly tailored to achieve it. The court held that ordinance was unconstitutional to the extent it limited sponsors to nonprofit organizations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment and held that the county ordinance was unconstitutional to the extent it distinguished between nonprofit and for-profit sponsors. The court remanded the case for further proceedings as to whether plaintiff was damaged by the unconstitutionality and for a determination at trial of the amount of any damages. The court awarded costs to plaintiff festival organizer.

Riepe v. Riepe


1 CA-CV 03-0184


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


208 Ariz. 90; 91 P.3d 312; 2004 Ariz. App. LEXIS 70; 429 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 29



May 25, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended June 29, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Coconino County. Cause No. DR 99-0089. The Honorable Danna D. Hendrix, Judge. The Honorable Charles D. Adams, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner stepmother filed a petition in the Superior Court in Coconino County (Arizona), seeking in loco parentis visitation pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 25-415(C) (2000) with a child who was in the custody of respondent, his legal mother. The trial court denied the petition. The stepmother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The child's legal parents were divorced. The father, who was the primary residential parent, married the stepmother. The father was killed in a traffic accident, and the child began living with the mother. Although the trial court found that the stepmother had been a caring and supportive step-parent, it held that she was not entitled to visitation under § 25-415(C) because she did not show that the child viewed her in the same sense as he viewed the mother. The appellate court agreed that the trial court improperly required the stepmother to prove that she stood in the place of either the father or the mother in order to establish in loco parentis status. To determine in loco parentis status under § 25-415(G)(1), the trial court should have considered only whether the child viewed the stepmother as a parent and whether they had formed a meaningful parental relationship that had endured for a substantial period of time. The legislature clearly intended to authorize in loco parentis visitation by a non-parent, and there was no requirement that the petitioning party be of a different gender than a legal parent.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

Grammatico v. Indus. Comm'n


1 CA-IC 01-0117


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


208 Ariz. 10; 90 P.3d 211; 2004 Ariz. App. LEXIS 68; 426 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 29



May 20, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Amended By Order Filed June 15, 2004.
Review granted by Grammatico v. Industrial Comm'n, 2005 Ariz. LEXIS 12 (Ariz., Feb. 8, 2005)
Affirmed by Grammatico v. Indus. Comm'n, 2005 Ariz. LEXIS 82 (Ariz., Aug. 10, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Special Action--Industrial Commission. ICA CLAIM NO. 20001-390571. CARRIER NO. AZ00008522. Administrative Law Judge J. Matthew Powell.



DISPOSITION: AWARD SET ASIDE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant appealed a decision by the Industrial Commission of Arizona that affirmed respondent employer's denial of benefits. The claimant sought further review and asked the instant court to decide whether Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1021(D) (Supp. 2003) violated Ariz. Const. art. 18, § 8, by depriving workers of compensatory benefits for injuries caused in whole, or in part, or contributed to by necessary employment risks and dangers.


OVERVIEW: Respondent insurance carrier denied claimant's benefits, which he protested. At a hearing before an administrative law judge (ALJ), evidence showed the employer maintained a certified drug-testing policy in compliance with Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 23-493 to -493.11 (1995 & Supp. 2003), and had certified its policy with the Industrial Commission, triggering the applicability of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1021(D). Applying the statute, the ALJ found the claim noncompensable because the claimant failed to prove his use of controlled substances was not a contributing cause of his injuries. The claimant, challenging the constitutionality of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1021(D), bore the burden of overcoming the presumption that the statute was constitutional. The appellate court would declare it unconstitutional only if it conflicted with Ariz. Const. art. 18, § 8. Because the statute abrogated claims for injuries partially contributed to by necessary risks of employment, it impermissibly conflicted with the constitution. Because the evidence suggested necessary risks of working on drywall stilts partially contributed to the accident, § 23-1021(D) was unconstitutional as applied.


OUTCOME: The decision of the commission was set aside.

Wonders v. Pima County


2 CA-CV 2003-0090


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


207 Ariz. 576; 89 P.3d 810; 2004 Ariz. App. LEXIS 65; 425 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 13



May 12, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. C20013005. Honorable Carmine Cornelio, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After submitting a native-plant preservation plan to comply with a local ordinance, plaintiff subdivision developer sued defendant county for inverse condemnation, alleging the ordinance effected a regulatory taking of its property, was unconstitutionally vague, and conflicted with preemptive state law. The Superior Court of Pima County, Arizona, granted the County's motion for summary judgment. The developer appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the developer contended the ordinance was preempted by state statute and resulted in an unconstitutional taking of its property. The appellate court found that, although mislabeling it as the exhaustion doctrine, the trial court correctly applied the doctrine of primary jurisdiction and acted within its discretion in exercising jurisdiction to hear some, but not all, of the developer's claims. Contrary to the developer's assertion, the appellate court found that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 3-914 authorized county ordinances not in conflict with the Arizona Native Plant Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 3-901 to 3-934. The ordinance in question did not conflict with the Act simply because it was a zoning ordinance; although the Act did not prevent the destruction of native plants on private property, neither did it confirm or confer an inalienable right to do so. The appellate court also ruled that the ordinance was not a regulatory taking of the developer's property, as it was able to make beneficial use of its land.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Daystar Invs., L.L.C. v. Maricopa County Treasurer


1 CA-CV 03-0458, DEPARTMENT E


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE


207 Ariz. 569; 88 P.3d 1181; 2004 Ariz. App. LEXIS 64; 431 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 21



May 6, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Daystar Invs. v. Maricopa Co Treasurer, 2004 Ariz. LEXIS 79 (Ariz., June 29, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 02-090932. The Honorable Bethany G. Hicks, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tax lien purchaser brought a foreclosure action in the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) and obtained a default judgment. The purchaser petitioned the trial court to order appellee county treasurer to issue a tax deed. The trial court treated the petition as an Ariz. R. Civ. P. 60(c) motion and set aside the default judgment. The purchaser appealed.


OVERVIEW: The treasurer, who was not a party to the foreclosure action, argued that the purchaser filed the foreclosure action before expiration of the three year redemption period in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-18201 (Supp. 2003). The parties, by stipulation, asked the trial court to resolve the legal issue of whether the treasurer was required to issue a deed pursuant to a foreclosure judgment if the treasurer believed that the foreclosure action was premature. The trial court rejected the stipulation and ruled on the validity of the default judgment, finding that the foreclosure was premature. The appellate court found that the treasurer had standing to question the foreclosure order, which was not binding on a non-party; the treasurer had an interest in determining whether he was required to issue the deed when he had reasonable grounds to believe that the foreclosure was improper. However, the trial court erred in treating the purchaser's petition as a motion to vacate the default judgment; it was unnecessary to vacate the judgment in order to determine whether the purchaser was entitled to an order directing the treasurer to issue the deed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order vacating the default judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

State v. Watkins


1 CA-CR 03-0197

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 2002-092482. The Honorable Barbara M. Jarrett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant with possession of narcotic drugs, and possession of marijuana. The Superior Court of Maricopa County, Arizona, denied defendant's motion to suppress the evidence. A jury convicted defendant of possession of marijuana and acquitted him of possession of cocaine. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim entered her apartment, only to see two men leaving with her property. The victim recognized the men as acquaintances of defendant. The victim confronted the suspects in defendant's apartment. The police officers, who responded to the victim's 911 call, considered defendant, at the very least, an investigative lead. The officers approached defendant and conducted a pat-down search for weapons. The officers felt marijuana stems during the search. A search incident to arrest was conducted, and the officers found cocaine. On appeal, defendant challenged the admission of the evidence as the forbidden fruit of an unlawful, warrantless search. The appellate court determined that the investigative stop of defendant as a material witness passed the Brown test of reasonableness. The stop was related to a specific and known crime, and the stop was of an identified eyewitness. Moreover, a public interest was furthered by stopping defendant. The interference with defendant's liberty was only minimally intrusive. The officers were legitimately concerned for their safety in conducting the pat down search when the marijuana was discovered.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Maycock v. Asilomar Dev., Inc.


1 CA-CV 02-0710


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T


207 Ariz. 495; 88 P.3d 565; 2004 Ariz. App. LEXIS 52; 424 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 20



April 22, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 2001-000347. The Honorable Sherry Hutt, Judge. The Honorable Michael A. Yarnell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant contractor built a home for the prior owner, who sold the house to plaintiff home buyers. After discovering defects in the home, the buyers filed suit against the contractor, alleging negligence and breach of warranty. The Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, granted the contractor summary judgment, finding that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-552(B) (2003) did not apply and the buyers' claims were barred. The buyers appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the buyers contended the second exception under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-552(B) (2003) for a latent defect not discovered until the eighth year was applicable to save their claims from dismissal. Although the appellate court agreed with the legal conclusion of the trial court that the knowledge of the seller was imputed to the buyers to determine application of § 12-552(B), it also found that genuine issues of material fact regarding the knowledge of the seller precluded summary judgment. Whether the seller's observations of unevenness in the floors before he sold it to the buyers constituted discovery of a defect, particularly in light of the contractor's alleged representation that the unevenness was normal settlement, was a question for the fact finder. Further, summary judgment granted in the contractor's favor on the buyers' negligence claim was improper, as the contractor's summary judgment motion focused on Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-552 (2003) and the negligence claim was not fully briefed prior to the argument. Because the successful party in the instant action was yet to be determined on remand, the appellate court declined to award the buyers attorney fees.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in the contractor's favor on the buyers' negligence and breach of implied warranty claims was reversed and remanded for further proceedings. The award of attorney fees and costs in favor of the contractor was also reversed.

Redelsperger v. City of Avondale


1 CA-CV 03-0309


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


207 Ariz. 430; 87 P.3d 843; 2004 Ariz. App. LEXIS 49; 423 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 18



April 6, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. LC 03-000094. The Honorable Michael D. Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona), which denied the property owner's petition for a writ of mandamus declaring that the approval of a conditional use permit was not a legislative matter subject to referendum and permanently enjoining appellees, city and officials, from placing the matter on the ballot.


OVERVIEW: The property owner sought and obtained the city zoning commission's approval of a conditional use permit to construct a storage facility. The city council affirmed the approval decision. A local interest group opposed to the construction of the facility circulated petitions requesting that the city council place the matter on the ballot. Sufficient signatures were collected. The trial court, in denying declaratory and injunctive relief to the property owner, concluded that the city council acted in a legislative capacity when it approved the conditional use permit and that such legislative action was subject to referendum action under Ariz. Const. art. 4, pt. 1, § 1(3). The court reversed, finding the approval decision to be administrative. The zoning commission was guided by objective criteria and standards set forth in Avondale, Ariz., Zoning Ord. § 108(B)(2), (3), (5) in considering the grant or denial of a conditional use permit. The city council's involvement in hearing an appeal under Avondale, Ariz., Zoning Ord. §§ 103(A)(2), 108(B) did not make the permit process a legislative act. Hence, as an administrative act, the approval of the permit was not subject to referendum.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded to the trial court with instructions to grant declaratory and injunctive relief in favor of the property owner.

State v. Rivera


1 CA-CR 02-0211


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


207 Ariz. 383; 86 P.3d 963; 2004 Ariz. App. LEXIS 41; 422 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 5



April 1, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Vacated by State v. Rivera, 2005 Ariz. LEXIS 41 (Ariz., Apr. 5, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 98-005850. The Honorable Thomas Dunevant, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, denied defendant's motion to exclude the testimony of two accomplices as being tainted by consistency provision in their plea agreements and did not advise the accomplices that the consistency provisions were unenforceable. Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, first-degree burglary, and kidnapping. He appealed, claiming error in the admission of the accomplices' testimony.


OVERVIEW: One accomplice testified that she, defendant, the other accomplice, and another woman drove the victim to a field. Both accomplices testified that defendant then shot the victim and directed each of them to shoot her as well, which they did. The accomplices admitted that they told police multiple versions of the events of the murder and that they knew that any variation in their trial testimony from the version given in a videotaped interview would cause them to lose the benefit of their plea agreements. The appellate court noted that, under Fisher, consistency provisions in plea agreements were unenforceable, and testimony tainted by such provisions was inadmissible. Defendant had standing to raise this issue, because his right to a fair trial was at stake. The error was not harmless, as the accomplices were the only eyewitnesses to testify. On retrial, the accomplices could testify if the taint were removed by not enforcing the consistency provision, by disclosing the terms of the agreement, and by properly instructing the jury. But, the State could not use their trial testimony or any statements they made after entering their plea agreements and before the taint was removed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Lucero


1 CA-CR 02-0739


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


207 Ariz. 301; 85 P.3d 1059; 2004 Ariz. App. LEXIS 35; 422 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 11



March 23, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Lucero, 2004 Ariz. LEXIS 117 (Ariz., Oct. 26, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 2001-008632. The Honorable Crane McClennen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) found defendant guilty of aggravated assault, possession of marijuana and drug paraphernalia, and four counts of endangerment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The charges against defendant arose out of a collision between his vehicle and another vehicle. Defendant had failed to yield the right of way. The State alleged that defendant's use of marijuana had impaired his ability to drive. The State introduced evidence of defendant's impairment in part through the testimony of a forensic toxicologist. Defendant requested a pretrial Frye hearing. He challenged the admissibility of the test used to detect marijuana in his body and the State's expert's opinion testimony regarding defendant's alleged impairment. The appellate court found that the trial court was not required to conduct a Frye hearing regarding the admissibility of the test because defendant failed to show either that the challenged evidence was a novel scientific method or was a formerly accepted method newly fallen into disrepute in the scientific community. Also, the appellate court found that a Frye hearing was not required to admit the expert's opinion evidence regarding defendant's impairment because the expert's testimony relied on no novel scientific principles and his opinion was based on his knowledge and experience as a forensic toxicologist.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Brown


2 CA-CR 2003-0001


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


207 Ariz. 231; 85 P.3d 109; 2004 Ariz. App. LEXIS 26; 419 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 15



February 17, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Brown, 2004 Ariz. LEXIS 81 (Ariz., June 29, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR20021979. Honorable Frank Dawley, Judge Pro Tempore. Honorable Howard Fell, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) convicted defendant of aggravated harassment, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2921. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The problem began when the victim ended her dating relationship with defendant, and defendant would not stay away. She requested and obtained an injunction against harassment against defendant, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-1809(A). That injunction order remained valid and in effect at all pertinent times. On appeal, defendant argued the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss and contended the harassment statute was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad and violated his First Amendment right to freedom of speech. Criminal liability under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2921 was based on the "manner" in which certain communication was conveyed and the underlying purpose for the communication. Because the statute only criminalized communications made with a specific, deliberate purpose, the statute did not apply to pure First Amendment speech and instead regulated, at most, a blend of speech and conduct. Defendant's repeated entreaties to the victim that they resume their relationship did not contain any such particularized political or social message warranting First Amendment protection.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Long


1 CA-CR 02-0960


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


207 Ariz. 140; 83 P.3d 618; 2004 Ariz. App. LEXIS 22; 418 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 5



February 3, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Long, 2004 Ariz. LEXIS 85 (Ariz., June 29, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 2001-015906. The Honorable Jeffrey A. Hotham, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) of sexual exploitation of a minor under the age of 15, sexual conduct with a minor under the age of 15, and sexual conduct with a minor aged 15 or older. The trial court imposed consecutive sentences. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been in a relationship with the victim's mother. Before the victim turned 15 years old, defendant threatened to kill the victim's mother if the victim did not engage in sexual intercourse with him. She complied. This continued after the victim turned 15 years old. The victim's mother later found that defendant had taped himself engaging in sexual intercourse with the victim. Defendant was arrested and convicted of sexual exploitation and sexual conduct. Defendant contested his convictions and sentences on appeal, but the court affirmed. The 20-year sentence defendant received pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604.01 (2001 & Supp. 2003) for sexual exploitation of a minor in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3553(A)(2), (C) (2001 & Supp. 2003) did not violate the prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment in U.S. Const. amend. VIII and Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 15. Defendant possessed the videotape because he threatened the victim, which led to her engaging in sexual intercourse with him. The trial court did not err in imposing an aggravated sentence, considering defendant's abuse of his position of trust and the multiple acts of abuse.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Phelps Dodge Corp. v. Ariz. Elec. Power Coop., Inc.


1 CA-CV 01-0068


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


207 Ariz. 95; 83 P.3d 573; 2004 Ariz. App. LEXIS 14; 421 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 7



January 27, 2004, Decided  
January 27, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Amended by order dated March 15, 2004.
Review denied by, Request denied by Dodge v. Ariz. Elec. Power, 2005 Ariz. LEXIS 6 (Ariz., Jan. 4, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] MARICOPA County Superior Court. No. CV1997-03748. The Honorable Colin F. Campbell, Judge, The Honorable B. Michael Dann, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff affected utility brought suit before the Maricopa County Superior Court, Arizona challenging the Arizona Corporation Commissions' ratemaking rules. Plaintiff cooperatives and plaintiff council filed several suits. The suits were consolidated. The superior court granted and denied motions for summary judgment, and vacated decisions approving certificates of convenience and necessity (CC&N). The parties appealed and cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Commission created the Retail Electric Competition Rules, Ariz. Admin. Code 14-2-1601 to 14-2-1616, to change the provision of electric generation from a system of regulated monopolies to a competitive one. Affected utilities could not offer competitive services other than as a part of their standard offer service. The rules also provided procedures for recovery of stranded costs. On appeal, the parties raised several issues concerning the viability of the rules under Ariz. Const. art. 15, §§ 3 and 14. The Commission conceded that the superior court correctly ruled that article 15, § 14 required the Commission to determine the fair value of property owned by the electric service providers, and consider that finding in setting rates. The appellate court determined, however, that the superior court erred by vacating the rules decisions in their entirety. The Commission only lacked constitutional or legislative authority to promulgate certain rules; for instance, those requiring divestiture of competitive generation assets affecting rates. Some of the rules could be severed from the rest. Finally, the superior court did properly vacate the CC&N decisions.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed that portion of the judgment vacating the rules decisions in their entirety. The appellate court also reversed the decisions promulgating some of the rules. Other rules were to be submitted to the attorney general. The remaining portions of the rules decisions were affirmed. The judgment vacating the CC&N decisions was affirmed. The award of attorneys' fees was affirmed. The matter was remanded for adjustments.

Washburn v. Pima County


2 CA-CV 2003-0107


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


206 Ariz. 571; 81 P.3d 1030; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 208; 415 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 18



December 19, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Washburn v. Pima County, 2004 Ariz. LEXIS 48 (Ariz., Apr. 19, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. C-20030754. Honorable Jane L. Eikleberry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's order granting summary judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, homebuilders and a homebuilders association, (homebuilders) sued defendant county seeking a declaration that the county lacked statutory authority to adopt an ordinance requiring homebuilders to incorporate greater wheelchair access design features, and that the ordinance violated their equal protection and privacy rights. The Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) granted summary judgment for the county. The homebuilders appealed.


OVERVIEW: The homebuilders claimed, inter alia, that the county lacked statutory authority to adopt its ordinance, and that the ordinance violated their right to privacy and their equal protection rights. The court initially held that neither res judicata nor collateral estoppel precluded the homebuilders from bringing the instant action. The court then held that the county was authorized, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 11-861(A), (C)(1), to adopt individual building design criterion promulgated by a national organization or association organized and conducted for the purpose of developing codes in enacting its ordinance. The court further held that the county's ordinance did not unconstitutionally infringe on the homebuilders' right to privacy under Ariz. Const. art. II, § 8 because the ordinance was proper exercise of the county's police power, and that the county's ordinance did not violate the homebuilders' equal protection rights under Ariz. Const. art. II, § 13 because the county advanced the legitimate governmental interest of increasing the number of homes accessible to those in wheelchairs.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment for the county was affirmed.
