State v. Tsinnijinnie


1 CA-CR 02-0958


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


206 Ariz. 477; 80 P.3d 284; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 199; 414 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 8



December 11, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Tsinnijinnie, 2004 Ariz. LEXIS 78 (Ariz., June 29, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Coconino County. Cause No. CR 2002-0063. The Honorable H. Jeffrey Coker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in Coconino County (Arizona) entered convictions for one count of sexual assault and two counts of molestation of a child, all dangerous crimes against children under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604.01 (2001). Defendant appealed from his convictions and sentences. The State cross-appealed the trial court's sentencing of defendant to concurrent sentences for the sexual assault count and one of the molestation counts.


OVERVIEW: Because only the court's resolution of the sentencing issue raised by the State merited publication, the court addressed and affirmed in a separate memorandum decision defendant's convictions. The State asserted that, under § 13-604.01(K), the trial court was required to impose consecutive sentences for defendant's convictions for sexual assault and molestation of a child. The court agreed, stating that, when the two sentences of § 13-604.01(K) were considered together, the sentencing discretion granted to the trial court by the first sentence was limited by the second sentence. Specifically, if defendant was convicted of child molestation or sexual abuse along with another offense that was not a dangerous crime against children, the trial court had discretion to order that the sentences be served concurrently if only one victim was involved. If, however, defendant was convicted of any "other" dangerous crime against children, the sentence for each such offense had to be served consecutively to any other sentence imposed. Therefore, the court reversed defendant's sentences for sexual assault and molestation of a child and remanded to the trial court for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions. The court reversed the sentences for defendant's convictions for sexual assault and molestation of a child. The court vacated those sentences in their entirety and remanded to the trial court for resentencing.

Aegis of Ariz., L.L.C. v. Town of Marana


2 CA-CV 2003-0057


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


206 Ariz. 557; 81 P.3d 1016; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 203; 415 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 10



November 20, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected December 22, 2003.
Reconsideration granted by Town of Marana v. Aegis of Arizona, LLC, 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 202 (Ariz. Ct. App., Dec. 17, 2003)
Review denied by Aegis of Arizona LLC v. Town of Marana, 2004 Ariz. LEXIS 56 (Ariz., May 25, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. C20000299. Honorable Ted B. Borek, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant town challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), entered upon a jury verdict, which awarded appellee developer damages for its federal substantive due process and equal protection claims, which it had brought under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and which summarily denied the town's new trial motion.


OVERVIEW: A company related to the developer purchased property in the town, which was in the heavy industrial zone, to maintain a mobile medical waste treatment system after the town's planning and zoning administrator orally stated that the proposed use would be permitted. However, the company was required to apply for a conditional use permit (CUP), which was eventually denied. Reversing and remanding, the court held that the developer had a personal stake in the town's denial of the company's CUP application and that the administrator's initial decision that the proposed use was permitted and the later decision of town staff that a CUP would be required were not, as a matter of law, final, and thus not ripe for judicial review. However, the trial court erred in denying the town's judgment as a matter of law motion on the developer's substantive due process and equal protection claims because it was clear that the developer could not have had a "reasonable expectation of entitlement" to have the CUP application granted, the town did not unconstitutionally deprive it of any interest, and the record did not reflect that the town treated the developer differently from other applicants.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded with directions to enter judgment in favor of the town.

City of Tucson v. Clear Channel Outdoor, Inc.


2 CA-CV 2002-0183


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


206 Ariz. 335; 78 P.3d 1056; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 179; 412 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 14



October 31, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Vacated by, Remanded by City of Tucson v. Clear Channel Outdoor, Inc., 2005 Ariz. LEXIS 14 (Ariz., Feb. 10, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. C-20003722. Honorable Carmine Cornelio, Judge. Honorable Charles V. Harrington, Judge.
City of Tucson v. Whiteco Metrocom, Inc., 194 Ariz. 390, 983 P.2d 759, 1999 Ariz. App. LEXIS 69 (Ariz. Ct. App., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which awarded summary judgment to defendant corporation in an action alleging that the corporation violated sign and zoning codes.


OVERVIEW: The city filed an action against the corporation, alleging that its billboards violated the city's sign and zoning codes. The corporation moved for summary judgment on the ground that the newly enacted statute of limitations, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 9-462.02(C), barred the city from pursuing the violations it had discovered more than two years before filing the complaint. The trial court granted the motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court determined that the city had no unassailable right to enforce its zoning and sign codes. The legislature could retroactively restrict or modify the city's enforcement authority. The court further found that the two-year limitation period prescribed in § 9-462.02(C) began upon the city's discovery of the zoning or sign code violations. The city had no vested rights in enforcing its zoning and sign codes. If the legislature had intended the new statute of limitations to only have prospective application, it could have so specified or otherwise indicated that any preexisting claims were preserved. Accordingly, the trial court did not err in refusing to consider the documents the city had proffered as evidence of the legislature's intent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court. The court granted the corporation's request for attorney fees on appeal.

Standhardt v. Superior Court of Ariz.


1 CA-SA 03-0150


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


206 Ariz. 276; 77 P.3d 451; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 167; 410 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 25



October 8, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Standhardt v. MCSC, 2004 Ariz. LEXIS 62 (Ariz., May 25, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: MARICOPA COUNTY Superior Court. Petition for Special Action.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner homosexual men filed a petition for special action seeking to compel respondent clerk of court of respondent Superior Court of the State of Arizona to issue the men a marriage license in real party in interest State and declare Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 25-101(C), 25-125(A) (2003) unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 25-101(C) (2003), which prohibited marriage between persons of the same sex, and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 25-125A (2003), which defined a valid marriage as one between a man and a woman, the clerk denied the men a marriage license. The men alleged that the statutes violated their fundamental right to marry and their right to equal protection under the laws. The court exercised its discretion to accept jurisdiction based on the issue of first impression raised, but the court denied the men the relief sought. The court held that the fundamental right to marry protected by the Fourteenth Amendment and Ariz. Const. art. II, § 4 did not encompass the right to marry a same-sex partner. The State had a legitimate interest in encouraging procreation and child rearing within the marital relationship and limiting that relationship to opposite-sex couples. Because the State's prohibition against same-sex marriages rationally furthered a legitimate State interest, the prohibition did not deprive the men of their constitutional rights to substantive due process, privacy under Ariz. Const. art. II, § 8, or equal protection under Ariz. Const. art. II, § 13.


OUTCOME: The court accepted jurisdiction of the special action, but denied the men relief.

Lindsay v. Cave Creek Outfitters, L.L.C.


1 CA-CV 02-0375


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


207 Ariz. 487; 88 P.3d 557; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 162; 409 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 32



October 2, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 4, 2003.
Later proceeding at Lindsay v. Cave Creek, 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 201 (Ariz. Ct. App., Dec. 11, 2003)
Review denied by, Request granted Lindsay v. Cave Creek Outfitters, 2004 Ariz. LEXIS 50 (Ariz., Apr. 19, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV2000-014210. The Honorable Mark R. Santana, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Trial court judgment affirmed; attorneys' fees and costs awarded on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, rider and spouse, sought review of the decision of the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee riding stable operator (operator), in the rider and spouse's action for personal injuries sustained by the rider when she was thrown from a horse.


OVERVIEW: The rider was injured when she was thrown from a house and she and her spouse filed an action against the operator alleging that its conduct had been negligent and willful, and outrageous. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the operator, holding that the operator was entitled to immunity from negligence under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-553 (2003). The court affirmed, stating that the issue in the case was whether the operator was immune form liability because it had met all of the conditions required by § 12-553. The document that the rider signed contained sufficient information to have been considered a release under § 12-553(E)(2). The release in question contained an acknowledgment that the rider knew of the inherent risks associated with riding a horse. The court further stated that § 12-553 was designed to protect equine owners and agents from lawsuits. That was a legitimate state interest and § 12-553 furthered that interest by immunizing equine owners from liability when their riders have signed a release. Accordingly, § 12-553 did not violate the Equal Protection Clause. Further, § 12-553 did not violate the anti-abrogation clause, Ariz. Const. art. 18, § 6.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Cervantes v. Cates


1 CA-SA 03-0157


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


206 Ariz. 178; 76 P.3d 449; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 154; 409 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



September 23, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Cervantes v. Cates, 2004 Ariz. LEXIS 32 (Ariz., Mar. 16, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Special Action from the Maricopa County Superior Court. Cause No. CR 2001-003989-001-DT, CR 2001-012648. The Honorable Jeffrey S. Cates, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Jurisdiction accepted, relief granted; case remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a special action to challenge a decision from respondent judge in Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona), which denied defendant's motion to compel real party in interest State to copy certain documents under Ariz. R. Crim. P. 15.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with numerous crimes involving sexual acts with children. Several videotapes and photographs were seized from defendant's possession by police. Defendant wanted the State to copy the materials for use in his defense. After the trial court denied defendant's motion to compel, he filed a special petition action. In vacating the trial court's decision, the court determined that the trial court abused its discretion by denying defendant's motion. Defendant was entitled to a copy of the materials under Ariz. R. Crim. P. 15.1 (Supp. 2002). There was nothing in Rule 15.1 that made an exception for contraband. The State failed to demonstrate any good cause for an order protecting it from compliance with Rule 15.1. There was no showing that defendant or his attorney would have used the material in violation of Ariz. R. Crim. P. 15.4. Defendant had no burden of proof when seeking production. Finally, the fact that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3553 did not provide immunity for defense counsel's possession of such materials did not mean that they were exempt from disclosure under Ariz. R. Crim. P. 15.1.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's decision to deny the motion to compel. The case was remanded to the trial court to conduct hearings, if necessary, to determine if there was good cause for a protective order. The court also noted that the trial court was permitted to issue an order imposing safeguards on the copying and use of the materials.

Tanque Verde Unified Sch. Dist. No. 13 v. Bernini

State v. Livingston


2 CA-CR 2003-0027


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


206 Ariz. 145; 75 P.3d 1103; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 151; 408 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 4



September 16, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Livingston, 2004 Ariz. LEXIS 46 (Ariz., Apr. 19, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF GILA COUNTY. Cause No. CR2002-330. Honorable Robert Duber II, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Gila County (Arizona) granted defendant's motion to suppress the evidence seized from her car after she was stopped for a possible traffic violation. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with transportation of marijuana for sale, personal possession of marijuana, possession of drug paraphernalia, and use of marijuana. Defendant filed a motion to suppress evidence and argued that the officer lacked reasonable suspicion to stop her vehicle because she had not violated any laws. The State countered that defendant had violated Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-729(1) by briefly traversing the shoulder line. The trial court granted the motion to suppress. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that under § 28-729(1), a driver was required to remain exclusively in a single lane only "as nearly as practicable" under the circumstances. That language demonstrated an express legislative intent to avoid penalizing brief, momentary, and minor deviations outside the marked lines. The State did not dispute that defendant otherwise drove safely on a dangerous, curved road apart from her alleged isolated and minor breach of the shoulder line. Under such circumstances, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it found that defendant committed no violation and implicitly found that the officer had lacked a reasonable basis for the stop.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting defendant's motion to suppress.

State v. Akins


1 CA-CR 02-0963


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


206 Ariz. 113; 75 P.3d 718; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 140; 408 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



September 2, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Counsel Corrected September 11, 2003.
Released for Publication March 11, 2004.
Review denied by State v. Akins, 2004 Ariz. LEXIS 22 (Ariz., Feb. 10, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 02-012215. The Honorable Stephen A. Gerst, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the order of the Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, suppressing all contraband seized from defendant incident to his arrest for failure to produce evidence of his identity pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1595(C) (1998).


OVERVIEW: Police officers conducted a traffic stop on a vehicle for the driver's failure to signal before a turn. One of the officers approached defendant, the front seat passenger in the vehicle, who was not wearing a seatbelt. The officer asked defendant for identification, and defendant responded that he lacked any written identification. The officer then arrested defendant pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1595(C) for failure to provide evidence of identification when he was not wearing his seatbelt. The trial court found Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1595(C) unconstitutionally vague for failing to give notice to passengers in motor vehicles of the type of identification that had to be produced under the statute. The appellate court ruled that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1595(C) was unconstitutionally vague because it failed to provide reasonable notice to passengers or others of what evidence of identity was required to avoid violation of the statute. The statutory definition of "evidence of identity" imposed upon drivers under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1595(B) (1998) could not be similarly imposed upon passengers under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1595(C).


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

State ex rel. Romley v. Rayes


1 CA-SA 03-0152


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


206 Ariz. 58; 75 P.3d 148; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 141; 407 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 42



September 2, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Special Action from the Maricopa County Superior Court. Cause No. CR 03-012660-001 DT. The Honorable Douglas Rayes, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Jurisdiction accepted; relief granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A real party in interest was indicted for sexual conduct with a minor and was granted bail despite the provisions of Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 22, and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3961(A), which precluded bail for such an offense with sufficient indicia of guilt. Petitioner State of Arizona sought special action to review the order of respondent judge of the Maricopa County (Arizona) Superior Court which declared the provisions unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The real party in interest contended that Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 22, and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3961(A), implementing a voter-approved proposition, unconstitutionally precluded bail for sexual conduct with a minor when the proof was evident or the presumption great that the party charged committed the offense. The party argued that the provisions violated his constitutional right to bail and, since his alleged criminal conduct occurred prior to the effective date of the provisions, constituted unlawful ex post facto laws. The appellate court first held that, since there was no absolute right to bail and the provisions did not totally abolish bail for the party's offense, no cruel and unusual punishment was inflicted by denying bail upon a proper showing of sufficient indicia of guilt. Further, the provisions did not change the definition of the crime or quantum of punishment, and thus the provisions were procedural rather than punitive, precluding any claim of ex post facto unconstitutionality.


OUTCOME: The appellate court accepted special action jurisdiction and vacated the order which held that the constitutional and statutory provisions limiting bail were unconstitutional.

Citizens Telecomms. Co. v. Ariz. Dep't of Revenue


1 CA-TX 02-0017


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T


206 Ariz. 33; 75 P.3d 123; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 138; 407 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



August 26, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at Citizens Telecomms. Co. of the White Mts., Inc. v. Ariz. Dep't of Revenue, 2006 Ariz. Tax LEXIS 50 (Ariz. Tax Ct., Mar. 15, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Arizona Tax Court Cause Nos. TX 98-00716, TX 98-00717, TX 98-00718, TX 98-00719, TX 98-00720, TX 98-00730, TX 98-00731, TX 97-00322, TX 97-00323, TX 97-00324, TX 97-0826, TX 97-00829. The Honorable Paul A. Katz, Judge.
U.S. West Communs., Inc. v. Arizona Dep't of Revenue, 193 Ariz. 319, 972 P.2d 652, 1998 Ariz. App. LEXIS 105 (Ariz. Ct. App., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Arizona Department of Revenue (ADOR) and 15 counties appealed from the Arizona Tax Court's judgment that ADOR violated the Uniformity Clause, Ariz. Const. art. 9, § 1, and the Equal Protection Clause, Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 13, in applying former Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 42-793 and 42-793.01 (1997) (repealed) (now Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-14403) to a regional telecommunications company and to 6 incumbent local exchange carriers.


OVERVIEW: The main issue was whether the property of the company and the local carriers, as comparison taxpayers, was functionally equivalent. The appellate court held that the U.S. West decision did not preclude the tax court from granting the company relief because of the nature of the company's claim and because of the changes in the telecommunications industry since the company brought its last challenge. The company challenged ADOR's use of the "market value" method under former §§ 42-793(A)(1) and -793.01 for valuing its class 3 property, which included intraLATA (Local Access and Transport Areas) toll calls, vertical services including such features as caller ID and call waiting, and access services between telecommunications networks. That method, which was different from the "historical cost less depreciation" method applied to the local carriers pursuant to § 42-793(A)(2), resulted in the company's higher valuation. However, the company produced substantial evidence that it was a direct competitor in the same industry as other telecommunications companies and that its class 3 telecommunications property was functionally identical to that of the local carriers.


OUTCOME: The tax court's ruling with respect to the company's discrimination claim was affirmed. The tax court's rulings with respect to the local carrier's discrimination claims was reversed and remanded for further consideration of functional equivalency. In addition, the company was awarded its attorney fees and costs on appeal.

 

490 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Jachimek v. State


1 CA-CV 02-0133


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


205 Ariz. 632; 74 P.3d 944; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 130; 406 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 13



August 21, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 26, 2004.
Review denied by Jachimek v. State, 2004 Ariz. LEXIS 13 (Ariz., Feb. 10, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. LC 01-000128. The Honorable Michael D. Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee city filed civil enforcement complaints to collect transaction fees from appellant president of a pawnbroker corporation, as required by the city's transaction fee ordinance. The municipal court found the fee ordinance was an invalid tax and dismissed the city's complaints. The Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, disagreed, holding that the ordinance imposed a valid regulatory fee. The president appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the president contended the city's pawnbroker transaction fee under Phoenix, Ariz., City Code § 10-151(A) was an unconstitutional "tax" in violation of the Ariz. Const. art. IX, § 6. Alternatively, he argued that the state legislature preempted local control over pawnshops, therefore, the transaction fee ordinance was invalid, as it exceeded the limited scope of local regulation allowed by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 44-1632 (2003). Finally, he contended that, at the least, the fees were unconstitutionally excessive, because they were not in reasonable proportion to the services rendered. The appellate court disagreed on all of defendant's points, holding first that the charges were fees and not taxes. Further, the fee was assessed by the governmental entity that had been delegated regulatory authority over pawn transaction reports pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 44-1625 (2003). Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 44-1626(B)(6) (2003) did not evince an intent to preempt the city's transaction fee ordinance. Even assuming that the transaction fees covered all of the city's intended costs, they were not unconstitutionally excessive.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, and the case was remanded to the municipal court for further proceedings.

 

491 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Roosevelt Elem. Sch. Dist. No. 66 v. State


1 CA-CV 02-0475, 1 CA-CV 02-0590, 1 CA-CV 03-0118, (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


205 Ariz. 584; 74 P.3d 258; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 126; 406 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 33



August 14, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 23, 2004.
Review denied by, Request denied by Roosevelt Elem. v. State, 2004 Ariz. LEXIS 8 (Ariz., Jan. 7, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause Nos. CV 99-019062; CV 99-019062-2; CV 02-011568. The Honorable Edward O. Burke, Judge.
Roosevelt Elementary Sch. Dist. No. 66 v. Bishop, 179 Ariz. 233, 877 P.2d 806, 1994 Ariz. LEXIS 79 (Ariz., 1994)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, eight school districts, claimed that Ariz. Const. art. 11, § 1 was violated because the Arizona Legislature failed to fund the Building Renewal Fund (BRF), a component of the Students FIRST legislation, according to the statutory formula for fiscal years 1999-2003, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 15-2031 (Supp. 2002). The Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) agreed with the districts. Appellant State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Although the districts showed that they had capital facilities needing repairs and renovation, they did not link those needs to their pupils' scholastic performance. They showed instead that district officials had a more difficult situation than they would have if there were sufficient funds available to improve their facilities not directly linked to pedagogical success. While the districts complained about the lack of funding of the BRF to the extent of the statutory formula, they did not complain that BRF expenditures were directed in the first instance to those facilities "necessary and appropriate to enable pupils to achieve designated academic standards," nor had they challenged the School Facilities Board (SFB) guidelines. The facilities about which they complained were either new construction excluded from the BRF or primarily administrative and as such, were not required to meet the State's academic standards. There was no doubt that the public schools in Arizona needed adequate funding for students to achieve the academic standards declared by the legislature. However, the school districts had not shown that they had current unmet needs related to academic achievement.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded. The award of attorney fees to the school districts was vacated.

State v. Hazlett


1 CA-CR 02-0713, 1 CA-CR 02-0743, 1 CA-CR 02-0810, 1 CA-CR 02-0888 (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


205 Ariz. 523; 73 P.3d 1258; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 121; 406 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



August 12, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended August 14, 2003.
Review denied by In re State, 2004 Ariz. LEXIS 29 (Ariz., Mar. 16, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause Nos. CR 2002-005175, CR 2002-002845, CR 2001-018833, and CR 2002-002875. The Honorable Stephen A. Gerst, Judge, The Honorable Pamela J. Franks, Judge.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, dismissed indictments against defendants for sexual exploitation of a minor, in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3553(a)(2) (Supp. 2002), by finding that the statute was unconstitutionally overbroad because it encompassed expression protected by the First Amendment. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the trial court erred by ruling that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3553 (Supp. 2002), which prohibited the creation and possession of child pornography, was constitutionally overbroad. The appellate court noted that the statute did not encompass material in which an actual child was not involved. Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3556, by using the term "participant," implied the existence of an actual person as opposed to a fictitious character. By permitting an inference that the participant was a minor, the legislature reinforced that its intent in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3553 was solely to prohibit material using actual minors. Even though the punishment for violating § 13-3553 was severe, this did not provide support for invalidating the statute. The term "simulated" modified the conduct which was depicted, not the participant. The statute proscribed conduct related to the material only where it involved actual children actually participating in real or simulated sexual or exploitative acts. The appellate court did not know if the materials at issue could arguably fall within any definition of having serious literary, artistic, scientific or educational value.


OUTCOME: The rulings by the trial court finding the statutes dealing with sexual exploitation of children to be constitutionally overbroad were reversed, the orders dismissing the indictments were vacated, and those case were remanded to the trial court.

Moulton v. Napolitano


1 CA-CV 02-0642


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


205 Ariz. 506; 73 P.3d 637; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 120



August 5, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by In re Moulton, 2004 Ariz. LEXIS 27 (Ariz., Mar. 16, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 2001-020297. The Honorable Cathy M. Holt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant vehicle owners filed suit in superior court against appellees, several state officials and agencies (State), alleging breach of contract and violations of their constitutional rights, after the legislature repealed some tax benefits for modified automobiles. The State moved to dismiss. The Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) dismissed all of the claims against the State, citing a lack of jurisdiction. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The superior court held that the owners had failed to exhaust their administrative remedies before the Arizona Department of Revenue (ADOR). Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-1516(4) provided tax credits and other benefits for people who converted their new vehicles to alternative fuel vehicles. The statute was called the April Law. In December 2002 (the December Law) the Arizona Legislature amended the April Law. The owners did not only contest the amount of tax credits that they had received; they also challenged the requirements imposed by the December Law to keep those credits. The appellate court held that, because the owners complained about government benefits for which the legislature had provided a mandatory administrative remedy, the doctrine of exhaustion of remedies applied and the appellate court rejected the owners' attempt to circumvent the administrative process by the construction of their complaint. If the owners had not been satisfied by the ADOR ruling, they could have appealed the decision to the State Board of Tax Appeals, which was independent of ADOR. Only if the administrative appeal was unsuccessful, could the owners then have filed an action in superior court.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part. The superior court's dismissal of the owners' action for public records was reversed and the matter was remanded.

State v. Box


2 CA-CR 2001-0491


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


205 Ariz. 492; 73 P.3d 623; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 118; 405 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



July 31, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF GILA COUNTY Cause No. CR 01-013 Honorable Edward L. Dawson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Gila County (Arizona), which, after denying a motion to suppress, convicted defendant of transporting marijuana for sale.


OVERVIEW: A state police officer observed defendant's car exceeding the speed limit and informed a dispatcher. A county officer was then dispatched to stop defendant for speeding. After the county officer gave defendant a warning and returned his driver's license and other documents, he asked defendant whether there were any weapons or drugs in the car. Defendant appeared evasive, made inconsistent statements about where he had been staying, and refused consent to search the car. The county officer, who had a trained narcotics detection dog in his cruiser, promptly conducted a dog sniff search. The dog alerted to the presence of drugs, and the officer found marijuana in the trunk. The court found no error in the denial of defendant's motion to suppress, holding that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1594 authorized the county officer to stop defendant for a traffic violation committed outside the county officer's presence. Moreover, a dog sniff of a lawfully detained vehicle was not a search for Fourth Amendment purposes, and the continued detention of defendant for the purpose of conducting the dog sniff was sufficiently brief to be permissible.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

State v. Darelli


1 CA-CR 02-0432


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


205 Ariz. 458; 72 P.3d 1277; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 109; 405 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 10



July 22, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied December 4, 2003, Reported at: 2003 Ariz. LEXIS 145. Released for Publication January 5, 2004.
Review denied by State v. Darelli, 2003 Ariz. LEXIS 145 (Ariz., Dec. 4, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Yavapai County. Cause No. CR 01-0799. The Honorable William T. Kiger, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Conviction and sentences vacated, and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On the day of defendant's jury trial on charges arising from a domestic disturbance, the Superior Court in Yavapai County (Arizona) refused to accept any plea agreement, which was currently being negotiated, unless defendant pleaded guilty as charged or the State dismissed all of the charges. Trial proceeded, and defendant was convicted of aggravated assault, misdemeanor assault, and disorderly conduct with a deadly weapon. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On the morning of trial, defendant attempted to accept a plea offer made the night before. The district attorney indicated she would call her supervisor and the victims for approval of the offer. Upon learning of the negotiations, the trial court stated that, only a plea of guilty as charged or a total dismissal of the charges would be accepted, as the jury panel was already gathered. On appeal, the court held that the trial court's refusal to consider any plea negotiated except on an all or none basis, merely because the jury panel was gathered, improperly read a plea cut-off date into Ariz. R. Crim. P. 17.4(a) and foreclosed plea negotiations. Under Ariz. R. Crim. P. 17.4, defendant had a right to have any plea agreement reached addressed on the merits by the trial court. Only the district attorney's office had the right to terminate plea bargaining. Refusing to accept a conditional or partial plea also did not address the concern about the prospective jurors' time. The court held that the proper remedy was to vacate the convictions and sentences and to allow the parties to proceed with the plea negotiations.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's conviction and sentences and remanded the matter to the trial court to allow the parties to continue the plea negotiations.

State v. Soltero


1 CA-CR 02-0698


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


205 Ariz. 378; 71 P.3d 370; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 103; 403 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 8



July 3, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 18, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. LC 02-000133. The Honorable Michael D. Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted him of driving while under the extreme influence of intoxicating liquor (extreme DUI) in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1382(A) (Supp. 2002).


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the extreme DUI charge on the ground that the 2001 amendment to § 28-1382(A), which reduced the alcohol concentration limit, was unconstitutional. The motion was denied, and defendant was found guilty as charged. The court concluded that, having the amendment to § 28-1382(A) become immediately effective, pursuant to an emergency clause, without a grace period or specific notice to the public, did not violate due process. The court held that, because the amendment was passed with an emergency clause, it became effective the date it was signed by the governor and filed with the secretary of state. The court held defendant's conduct in operating a vehicle under the influence could not be construed as a passive act and did not involve conduct or circumstances so presumptively innocent as to fall within the exception to the traditional rule that ignorance of the law was no excuse. The court held that defendant was on notice of the existence of the laws regulating driving under the influence and could not avoid prosecution by asserting that the State failed to inform him of the particulars of the amended statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against defendant.

In re One Residence at 319 E. Fairgrounds Dr.


2 CA-CV 2002-0117


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


205 Ariz. 403; 71 P.3d 930; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 104; 403 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 4



July 3, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. C20004100. Honorable John F. Kelly, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowner was convicted of possession of a narcotic drug for sale and possession of drug paraphernalia. Appellee State filed a civil, in rem complaint seeking forfeiture of the house. The Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) entered summary judgment in favor of the State and forfeited the owner's interest in his house, in which police had found a large amount of drugs, cash and several guns. The homeowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Inter alia, the owner argued that the trial court erred by allowing the state to exact an excessive fine. He contended the forfeiture of his house amounted to a punitive fine wholly out of proportion to the crimes for which he was convicted. The appellate court applied the Austin and Bajakajian analyses to in rem forfeiture under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2314 to determine if it too had a punitive element. Because § 13-2314(G) had a deterrent purpose, it was not solely remedial. Since the owner's house was not the instrument of his crime, and because Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2314(G) had both retributive and deterrent aspects, the Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A, found that the civil, in rem forfeiture of the house was punishment, at least in part. However, the legislature considered possession of a narcotic drug for sale a very serious crime. Comparing the value of the house to the offense, the forfeited amount (or value) was not grossly disproportional to the crime committed. The appellate court concluded that the forfeiture of the owner's house, although subject to review under the U.S. Const. amend. VIII, did not amount to an unconstitutionally excessive fine.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Rodriguez


2 CA-CR 2001-0537


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


205 Ariz. 392; 71 P.3d 919; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 99; 403 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 18



June 27, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Rodriguez, 2004 Ariz. LEXIS 23 (Ariz., Feb. 10, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-20012298. Honorable Frank Dawley, Judge Pro Tempore. Honorable Richard D. Nichols, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile was prosecuted as an adult and, after a bench trial, was found guilty by the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) of possession of a deadly weapon by a prohibited possessor. The juvenile was placed on intensive probation for four years, conditioned on a four-month jail term. The juvenile appealed the convictions and probationary term.


OVERVIEW: The superior court had personal jurisdiction over the juvenile, even though the State violated the directive of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-501(D) because, despite the lack of notice, the juvenile was well aware of the allegation that he was a chronic felony offender. Moreover, he received a hearing pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-501(E) at which the State had to prove, and the superior court had to find, that he in fact was a chronic felony offender as defined in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-501(G)(2). The State satisfied its burden that the juvenile was a chronic felony offender because it was not required to introduce the juvenile court minute entries into evidence for the superior court to make the factual finding. In addition, by not objecting at the time, the juvenile waived any argument that the State's evidence was inadequate. Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-501(E) was not constitutionally flawed under the Apprendi rule because it was not a sentence enhancement scheme. The superior court properly denied a motion to suppress the gun because the officers could have reasonably perceived an immediate danger to their safety that warranted lifting a mattress and temporarily seizing the gun.


OUTCOME: The convictions and probationary term were affirmed.

State v. Johnson


1 CA-CR 01-0204


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


205 Ariz. 413; 72 P.3d 343; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 89; 402 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



June 17, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 28, 2003.
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Johnson v. Bartos, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 141933 (D. Ariz., Dec. 23, 2010)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Without prejudice, Certificate of appealability denied Johnson v. Ryan, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 161676 (D. Ariz., Dec. 2, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 1994-010138. The Honorable Crane McClennen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant fired one round from his rifle, hitting a police officer. A jury found defendant guilty of aggravated assault for shooting the police officer, in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1203(A)(1) (1989). Defendant was then retried in the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) on bystander assault charges using the doctrine of transferred intent and was found guilty of five counts of aggravated assault. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Over defendant's objection, the trial court instructed the jury on transferred intent, permitting the State to argue that defendant's intent to shoot the police officer could be transferred to serve as the intent for the assaults on the bystanders. Defendant argued that the court erred by instructing the jury on transferred intent. The appellate court concluded that the intent to shoot and cause injury or death could not have been transferred to have provided the intent to have placed the bystanders in reasonable apprehension of imminent physical injury, and the jury instruction had therefore been erroneous. The assault conviction against defendant for the shooting of the officer was for the form of assault defined in § 13-1203(A)(1) (1989) as "intentionally, knowingly or recklessly causing any physical injury to another person." In contrast, the bystander assault charges were based on the apprehension form of assault defined in § 13-1203(A)(2) (1989) as "intentionally placing another person in reasonable apprehension of imminent physical injury." It could not have been presumed from the act of firing a shot at the officer that defendant intended to scare any of the bystanders.


OUTCOME: The conviction was reversed, and the case was remanded.

State v. Brown


2 CA-SA 2003-0003


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


205 Ariz. 325; 70 P.3d 454; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 106



May 23, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Brown, 2004 Ariz. LEXIS 72 (Ariz., June 29, 2004)
Vacated by, Remanded by State v. Brown, 209 Ariz. 200, 99 P.3d 15, 2004 Ariz. LEXIS 114 (Ariz., 2004)
Post-conviction relief granted at, in part, Post-conviction relief denied at, in part State v. Brown, 2005 Ariz. App. LEXIS 77 (Ariz. Ct. App., June 22, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Santa Cruz County Cause No. CR-01-199.



DISPOSITION: Orders vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After real party in interest, pursuant to a plea agreement, pleaded guilty to reckless manslaughter, respondent trial court judge entered presentence orders regarding the constitutionality and burden of proof under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-702 and -702.01. The judge sua sponte vacated its order to allow petitioner State of Arizona to seek review in the instant special action.


OVERVIEW: The plea agreement set forth the minimum sentence of 3 years, presumptive sentence of 5 years, and maximum sentence of 12.5 years for reckless manslaughter. The judge entered an order that the State would have to prove to a jury and beyond a reasonable doubt any aggravating circumstances alleged under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-702(C). After the State petitioned for relief from that order, the judge ruled that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-702 and -702.01 were unconstitutional facially and as applied to real party in interest. The court granted the State's petition for review in a special action and held that the statutes were not unconstitutional. Reckless manslaughter, a violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1103(A)(1) and (B), was a class two felony, the sentence for which was provided to be 5 years under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-701. The court held that such was a presumptive, not a maximum, sentence. The court further held that the trial court could order a sentence within the 3- to 12.5-year range without running afoul of the Fifth or Sixth Amendments, as such would not result in a sentence greater than the maximum prescribed by statute.


OUTCOME: The court granted relief, reaffirmed its prior order vacating the judge's orders, and vacated the judge's orders. The court directed that further proceedings could proceed in the trial court.

 

501 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sanders


1 CA-CR 00-0326


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


205 Ariz. 208; 68 P.3d 434; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 74; 400 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



May 13, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 6, 2004.
Review denied by State v. Sanders, 2003 Ariz. LEXIS 148 (Ariz., Dec. 5, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 99-017496. The Honorable Steven D. Sheldon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Conviction vacated without prejudice; remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An amendment proposed mid-trial changed the original charge from an assault committed by a knowing touching of an officer with the intent to injure, insult, or provoke to an assault committed by intentionally placing the officer in reasonable apprehension. After overruling defendant's objection to the amendment, the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Arizona, convicted defendant of aggravated assault. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the trial court violated the Sixth Amendment's notice requirement when it permitted the State to amend the assault charge after the close of the state's case-in-chief. The appellate court determined that the amendment changed the nature of the originally charged offense, as the amended charge specified that defendant intentionally placed the officer in reasonable apprehension of imminent physical injury. Assault committed in this fashion required a showing of defendant's intent to create fear of injury in the officer, and merely showing an intent to provoke or insult would not have sufficed. As "reasonable apprehension" assault was a different offense from "knowing touching" assault, the appellate court held that the mid-trial amendment from the one to the other changed the nature of the offense, was prejudicial per se, and was therefore impermissible under Ariz. R. Crim. P. 13.5(b). As such, the trial court violated the Sixth Amendment by permitting the State to amend the charge, thereby depriving defendant of his right to sufficient notice of the charges against him.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

Armenta v. City of Casa Grande


2 CA-CV 2000-0138


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


205 Ariz. 367; 71 P.3d 359; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 97; 402 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 17



April 22, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Corrected by interlineation per order dated 6/25/2003. Motion to Redesignate Decision as Published Opinion Granted June 25, 2003. Released for Publication August 5, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PINAL COUNTY. Cause No. CV99046853. Honorable William J. O'Neil, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother, on her own behalf and that of her minor son, filed a personal injury lawsuit against defendant city seeking damages for injuries the son suffered while playing in a city park. The Superior Court of Pinal County, Arizona, granted the city's motion for summary judgment. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The son was injured when, while riding his bicycle under a soccer goal, he tried to reach up to grab the crossbar; the crossbar broke and both he and the bar fell to the ground. On review, the mother contended, inter alia, that Arizona's recreational use immunity statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 33-1551 did not apply to this case. Finding that Ariz. Rev. Stat. 13-1551(C)(3) specifically included parks in its definition of premises, that installing soccer fields, including goals, in a park did not change the park's recreational character, and that soccer goals were the type of apparatus one would expect to find on a park field, the appellate court ruled that the statute applied. Future, the mother did not present sufficient evidence to create a material issue of fact on whether the city knew or should have known, even by regular inspections, about the goal's allegedly defective condition and, thus, knew or should have known that the goal posed an unreasonable risk of death or serious bodily injury to children in the park. The mother failed to raise material issues of fact to preclude summary judgment on her attractive nuisance and gross negligence causes of action.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Mutschler


1 CA-CR 02-0002, 1 CA-CR 02-0003, 1 CA-CR 02-0004, 1 CA-CR 02-0005, (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


204 Ariz. 520; 65 P.3d 469; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 51; 396 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 16



April 1, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Mutschler v. City of Phoenix, 2006 Ariz. App. LEXIS 11 (Ariz. Ct. App., Feb. 14, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause Nos. LC 00-001992, LC 00-001999, LC 00-002000, and LC 00-002002. The Honorable Michael D. Jones, Judge.
Recreational Devs. of Phoenix, Inc. v. City of Phoenix, 83 F. Supp. 2d 1072, 1999 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 20738 (D. Ariz., 1999)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted in municipal court for violating Phoenix, Ariz., City Code § 23-54 (1999). Defendants appealed their convictions arguing that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague and/or overbroad. The Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, found that the ordinance was not vague, that defendants lacked standing to claim the ordinance was overbroad, and affirmed defendants' convictions and sentences. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendants continued to assert that Phoenix, Ariz., City Code § 23-54 (1999), was unconstitutionally vague and/or overbroad. Contrary to the court below, the instant court found that defendants had standing to bring their vagueness and overbreadth challenges as defendants arguments included the assertion that terms within the ordinance were subject to varying interpretations and/or meanings, and some forms of nude dancing had previously been found to be marginally within the outer perimeters of the First Amendment. However, the instant court found that § 23-54 was not vague as the applicable ordinances and rules reasonably informed employees of such facilities as to the limits of their permitted activities and the prohibitions regarding live sex act businesses found in § 23-54 did not conflict with any other city ordinance or State law regarding sexually oriented businesses. The instant court also found there was no realistic danger that § 23-54 would significantly jeopardize recognized First Amendment protections of nude or erotic dancers/performers; thus, the ordinance was not overbroad.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Kaiser


1 CA-CR 02-0448


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


204 Ariz. 514; 65 P.3d 463; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 53; 396 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 19



April 1, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied September 9, 2003.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Kaiser v. Ariz., 2004 U.S. LEXIS 861 (U.S., Jan. 26, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. LC 2001-000277. The Honorable Michael D. Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted for refusing to obey a peace officer. The Maricopa County Superior Court, Arizona, affirmed the conviction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A police officer stopped the car in which defendant was a passenger. Defendant's wife was the driver. Despite being told to remain in the car, defendant got out of the car and approached the officer. Eventually, he was arrested for failing to return to and remain in the car when told to do so, and for interfering with the investigation. Defendant argued on appeal that Scottsdale, Ariz., Code § 19-13, was vague because no mens rea was required. Contrary to defendant's arguments, the appellate court determined that a person of ordinary intelligence would understand what the ordinance here prohibited, and in what context that conduct may be prohibited. Further, § 19-13 provided sufficient objective standards for one charged with its enforcement to know what conduct is unlawful. The appellate court could not discern a realistic danger that § 19-13 would significantly put at risk the First Amendment rights of those persons not before the court. The ordinance was not vague or overbroad.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the conviction.

In re Property Located at 6757 S. Burcham Ave.


2 CA-CV 2002-0092


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


204 Ariz. 401; 64 P.3d 843; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 38; 395 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 20



March 17, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. C-20010960. Honorable Lina S. Rodriguez, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) ordered appellant property owner's real property forfeited, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 13-2301(D)(4), 13-2314(G), 13-3413, and 13-4301 through 4315, after the State found a total of 862.5 pounds of marijuana at the premises. The owner appealed the denial of his motion for new trial, arguing the court abused its discretion by allowing the state, inter alia, to call a surprise witness.


OVERVIEW: The state argued that, because the owner failed to comply with Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2314(M) by not timely serving the attorney general with a copy of the notice of appeal and the opening brief, the appellate court lacked jurisdiction and should have dismissed the appeal. Because the owner timely filed a notice of appeal from an appealable order, the appellate court concluded that it had jurisdiction. The legislature could not have divested the owner of that substantive right or the appellate court to hear his appeal because of his failure to have complied with a statute that conflicted with a rule promulgated by the Supreme Court of Arizona. The State disclosed the witness's name on July 6, 2001, and the fingerprint evidence on July 10, although the owner moved to produce reports of "fingerprint comparisons" in March 2000. Trial began on July 12. The State claimed the witness had not been a surprise witness, as his name was disclosed in the police reports, and the owner repeatedly discussed the witness's prior criminal history before trial with the prosecutor. The trial court had not abused its discretion in allowing the state to introduce the evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

506 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


In re Miguel R.


1 CA-JV 02-0016, 1 CA-JV 02-0072, (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


204 Ariz. 328; 63 P.3d 1065; 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 29; 394 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 44



February 25, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 1, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause Nos. JV 151184 and JV 150204. The Honorable Thomas Dunevant, III, Judge. The Honorable Janet E. Barton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, two juveniles, pled guilty to separate crimes of possession of marijuana and theft. Appellants challenged the judgment of the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona), which entered dispositions requiring the two juveniles to participate in the Maricopa County Juvenile Drug Court program as a special term of standard probation. The juveniles' appeals were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the juveniles argued that participation in Drug Court violated fundamental constitutional rights. The juveniles argued that involuntary placement in Drug Court did not promote rehabilitation and was not in fact reasonably related to the purpose of juvenile probation. Further, the juveniles contended that the facts of their respective cases did not support their placement in Drug Court. The appellate court held that the purposes of the Drug Court were directed towards rehabilitation and based upon the record. The juveniles' constitutional rights were not violated. Both juveniles were already on standard probation, and both juveniles' parents indicated willingness to have their children in the program. Furthermore, both juveniles initially wanted to participate. Therefore, the trial court's disposition was not an abuse of discretion. The court also found that the Drug Court procedures did not violate due process, the juvenile's protection against self-incrimination, or equal protection. Requiring Drug Court participation as a special term of probation was rationally related to rehabilitation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

507 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Bertleson v. Sacks Tierney, P.A.


1 CA-CV 01-0527


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


204 Ariz. 124; 60 P.3d 703; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 200; 389 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 12



December 26, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Released for Publication July 22, 2003. Review denied by Bertleson v. Tierney, 2003 Ariz. LEXIS 102 (Ariz., July 2, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV00-008230. The Honorable Paul A. Katz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant clients challenged a decision from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which dismissed their negligence action against appellee attorneys after the clients failed to produce an expert opinion certificate, as required by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-2602(A) (2000).


OVERVIEW: The clients retained the attorneys to represent them in a case against a corporation. Later, the clients filed a negligence action. However, the claim was dismissed, as the clients failed to file an expert witness certificate, as required by § 12-2602(A). The clients contended that § 12-2602 was unconstitutional. In affirming, the court determined that § 12-2602 did not violate the Equal Protection Clause, Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 13. Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-2602 did not implicate a fundamental right or discriminate against individuals based on a suspect class. First, § 12-2602 had been amended so as not to require an expert opinion. Moreover, it did not restrict the choice of experts, require service of an expert affidavit with the complaint, and did not mandate dismissal. The court also found that § 12-2602 did not implicate a suspect class. Because § 12-2602 was rationally based and furthered a legitimate state interest, it was constitutional. Additionally, the court determined that the Separation of Powers Clause, Ariz. Const. art. 3 was not violated. Nothing in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-2602 was in conflict with or engulfed the Arizona Supreme Court's rulemaking power.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

508 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Empress Adult Video & Bookstore v. City of Tucson


2 CA-CV 2000-0079


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


204 Ariz. 50; 59 P.3d 814; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 183; 387 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 14



November 27, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 8, 2003.
Review denied by Empress Adult Video v. City of Tucson/State, 2003 Ariz. LEXIS 75 (Ariz., May 28, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. 336804. Honorable Nanette M. Warner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adult-oriented business sought an injunction against the enforcement of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1422, which enforced certain mandatory closing times, and a declaratory judgment that the statute violated Ariz. Const. art. II, §§ 6 and 13. The Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) denied injunctive relief, holding that the statute did not violate Arizona's constitution. The business appealed.


OVERVIEW: The business contended the greater scope of art. II, § 6 protected the non-obscene, sexually explicit materials and live performances encompassed by Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 13-1422 and 11-821. The appellate court held that the application of § 13-1422 to an adult theater, as defined in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 11-821, did not violate Ariz. Const. art. II, §§ 6 or 13. The appellate court further held, that the application of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1422 to an adult arcade, adult bookstore or video store, and adult motion picture theater, as they were defined in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 11-821, did violate Ariz. Const. art. II, § 6. The closing-hours requirement of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1422 was valid and enforceable as applied to an adult theater and invalid and unenforceable as applied to an adult arcade, adult bookstore or video store, and adult motion picture theater. Accordingly, as to the valid, enforceable application of § 13-1422, the appellate court affirmed the trial court's granting of declaratory judgment in favor of the city and denial injunctive relief to the business. The invalid portions were severable from the remainder of § 13-1422, and the remaining valid portion remained in force.


OUTCOME: The trial court's granting of declaratory judgment in favor of the city and state and denial injunctive relief to the business was affirmed. But, as to the invalid, unenforceable application of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1422, the appellate court reversed the trial court and directed that it enter declaratory judgment and injunctive relief in favor of the business.

 

509 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Parker v. Ariz. Interscholastic Ass'n


1 CA-CV 01-0364


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


204 Ariz. 42; 59 P.3d 806; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 185; 393 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 13



November 26, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 8, 2003. Review denied by Parker v. AZ Interscholastic, 2003 Ariz. LEXIS 54 (Ariz., Apr. 22, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 2000-016302. The Honorable Barry C. Schneider, Judge. The Honorable Roland J. Steinle, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, granted judgment in favor of appellee interscholastic association, in appellant student's suit against the association for violating Arizona's open enrollment statutes, Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 15-816 and 15-816.01 (2002), and equal protection rights. The student appealed.


OVERVIEW: The student voluntarily transferred to another school and was found ineligible to play sports for one year. The student argued that the transfer rule was invalid, as it conflicted with Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 15-816 and 15-816.01(A), which established an open enrollment policy in Arizona schools. The appellate court found that, while a student had a right to a public education, participation in interscholastic athletics was not a constitutionally protected right. The open enrollment statutes did not protect a transferring student's right to participate in interscholastic athletics. The association's bylaws did not prohibit the application of the open enrollment policy and were not an improper encroachment on the legislature's powers. Because the student was not a member of a suspect class, nor had he been deprived of a fundamental right, the rational basis test was the appropriate test to determine whether the transfer rule violated equal protection rights. By establishing objective eligibility standards, the transfer rule acted to deter athletically motivated transfers. The judgment enjoining enforcement of the restitution rule was a judgment in the student's favor.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Emmett McLoughlin Realty, Inc. v. Pima County


2 CA-CV 2001-0198


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


203 Ariz. 557; 58 P.3d 39; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 176



November 19, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Emmett McLoughlin Realty v. Pima County, 2006 Ariz. App. LEXIS 17 (Ariz. Ct. App., Feb. 17, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. C20003514. Honorable Charles V. Harrington, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff realty company did not consent to rezoning of its property and filed an action against defendant county's downzoning of its property. The county argued that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 11-829(F) was an unconstitutional delegation of authority. The Pima County Superior Court, Arizona, agreed. The realty company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county board of supervisors considered and approved a county-initiated rezoning of a parcel of land owned by realty company and the convenience stores. The county admitted its legislative act of downzoning the property was undertaken without the express written consent of the owners of the property, in contravention of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 11-829(F). The realty company first contended Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 11-829(F) was not a delegation of authority to property owners, but merely constituted the legislature's withdrawal of a portion of the counties' zoning power. The appellate court determined that nothing in the legislative history suggested the Arizona legislature adopted Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 11-829(F) intending to completely withdraw counties' zoning powers or to enact a total prohibition on county-initiated downzoning. Instead, the legislative history indicated that the legislature's purpose in adopting the subsection was protecting property values through the owner consent provision. The appellate court agreed with the trial court that the entire subsection was invalid.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Facilitec, Inc. v. Hibbs


1 CA-CV 01-0139


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T


204 Ariz. 39; 59 P.3d 803; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 172; 388 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 6



November 5, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Corrected by, 11/29/2002
Review granted by Facilitec, Inc. v. Hibbs, 2003 Ariz. LEXIS 39 (Ariz., Apr. 22, 2003)
Vacated by, Remanded by Facilitec, Inc. v. Hibbs, 2003 Ariz. LEXIS 141 (Ariz., Dec. 10, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 99-22372. The Honorable Susan R. Bolton. The Honorable Kenneth L. Fields. The Honorable Edward O. Burke.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Arizona Department of Administration (ADOA) challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Arizona, granting partial summary judgment to appellee contract bidder on the bidder's challenge to a decision rendered by the ADOA's Deputy Director concerning the bidder's demand that a contract to provide office furniture to the State of Arizona be rescinded and a new one be awarded to it.


OVERVIEW: The ADOA awarded the contract to a third party, and the bidder protested. The State Procurement Officer denied the protest, and the bidder appealed to the ADOA Director, who delegated the matter to the ADOA Deputy Director. The deputy director referred the matter to an administrative law judge (ALJ), who recommend that the bidder be awarded an additional, non-exclusive contract to provide office furniture to the State of Arizona. On review, the deputy director rejected that part of the ALJ's recommendation and issued an agency decision that denied the bidder's protest. The trial court agreed with the bidder that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 38-462 (2001) could not be validly interpreted to impliedly grant to the deputy director the judicial function of the director. The appellate court ruled that the deputy director decided the bidder's procurement protest pursuant to a proper grant of authority from both the Arizona Legislature and the ADOA Director. The language of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-702(A) authorized the director to delegate to the deputy the decision-making duty in question.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded with directions to grant partial summary judgment to the ADOA.

Maricopa County v. Kinko's Inc.


1 CA-TX 01-0010


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T


203 Ariz. 496; 56 P.3d 70; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 164; 385 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 42



October 24, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 15, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Arizona Tax Court. Cause Nos. TX 99-000248/00-00125/00-00129/00-00130. The Honorable Jeffrey S. Cates, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, companies that owned personal property and did business in Arizona at multiple locations, appealed the summary judgment entered by Arizona Tax Court against them based on the conclusion that the Arizona Constitution allowed the legislature to exempt from taxation a maximum of $ 50,000 per year of personal property of a taxpayer used for agricultural, trade, or business purposes, regardless of the number of locations owned.


OVERVIEW: The companies contended that Arizona law should have been interpreted to have allowed a $ 50,000 annual exemption for property at each location. On the basis of Ariz. Const. art. 9, § 2(6), the appellate court affirmed the judgment of the tax court. Article 9, § 2(6) limited the power of the legislature to extend to each taxpayer more than one annual tax exemption up to $ 50,000 of agricultural, trade, or business property, regardless of the number of locations at which the taxpayer put such property to use, and the appellate court held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-11127 (1999) was unconstitutional, because it purported to grant exemptions to each "assessment account" or location, allowing multiple exemptions for multiple locations. The appellate court declared former Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-280 (1997) to have been automatically revived to take the place of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-11127. The tax court did not abuse its discretion by denying the companies additional time to conduct discovery pertaining to their Uniformity Clause argument. Because the companies did not prevail, their request for attorney fees pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-348(B) (Supp. 2001) was denied.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the tax court was affirmed.

LaFaro v. Cahill


1 CA-CV 01-0084


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


203 Ariz. 482; 56 P.3d 56; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 163; 385 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 8



October 22, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 10, 2002,


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 2000-093239. The Honorable M. Jean Hoag, Judge. The Honorable Cheryl K. Hendrix, Judge (Retired).



DISPOSITION: VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city councilman appealed from an injunction against harassment issued by the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) that precluded him from initiating "in person" contact with appellee chairman of a citizen's committee. The chairman petitioned for an ex parte injunction against the councilman to prohibit "harassment," pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-1809(R) (Supp. 2000).


OVERVIEW: The issues were whether an injunction against harassment that restricted protected political speech was unconstitutional and could the statute that authorized injunctions against harassment be given an interpretation that rendered it constitutional? The appellate court answered those questions in the affirmative. The plain language of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-1809(R) (Supp. 2000) required a finding that the councilman engaged in a "series of acts" of harassment that were "directed at a specific person." One of the two reported incidents concerned a conversation between the councilman and another person. The committee chairman overheard part of that conversation in which the councilman denounced the committee's efforts and allegedly used words such as "bigot," "fascist," and "homophobe" to describe him. The councilman's communication did not satisfy the definition of harassment. The appellate court also held that § 12-1809 was not unconstitutional in all its potential applications, as long as its definition of harassment, conduct that "served no legitimate purpose," was construed to exclude pure political speech.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was vacated, and the case was remanded.

State v. Stauffer


2 CA-SA 2002-0067


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


203 Ariz. 551; 58 P.3d 33; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 160; 384 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 26



October 10, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Graham County Cause No. CR 2002-089.



DISPOSITION: RELIEF GRANTED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State sought special action relief in the Arizona Court of Appeals from respondent Graham County District Court's order in defendant's underlying sexual abuse prosecution, granting defendant's motion to compel interviews of three witnesses the State intended to call at trial.


OVERVIEW: The State sought to call three witnesses to testify that defendant committed similar acts of sexual misconduct against them. The State claimed the three were victims who had the right to refuse defense interviews under the Victims' Bill of Rights, Ariz. Const. art. II, § 2.1(A) and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4433. Only one of the witnesses' claims resulted in criminal charges against defendant. Defendant moved to compel interviews with the witnesses, and the trial court granted the motion. The appellate court had to address the issue of whether victims' rights attached to witnesses in the prosecution of a defendant for an offense against a third person. The court found that the witness who's claim resulted in criminal charges against defendant had the right to refuse an interview as a continuation of her rights that were implemented pursuant to her status as a victim in her own case, not from defendant's arrest or prosecution in the instant case. However, the court found that the remaining two witnesses' rights to refuse to be interviewed had not yet arisen, because defendant had not been charged for any criminal acts he might have committed against those two prospective witnesses.


OUTCOME: The trial court's granting of defendant's motion to compel interviews with three witnesses was reversed as to one witness and affirmed as to the other two witnesses.
