Tornabene v. Bonine ex rel. Ariz. Highway Dep't


2 CA-CV 2001-0124


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


203 Ariz. 326; 54 P.3d 355; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 146; 382 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 6



September 19, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 3, 2003.
Review denied by Tornabene v. Bonine, 2003 Ariz. LEXIS 79 (Ariz., May 28, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. C20005504. Honorable Michael J. Brown, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order of the superior court reversed; ALJ's order that suspended plaintiff's driver's license reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After an evidentiary hearing pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1321(G) and (K), a department of transportation, motor vehicle division (MVD), administrative law judge (ALJ) suspended appellee motorist's license for 12 months for driving under the influence (DUI). The Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) vacated the suspension of the license because it held that the police had lacked probable cause to stop the motorist. The MVD appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue, one of first impression in Arizona was: did the alleged unconstitutionality of a law enforcement officer's stop of a vehicle invalidate the State's subsequent suspension of the motorist's driver's license, pursuant to § 28-1321, based on the motorist's refusal to submit to a breath test after having been arrested for DUI? The ALJ implicitly answered the question in the negative. The superior court ruled otherwise. The MVD contended the superior court erroneously considered whether the stop of the vehicle had been lawful, arguing that § 28-1321(K) expressly limited the scope of issues for administrative review. The appellate court found that there was nothing in § 28-1321 or its underlying rationale that suggested any intent to incorporate all the procedural protections available to a DUI criminal defendant into a civil license suspension. Rather, the legislature had apparently intended such hearings to be narrowly focused, inter alia, on the question of whether a police officer had reasonable grounds to believe that the motorist had been driving while under the influence regardless of the circumstances of the underlying stop.


OUTCOME: The superior court's order was reversed and the ALJ's license suspension order was reinstated.

In re Wilber W.


1 CA-MH 01-0008 SP


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


203 Ariz. 301; 53 P.3d 1145; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 137; 382 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 34



September 11, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

 [***1] THIS OPINION WAS VACATED BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Vacated, Stay vacated, Remanded: In re Detention of Wilber W., 2003 Ariz. LEXIS 12 (Ariz. Jan. 23, 2003).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Mohave County. Cause No. CV 2000-0152. The Honorable James E. Chavez, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Commitment order vacated; matter remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed from an order of the Superior Court in Mohave County (Arizona) that committed him to the Arizona Community Protection and Treatment Center as a sexually violent person (SVP) following a jury trial conducted pursuant to Arizona's Sexually Violent Persons Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 36-3701 to -3717 (Supp. 2001). Petitioner raised several evidentiary issues and also argued that the Act was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner also argued that the Act violated the due process rights of persons committed thereunder by not requiring a finding of serious difficulty in controlling behavior, in accordance with Crane. He also contended that he was improperly found to be an SVP because the trial court failed to give a jury instruction defining "likely" in § 36-3701(7)(b) to mean "highly probable" that he would "engage in acts of sexual violence." The State responded that the Act sufficiently narrowed the class of persons eligible for confinement to those who have serious diminished control over their dangerousness. The appellate court vacated the commitment order, because there was no specific finding at the commitment hearing that petitioner had serious difficulty controlling his behavior. The court then asked whether due process, according to Hendricks, required an additional finding of volitional incapacity? The appellate court held that based on Crane, it was not enough that Arizona's Act required a finding of dangerousness linked with the existence of a mental disorder. To pass constitutional muster, the Act had to also require proof of serious difficulty controlling behavior, which it did.


OUTCOME: The commitment order was vacated and the case was remanded for a new commitment hearing with the jury to be instructed in accordance with the decision.

 

517 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Benenati


2 CA-CR 1999-0064


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


203 Ariz. 235; 52 P.3d 804; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 134; 381 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



September 3, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied February 11, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-55006. Honorable Clark W. Munger, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; VACATED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury of the Pima County Superior Court, Arizona, found defendant guilty of two counts of unlawful sale of a narcotic drug. After finding he had three prior convictions and had committed these offenses while on release for a separate felony offense, the trial court sentenced defendant to concurrent, presumptive, 17.75-year prison terms, including a two-year mandatory enhancement, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604(R). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in: (1) responding ex parte to a jury question; (2) finding, instead of permitting the jury to find, that he was on release at the time he committed his offenses; and (3) finding that his out-of-state convictions constituted historical prior felony convictions. The instant court found no merit to defendant's first and third claims. In answering the jury's question, the trial court neither explicitly nor implicitly commented on the evidence. The instant court was unable to conclude that defendant suffered any prejudice; thus, any error the trial court might have committed was harmless. Regarding defendant's out-of-state convictions, the trial court did not err in imposing an enhanced sentence, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604(D), based on defendant's having had two or more historical prior felony convictions. The trial court erred, however, in failing to submit defendant's release status to the jury. The instant court agreed that Apprendi v. New Jersey required that any fact, other than the fact of a prior conviction, exposing a defendant to a punishment greater than that otherwise permissible had to be determined by a jury.


OUTCOME: The instant court vacated defendant's sentence enhancement. However, because the trial court found neither aggravating nor mitigating factors, it did not need to vacate the presumptive sentences the trial court imposed on defendant's unlawful sale convictions.

Long v. Napolitano


1 CA-CV 02-0036


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


203 Ariz. 247; 53 P.3d 172; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 129; 381 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 26



August 27, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 27, 2002.
Review denied by Long v. Napolitano, 2002 Ariz. LEXIS 228 (Ariz., Dec. 6, 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 01-015659. The Honorable Mark Santana, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tax payer filed a special action in the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) that challenged the Arizona Tourism and Sports Authority (TSA), Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 5-802 to -877 (Supp. 2001), as an unconstitutional "special law," as it benefited only one county in the state. The superior court concluded that the TSA legislation did not violate any constitutional provision. The tax payer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issues were whether legislation creating and implementing the TSA was an unconstitutional special law favoring only one of the state's counties and whether the TSA funding mechanism violated the constitutional debt limitation. The appellate court held that the population classification used in the TSA legislation was sufficiently elastic, as it allowed entry and exit from the class upon requisite changes in population, and, after severing language from Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 5-866 that authorized the TSA to pledge all monies received by it to pay and secure bond obligations, did not violate Ariz. Const. art. 9, § 5, as it was not an unconstitutional special law favoring only the one county. The appellate court also held that the TSA did not violate the constitutional state-debt restriction by pledging specified transaction privilege taxes and income taxes to pay and secure bond obligations. However, the TSA could not constitutionally pledge income taxes paid by a sports team's employees or their spouses on income unrelated to professional football. Likewise, the TSA was prohibited from pledging monies from the state's general funds to pay and secure bond obligations.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed as modified.

 

519 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Putz v. Indus. Comm'n


1 CA-IC 01-0103


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


203 Ariz. 146; 51 P.3d 979; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 123; 380 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 20



August 15, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 17, 2002.
Amended by, 08/26/2002


PRIOR HISTORY: Special Action___Industrial Commission ICA CLAIM NO. 20003-290011. CARRIER NO. NONE. Administrative Law Judge Joseph L. Moore. AWARD SET ASIDE.



DISPOSITION: AWARD SET ASIDE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent employee's claim for workers' compensation benefits was denied by the No Insurance Section of respondent Industrial Commission of Arizona's Special Fund Division. Following a hearing, an administrative law judge (ALJ) found the claim was compensable. Petitioner employer filed a special action requesting that the Commission's award for compensable claim be set aside.


OVERVIEW: The employer, a licensed residential contractor, hired the employee to help construct a 40-by-80-foot prefabricated metal building. On the job site, the employee fell from a ladder, sustaining multiple broken bones and a ruptured lung. In determining that the employee's claim was compensable, the ALJ found inter alia that the employer was an employer subject to the Act within the meaning of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-902(A). The ALJ based his finding on the employee's argument that the "definitive factor" for determining the Act's applicability was the existence of a scheme or plan or periodic need for extra short-term employees in the usual course of the business of the employer, and that for a part of the year during which his injury occurred, the employer hired workers 25 percent of the time. The court rejected the ALJ's reasoning, finding that the determinative question was whether the employer customarily or regularly employed at least one worker, or whether he hired extra labor only occasionally and unpredictably, and that the record did not reveal a hiring plan for short-term labor by the employer that was anything but occasional and unpredictable.


OUTCOME: Concluding that the employer was not an employer covered by the Act, the court set the award aside.

 

520 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jeffrey


2 CA-CR 2000-0260


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


203 Ariz. 111; 50 P.3d 861; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 119; 379 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



July 30, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Jeffrey, 2003 Ariz. LEXIS 92 (Ariz., July 1, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-66422. Honorable Howard Hantman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After her first trial, a jury convicted defendant of four counts of disorderly conduct and one count of theft by control, but could not reach a verdict on four kidnapping charges. Following her second trial, a new jury convicted defendant on all kidnapping counts. Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which convicted her of four kidnappings.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and the perpetrator entered the victims' home in an attempt to steal drugs. They forced the victims' to move about within the house and tied them up. The defense was duress, but defendant testified that she had not attempted to escape from the crime scene, the perpetrator had twice given her his gun, she returned it to him, and she admitted to a police officer that she assisted the perpetrator because she was stupid. The appellate court found that: (1) because the absence of duress was not an element of kidnapping, the legislature could constitutionally impose upon the defendant the burden of proving it; (2) refusal to give a jury instruction that erroneously treated lack of duress as an element of the crime was not an abuse of discretion; (3) refusal to permit evidence of the perpetrator's previous suicide attempt was harmless error, because of the overwhelming evidence of guilt and lack of duress; and (4) refusal to grant a mistrial based on the bullet was not an abuse of discretion, as the trial court gave a cautionary instruction.


OUTCOME: The superior court's judgment was affirmed.

Robson Ranch Mts., L.L.C. v. Pinal County


2 CA-CV 2002-0054, 2 CA-CV 2002-0060 (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


203 Ariz. 120; 51 P.3d 342; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 110; 378 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 94



July 18, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 4, 2002.
Review denied by Robson Ranch Mts., L.L.C. v.Pinal County, 2002 Ariz. LEXIS 148 (Ariz., Sept. 10, 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PINAL COUNTY. Cause Nos. CV 2001-00818 and CV 2001-00610. Honorable William J. O'Neil, Judge.



DISPOSITION: TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT WAS VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, appellants, a ranch and a land investment company, appealed rulings of the Pinal County Superior Court, Arizona, denying their requests for declaratory and injunctive relief against placing two referenda, both initiated by appellee proponent, on the November 2002 general election ballot.


OVERVIEW: The issue the instant court addressed was when, for purposes of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 19-142, did the 30-day time period commence for filing a referendum petition challenging a county rezoning ordinance: (1) when the ordinance was enacted and executed by a county board of supervisors; or (2) only later, when the county's elections director obtained the ordinance and provided it to the proponent. Appellants argued that the referendum petitions had not been timely filed, while the proponent contended otherwise. The instant court held that the referendum petitions were untimely filed were void. It found untenable the proponent's argument that a duly enacted and executed county ordinance was not available for purposes of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 19-142(C), (D), unless and until the county elections director obtained a copy of the ordinance and provided it to the proponent. The ordinances were legally available upon their enactment. The proponent's reliance on inaccurate advice from the county elections director did not extend the time period for filing the petitions or otherwise excuse noncompliance with the statutory requirements.


OUTCOME: The trial court's rulings in both cases were vacated. Because the proponent's referendum petitions in both cases were untimely filed and were void, the instant court directed entry of judgment in favor of appellants on their complaints. The instant court denied the investment company's request for an award of attorney's fees in both the trial court and on appeal pursuant to the private attorney general doctrine.

McNutt v. McNutt


1 CA-CV 01-0255


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


203 Ariz. 28; 49 P.3d 300; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 100; 376 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 22



June 27, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Yavapai County. Cause No. DO 99-0610. The Honorable William T. Kiger, Judge.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father appealed the order of the Superior Court in Yavapai County (Arizona) that he pay appellee mother $ 484 per month in child support. He also appealed the court's failure to allocate the federal tax exemption for the parties' minor child. In calculating the father's gross income for child support purposes, the court imputed additional income to the father based on his previous 80-hour workweek.


OVERVIEW: The trial court did not articulate any reasons for attributing 16 additional hours to the father's weekly schedule. Interpreting the applicable sections of the Arizona Child Support Guidelines, Appendix to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 25-320 (1996), the appellate court concluded that the phrase "full-time employment" could have encompassed more than 40 hours per week, if part of a regular schedule. The appellate court further concluded, however, that, because the father was not working below "full earning capacity" at the time of trial, the trial court erred by attributing additional income to him based on the 80-hour workweek he once worked. The trial court also erred by failing to allocate the tax exemption. However, the appellate court refused to construe Guideline 4(a) as imposing an hourly limitation of 40 hours per week on the amount of earned income generated from full-time hourly employment, because that construction would have fostered a situation in which children of parents with comparable gross incomes would have received inconsistent child support awards depending on the parent's type of employment rather than ability to pay, a result unfair to children and parents.


OUTCOME: The trial court's child support order was vacated, and the case was remanded for proceedings consistent with the appellate opinion.

Webb v. State ex rel. Ariz. Bd. of Med. Exam'rs


1 CA-CV 01-0010


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


202 Ariz. 555; 48 P.3d 505; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 102; 376 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 11



June 25, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 3, 2002. Amended By Order Filed 8-15-02.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 96-15905. The Honorable Donald F. Daughton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, the Arizona Board of Medical Examiners, after investigating a patient's complaint against appellant physician, publicly censured the physician after an interview. The physician requested rehearing, which the board denied. The Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) dismissed the physician's complaint, but the court of appeals reversed. On remand, the superior court affirmed, and the physician appealed.


OVERVIEW: The physician was certified to perform both general and thoracic surgery. A patient filed a complaint with the board, the gist of which was that the physician had failed to take proper diagnostic measures when treating her for a condition that the a clinic three months later diagnosed as cancer. She also alleged that the physician's office had refused to provide her copies of her medical records. The board scheduled an interview with the physician, who appeared without counsel. The board then censured the physician, who appealed the decision. The decision was ultimately remanded. Upon remand, the physician once again challenged the decision to censure him. The court of appeals held that the board failed to provide due process of law, and the physician was entitled to a new hearing that satisfied the requirements of due process. Upon remand, if the board undertook to establish that the physician's conduct was negligent, and thus unprofessional under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 32-1401(25)(11), it must establish a deviation from an articulated standard of professional care, establish that the deviation resulted in actual harm, and provide reviewable findings on both points.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, the board's decision was set aside, and the case was remanded. The physician's request for attorney fees on appeal was granted.

 

524 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Siddle


2 CA-CR 2000-0253


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


202 Ariz. 512; 47 P.3d 1150; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 95; 376 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 35



June 18, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED October 31, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-63967. Honorable Michael J. Cruikshank, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of unlawful possession of a dangerous drug for sale, unlawful possession of equipment or chemicals for the purpose of manufacturing a dangerous drug, possession of drug paraphernalia, and possession of a deadly weapon during the commission of a felony. The Superior Court Of Pima County (Arizona) sentenced him to concurrent terms for the drug offenses and a consecutive term for weapon charge. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that: (1) the trial court improperly permitted a witness to refer to the fact that he had invoked his Fifth Amendment right to remain silent; and (2) his convictions for both the drug offenses and for possession of a deadly weapon during a felony drug offense violated federal and state double jeopardy principles and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-116. The appellate court held that because the officer here did not state or imply that defendant had invoked his right to remain silent, the trial court did not commit error, much less fundamental error. Because defendant's convictions occurred in a single trial, the appellate court was only concerned with the prohibition against multiple punishments for the same offense. With the exception of possession of drug paraphernalia, the drug offenses were greater offenses than the weapons offense by reason of felony classification. As a result, the weapons offense was not a lesser-included offense as defendant claimed and there was no violation of double jeopardy principles. The statutory provisions were not composed of the same elements, and were not the same offense. The consecutive sentences were permissible under § 13-116.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were affirmed.

May v. McNally


1 CA-SA 02-0073


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


203 Ariz. 13; 49 P.3d 285; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 93; 376 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 31



June 17, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Corrected by, 06/19/2002
Stay granted by, Sub nomine at May v. Weisberg, 2002 Ariz. LEXIS 103 (Ariz., July 3, 2002)
Later proceeding at May v. Weisberg, 2002 Ariz. LEXIS 105 (Ariz., July 9, 2002)
Later proceeding at May v. McNally, 2002 Ariz. LEXIS 106 (Ariz., July 9, 2002)
Vacated by May v. McNally, 203 Ariz. 425, 55 P.3d 768, 2002 Ariz. LEXIS 177 (Ariz., 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Special Action from the Maricopa County Superior Court. Cause No. CV 2001-006078. The Honorable Colleen A. McNally, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought special action review of the decision of the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona) that upheld a provision of the Citizens Clean Elections Act (Act), which permitted certain fine surcharges to be distributed to political candidates, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 16-954(C) (Supp. 2001). Petitioner received a parking ticket and was fined $ 27, which included a 10 percent surcharge pursuant to the Act.


OVERVIEW: The Act established a system of campaign finance whereby certain candidates could receive campaign funds in exchange for agreeing to limit campaign contributions and expenditures. The appellate court held that, based on the Supreme Court holdings of Buckley, Abood, Keller, and United Foods, § 16-954(C), the authorization of a surcharge on civil and criminal fines to finance state elections, imposed an unconstitutional restraint on the exercise of free speech. In the case at bar there was no compelling interest to promote speech when the individuals paying the surcharge and the political speech they funded had no connection. The appellate court found the surcharge was more akin to a regulatory fee than to a general tax because it was imposed upon a specific group of individuals, placed in a special fund, and geared toward a specific purpose: political campaigns. The participating politicians directly benefit from the funds. The surcharge created an involuntary association of those forced to pay the surcharges, and the speech that was being supported was not germane to the purpose of the association. The secretary of state and treasurer were enjoined from enforcing § 16-954(C).


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision was reversed.

S. Pac. Transp. Co. v. Dep't of Revenue


1 CA-TX 00-0024


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T


202 Ariz. 326; 44 P.3d 1006; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 57; 372 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 25



April 25, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 14, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Arizona Tax Court. Cause No. TX 98-00774 (Consolidated). The Honorable Jeffrey S. Cates, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff railroad sued Arizona Department of Revenue (ADOR) in the Arizona Tax Court to contest assessments of delinquent transaction privilege taxes imposed on its gross earnings for transporting copper concentrate from the town of Clifton to other points in Arizona over a railroad route that exited and then re-entered Arizona's boundaries. The tax court entered summary judgment in favor of ADOR. The railroad appealed and ADOR cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The railroad argued that U.S. Const. art, 1, § 8, cl. 3 (the Commerce Clause), required apportionment of state and local business privilege taxes on gross receipts from transportation services between points in Arizona when approximately 20 percent of the route was located in a neighboring state, New Mexico. ADOR argued in its cross-appeal that its assessment properly encompassed the railroad's entire gross receipts from transportation services between Clifton and smelters in Arizona, and that the tax court erred by holding otherwise. ADOR contended that non-apportionment of taxes on these gross receipts did not unduly burden interstate commerce and that the railroad failed to establish that any portion of those receipts was subject to multiple taxation. The appellate court held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-5062(A) could not constitutionally be applied to tax the railroad's gross receipts from shipping goods from Clifton to other points in Arizona via connections in Lordsburg, New Mexico. Neither Arizona statutory law nor Arizona case law provided authorization for allocating gross receipts from the transportation business between services performed within and without Arizona.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed and remanded with directions to enter judgment for the railroad. The appellate court granted the railroad's request for an award of attorneys' fees and costs.

State v. Tousignant


1 CA-CR 01-0418


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


202 Ariz. 270; 43 P.3d 218; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 50; 371 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



April 9, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied on December 3, 2002 by Arizona Supreme Court CR 02-0188PR. Released for Publication January 13, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 2000-000088. The Honorable James E. Padish, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant had pled guilty to solicitation to possess narcotics, the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Arizona, placed defendant on mandatory probation pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-901.01. The State then filed a petition to revoke defendant's probation, alleging probation violations. Defendant informed the trial court that he wished to reject probation, which the trial court allowed him to do. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: As a condition of probation, defendant was to serve a 60-day jail term, to be determined later. When the trial court accepted defendant's rejection of probation after he was found to be in violation, the State argued that the trial court should at least impose the 60-day jail term. The trial court disagreed, terminated defendant's probation unsuccessfully, and released defendant from custody. At issue on appeal was whether a defendant, who had violated his probation under Proposition 200, 1997 Ariz. Sess. Laws 2897, could then choose to reject any further probation. The appellate court held, in accordance with Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-901.01(E) (2001), that such a defendant could not reject probation, and the trial court was required to continue the defendant on probation and impose appropriate additional conditions. The trial court erred by accepting defendant's rejection of probation and by terminating his probation as unsuccessful.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated the order terminating defendant's probation, and remanded the matter to the trial court to reinstate probation.

Flood Control Dist. v. Gaines


1 CA-SA 01-0186


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


202 Ariz. 248; 43 P.3d 196; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 47; 370 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 37



April 2, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied September 24, 2002. Released for Publication October 16, 2002.
Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by Flood Control Dist. v. Paloma Inv. Ltd. P'ship, 230 Ariz. 29, 279 P.3d 1191, 2012 Ariz. App. LEXIS 87 (Ariz. Ct. App., 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Special Action From the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 97-07081. The Honorable F. Pendleton Gaines, Judge.
A Tumbling-T Ranches v. Paloma Inv. Ltd. Pshp., 197 Ariz. 545, 5 P.3d 259, 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 65 (Ariz. Ct. App., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded..


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner flood control district (FCD) sought special action relief from the denial by the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) of its motion for summary judgment on a counterclaim filed by real parties in interest (RPIs). The controlling issue was whether the period within which an inverse condemnation action must be commenced after accrual was the one-year period for actions against public entities, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-821 (1994).


OVERVIEW: Relying on § 12-821, FCD contended that the RPIs' counterclaim was time-barred, as it was not brought within one year of accrual. The counterclaim was filed December 31, 1998. If the one-year limitations period of § 12-821 applied to inverse condemnation actions, then the counterclaim was time-barred, if it accrued before December 31, 1997. RPIs contended that the applicable limitations period was the 10-year period for commencing an action to recover lands in the possession of another. Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-526(A). According to the RPIs, the 10-year period was mandated by the Arizona Supreme Court's decision in Water District. The appellate court concluded that the RPIs' reliance on Water District was misplaced and that § 12-821's one-year limitations period was reasonable, as it regulated, rather than abrogated, the time within which an action had to be filed against a public entity. Section 12-281 (in its present form) was relatively new, and the issue presented was one of first impression. Section 12-821, which barred all actions against the state or its political subdivisions not brought within one year of when the cause of action accrued, superceded Water District.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order denying summary judgment motion was reversed, and the case was remanded.

State v. Crowley


2 CA-CR 01-0162


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


202 Ariz. 80; 41 P.3d 618; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 22



February 22, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected March 1, 2002. Petition for Review Denied September 24, 2002. Petition for Review Denied by Order of the Arizona Supreme Court October 23, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-20002681. Honorable Michael J. Cruikshank, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee was charged with possession of a narcotic drug for sale, possession of marijuana, and possession of drug paraphernalia. Based on State v. Berge, 130 Ariz. 135, 634 P.2d 947 (1981), the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) granted appellee's motion to suppress evidence seized from his home, finding invalid the warrant that authorized the search. The state dismissed the case and appealed pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4032.


OVERVIEW: U.S. Customs "sniffer" dogs alerted to a package from Amsterdam that was addressed to appellee. The package contained a little over two pounds of hashish. Other than the package, the officers had no information suggesting that appellee unlawfully possessed drugs or was involved in drug-related activities. The package was delivered several days after a warrant was issued. The warrant was executed, and in searching the residence, officers found paraphernalia for growing marijuana, hallucinogenic mushrooms, and a pound of marijuana. They also found the unopened package of hashish. Challenging the trial court's order granting appellee's motion to suppress, the state contended that, inter alia, Berge was no longer good law in light of the Supreme Court's decision in Illinois v. Gates, 462 U.S. 213 (1983), and case law from other jurisdictions, both federal and state, decided since Gates. The appellate court conceded that some of the cases were persuasive. But the state's supreme court reached a different result in Berge. Having concluded that Berge remained good law in Arizona notwithstanding Gates, the appellate court was compelled to follow it.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order granting the motion to suppress the evidence seized was affirmed.

 

531 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Romley v. Arpaio


1 CA-CV 01-0013


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


202 Ariz. 47; 40 P.3d 831; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 21; 367 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 19



February 19, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 00-000220. The Honorable Arthur T. Anderson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sheriff directed an administrative employee, an attorney, to represent the sheriff in proceedings before the employee merit system commission. Plaintiff county filed a complaint claiming that the sheriff had no authority to hire in-house counsel to perform duties that the county attorney was legally charged to perform. The Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) granted summary judgment to the county. The sheriff appealed.


OVERVIEW: A terminated employee appealed his termination to the commission and, because he intended to call the county attorney as a witness, the county attorney had a conflict of interest in representing the sheriff before the commission in this matter. Instead of using an attorney obtained by the county attorney, the sheriff directed an administrative employee, who was also a licensed attorney, to represent him in the appeal. The sheriff contended that the county board of supervisors (Board) possessed the authority to employ counsel in that manner and delegated it to him by ratifying a merit system rule, which he claimed permitted an agency to choose its own counsel in appeals to the commission. The appellate court held that the rule allowed only employees who brought a claim before the commission to represent themselves or secure lay or legal representation in appeals. Absent authorization by the board, county officials had to use counsel obtained by the county attorney to represent their interests in commission appeals. Neither the board nor the county attorney authorized the sheriff to use the administrative employee as counsel before the commission in the appeal.


OUTCOME: The trial court's entry of summary judgment was affirmed.

Blake v. Schwartz


1 CA-SA 01-0168


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


202 Ariz. 120; 42 P.3d 6; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 12; 366 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 10; 367 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 23



February 5, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 11, 2002. As Corrected February 21, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Special Action from the Maricopa County Superior Court. Cause No. CR 99-006023. The Honorable Jonathan H. Schwartz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was found guilty except insane (GEI) of murder, attempted murder, kidnapping, and arson of an occupied structure. The Maricopa County Superior Court, Arizona, committed her to the jurisdiction of the psychiatric security review board (PSRB) pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3994 (2001). Petitioner sought review, arguing that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The issues on appeal were whether Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3994(A), (F), and (G) (2001) required a mandatory 120-day period of confinement, and if so, whether a 120-day confinement period was constitutional. The appellate court held the statute was constitutional, but did not reach the issue of whether an initial 120-day confinement, without the prospect of release, for a GEI defendant guilty of a crime involving death or serious physical injury, would or would not be constitutional. Petitioner claimed that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3994 violated her due process rights because it did not allow her or anyone else to seek a release hearing on her behalf prior to the expiration of the initial 120-day confinement period. The State contended that although the legislature chose to prohibit the defendant from requesting a release hearing within the first 120 days, it did not intend to limit the medical director's ability to request a hearing. The appellate court concluded that the statute allowed the medical director to request a release hearing within the 120-day period referenced and did not preclude the medical director from requesting a release hearing at any time.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Mara M. v. Ariz. Dep't of Econ. Sec.


1 CA-JV 01-0059


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


201 Ariz. 503; 38 P.3d 41; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 4; 365 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 35



January 22, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 27, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. JD 6366. The Honorable George H. Foster, Jr., Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother appealed the severance of her parental rights by the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona). She claimed that service upon her attorney of the motion to terminate those rights violated her constitutional right to due process for having service made upon her directly or by publication.


OVERVIEW: The mother had a history of mental health problems and drug abuse, and she had been hospitalized for these problems. She was jailed numerous times for prostitution. The mother could only be contacted by child protective services (CPS) when she was in jail, as she frequently disappeared for months on end and could not even be contacted by her attorney. The mother had been warned by CPS that she was in danger of losing her parental rights. The appellate court held that realistically, service of process on counsel in a case such as the one at bar may not have in fact apprised a parent such as the mother of the pendency of termination proceedings, but, nonetheless, it was a means reasonably calculated under the circumstances to notify the parent and to protect her rights, as opposed to attempted service on a person who disappeared or service by publication. The court did not find the application of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-863 and Ariz. R. Civ. P. 5(c)(1) to be unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The order terminating parental rights was affirmed.

State v. McMahon


1 CA-CR 01-0333


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


201 Ariz. 548; 38 P.3d 1213; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 5; 365 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 8



January 22, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied May 21, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. LC 2000-000498. The Honorable Steven D. Sheldon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant with exhibition of speed in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-708(A). Defendant was found guilty and fined $ 200 plus applicable surcharges. The Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) affirmed the guilty verdict, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: An officer observed a vehicle driven by defendant squeal its tires and fishtail into the median lane, as it turned right from a stop sign. Defendant argued that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-708(A) was unconstitutionally vague, in that the portion prohibiting an exhibition of speed or acceleration, failed to provide any clarification as to whether it encompassed both intentional and unintentional conduct. The court ruled that the specific intent required by the offense could be shown through direct or circumstantial evidence. The offense of exhibition of speed went beyond the mere speed that a person was traveling; it also prohibited the quick acceleration of a vehicle for the purpose of drawing public attention to the swiftness of one's vehicle. There was no constitutional infirmity with respect to the portion of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-708(A) criminalizing an exhibition of speed or acceleration on a street or highway.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

535 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cox


1 CA-CR 00-0812


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


201 Ariz. 464; 37 P.3d 437; 2002 Ariz. App. LEXIS 1; 364 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



January 10, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 99-012934. The Honorable Steven D. Sheldon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; VACATED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences in the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) for kidnapping with intent to promote, further, or assist criminal conduct by a criminal street gang, a class two felony, and aggravated assault with intent to promote, further, or assist criminal conduct by a criminal street gang, a class six felony.


OVERVIEW: The trial court did not err in not permitting defendant to cross-examine the victim regarding the specific nature of the victim's prior felony conviction. Evidence that the witness had been convicted of a felony was to be admitted if the court determined that the probative value of admitting the evidence outweighed its prejudicial effect. That the court did not admit evidence of the nature of the prior conviction did not damage defendant's ability to argue that the victim was not credible. The trial court's instruction on criminal street gangs said "any criminal act" when it should have said "any felony act." This error was harmless. No reasonable possibility existed that the jury based its criminal street gang decision on crimes other than felonies. The trial court clearly erred when it found the Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604.02(B) allegation proved, for the record reflected no evidence to support the allegation. The error was not harmless. A jury trial was not required on the Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604.02(B) allegation.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the convictions, vacated the sentences, and remanded for resentencing.

State v. Cecil


1 CA-CR 01-0054


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A

December 24, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied and ordered not published by, Remanded by State v. Cecil, 205 Ariz. 70, 66 P.3d 1247, 2003 Ariz. LEXIS 47 (Ariz., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR2000-005898. The Honorable Frank T. Galati, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant challenged the judgment of the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona), which convicted the defendant for first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the defendant argued that the definition of "premeditation," as given to the jury, and found in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1101(1) (2000), was unconstitutionally vague, as it failed to adequately distinguish first-degree murder from second-degree murder and thus allowed for arbitrary and discriminatory application of the statute. The appellate court found that the statute, as applied to the defendant, resulted in harmless error and affirmed. In a prior case, the court determined that the statute, while constitutional on its face, was unconstitutionally vague because of the judicial construction of the statute by the Arizona Supreme Court to the effect that premeditation could be "as instantaneous as successive thoughts of the mind." The court found however that the offending "instantaneous" language was not introduced into the case in any way, and the defendant was convicted solely using the constitutional portion of the statute. Therefore, the defendant was not prejudiced by the application of a vague statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Navarro

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) of attempted second-degree murder and two counts of aggravated assault. The trial court sentenced him to concurrent, presumptive prison terms. Defendant challenged the denial of his suppression motion and the sentence imposed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erroneously denied his motion to suppress photographs taken at the police station, and all evidence derived therefrom. He also argued that Ariz. Rev. State v. Carrasco


2 CA-CR 00-0337

October 30, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 5, 2002. Petition for Review was filed and DENIED by Order of the Arizona Supreme Court July 5, 2002. Petition for Review to Supreme Court of Arizona Denied May 23, 2002. Writ of certiorari denied: Carrasco v. Arizona, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 8115 (U.S. Nov. 4, 2002).
Writ of certiorari denied Carrasco v. Arizona, 537 U.S. 1002, 123 S. Ct. 487, 154 L. Ed. 2d 398, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 8115 (2002)
Appeal after remand at State v. Carrasco, 2003 Ariz. App. Unpub. LEXIS 462 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-64234. Honorable Richard Nichols, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee attorney was found guilty of obstructing a criminal investigation or prosecution in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2409. After the jury found him guilty of the charge but before he was sentenced, he renewed his motion for judgment of acquittal that he had filed prior to the close of trial. The Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) granted the motion. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The attorney represented his cousin in a child molestation case. The attorney called the shelter where one of the children was staying and misrepresented that he was the child's lawyer and was allowed to speak to her. He told her not to talk to the police. The state contended that the trial court erroneously held that § 13-2409 required proof that the misrepresentation was made directly to the child victim. Attorney argued that he did not make any misrepresentations to the victim because his statement to her that she was not required to talk to police was entirely accurate. The attorney did misrepresent his role in the investigation to the shelter worker in order to gain access to the victim. The appellate court held that the trial court construed § 13-2409 too narrowly, it did encompass the attorney's conduct which was a misrepresentation to a minor child's caregiver, rather than to a child victim or witness directly, for the purpose of obstructing, delaying, or preventing the victim or witness from communicating relevant information concerning an alleged crime to a peace officer.


OUTCOME: The grant of the motion for judgment of acquittal was reversed and the case was remanded.

 

539 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nichols


2 CA-SA 01-0062


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


201 Ariz. 234; 33 P.3d 1172; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 161; 359 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 25



October 30, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Pima County Cause No. CR-68059.



DISPOSITION: Relief was granted and order was vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by indictment with possessing a dangerous drug for sale and possessing marijuana for sale. Defendant requested a bifurcated trial. Petitioner, State, filed an allegation of serious drug offense (significant source of income) pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3410(A). The respondent judge found § 13-3410(A) unconstitutional and dismissed the allegation. The State challenged that ruling in a special action.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that based on the transcript of the hearing below and the ultimate dismissal of the allegation, it appeared likely that the respondent judge found § 13-3410(A) unconstitutional based on the grand jury issue raised in defendant's motion; that the state could pursue the serious drug offense allegation only by way of a grand jury indictment and not merely by filing an allegation, as the state had done. That motion was based strictly on a purported similarity between § 13-3410(A) and the federal crime of continuing criminal enterprise (CCE), 21 U.S.C.S. § 848. An indictment or information could not be brought against an accused under § 13-3410 unless that person had already been convicted of "a serious drug offense." The court found no constitutional infirmity in the legislature's enactment of § 13-10 to define not a substantive offense but, rather, an enhanced penalty for conviction of serious drug offenses when additional facts were proven. Those facts need not be alleged in the charging document provided that the notice of them given the defendant comported with Arizona's traditional notice requirements for alleging sentence enhancements.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court was vacated.

State v. Evenson


1 CA-CR 00-0621


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


201 Ariz. 209; 33 P.3d 780; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 158; 29 Media L. Rep. 2601; 359 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 12



October 30, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review or Rehearing granted: State v. Evenson, 2002 Ariz. LEXIS 56 (Ariz. Apr. 23, 2002). Released for Publication January 7, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 97-09901. The Honorable Frank T. Galati, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted and sentenced by the Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, on 13 counts of displaying, selling, or offering to sell from a vending machine material that was harmful to minors, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3513 (Supp. 1997). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The primary issue on appeal was whether Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3513 (Supp. 1997) was an unconstitutional restriction on freedom of speech. The court of appeals held that: (1) the State adequately showed a compelling state interest by proving there was a real risk of children being exposed to defendant's adult-oriented magazine, which consisted of sexually oriented advertisements for adult bookstores and "escort" and "model" services; (2) § 13-3513 was the least restrictive means that was equally effective in keeping harmful materials sold from vending machines out of the reach of children, yet keeping such materials reasonably accessible to adults; and (3) it rejected defendant's equal protection and due process arguments as meritless.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed.

Taylor v. Graham County Chamber of Commerce


2 CA-CV 01-0032


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


201 Ariz. 184; 33 P.3d 518; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 155; 17 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1807; 358 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 20



October 18, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for Review DENIED March 21, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF GRAHAM COUNTY. Cause No. CV990086. Honorable Monica Stauffer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee brought a wrongful termination action under the Employment Protection Act (EPA), Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1501 et seq., and the Arizona Civil Rights Act (ACRA), Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-1401 et seq. The Superior Court of Graham County (Arizona) entered summary judgment in defendant employer's favor. Employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee brought a tort claim for discriminatory treatment and wrongful termination, in violation of the public policy expressed in ACRA's anti-discrimination provision, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-1463(B)(1). However, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1501(3)(b) neither authorized nor supported the employee's wrongful termination claim. The employer was not subject to and, therefore, did not violate ACRA. The EPA barred employee's wrongful termination claim based on the public policy of the ACRA. The employee failed to overcome the presumption that she had at-will employment status. The policy manual did not satisfy the statutory prerequisites for maintaining a viable action for breach of contract under the EPA. The manual clearly confirmed the at-will status of all employees. The employee failed to establish the requirements under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1501(2); thus her contract claim failed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Seyrafi


1 CA-CR 00-0828


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


201 Ariz. 147; 32 P.3d 430; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 154; 358 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



October 16, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 30, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. LC-98-001052. The Honorable Michael O. Wilkinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of nine misdemeanor violations of various property maintenance provisions under Scottsdale, Ariz., Rev. Code ch. 18. The Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) affirmed the convictions, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Scottsdale, Ariz., Rev. Code § 18-11 was unconstitutional because it contained a mandatory presumption that shifted the burden of proof from the State to the defense. The pertinent language in Scottsdale, Ariz., Rev. Code § 18-11(b) was mandatory because the ordinance's provision left no room for rebuttals or inferences in favor of a property owner's innocence. It relieved the prosecution of the burden of proving an element of the offense: that the owner of record was also the person in control of the property and therefore liable for the violations. The ordinance created a mandatory evidentiary presumption that impermissibly removed the burden of proof from the State in violation of due process. The ordinance was therefore facially invalid and unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were reversed and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

McGovern v. McGovern


2 CA-CV 01-0016


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


201 Ariz. 172; 33 P.3d 506; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 152; 358 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 11



October 11, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 4, 2002. Petition for Review was filed and DENIED by order of the Arizona Supreme Court April 4, 2002. Writ of certiorari denied: McGovern v. McGovern, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 4946 (U.S. June 28, 2002).


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. D-125189. Honorable Karen S. Adam, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; VACATED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grandparents filed a motion for visitation pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 25-409. Upon reconsideration, the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) vacated its earlier order granting visitation and left visitation to the sole discretion of appellee mother. The grandparents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The grandparents filed an action under § 25-409 to obtain court-ordered visitation with their granddaughter. The mother opposed the petition. Upon reconsideration, the trial court concluded that it had unconstitutionally applied § 25-409 in a manner that violated the mother's fundamental right to parent her child without state interference. However, the trial court's ultimate ruling that the issue of grandparent visitation was left in the discretion of the mother was vacated. The court was unable to conclude as a matter of law that the grandparents did not carry their burden of rebutting the presumption of parental primacy or could not do so if given the opportunity.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was affirmed except for the aspect that left the issue of visitation solely in the mother's discretion. That portion of the order was vacated and remanded for an evidentiary hearing to determine whether to grant grandparent visitation and, if so, its extent or frequency.

State v. Boyd


1 CA-CR 00-0761


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


201 Ariz. 27; 31 P.3d 140; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 141; 357 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 5



September 25, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 2000-005447. The Honorable Robert L. Gottsfield, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted for driving with a suspended license while having a dangerous drug or its metabolite in his body, under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1381(A)(3), in the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona). The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1381(A)(3) violated due process because, although it incorporated Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3401, which defined "dangerous drug" to include gamma hydroxybutyrate (GHB), it nonetheless failed to give him notice that his action, i.e., ingesting gamma butyrolactone (GBL) was illegal. The defendant ingested GBL, a legal product, purchased in fact from a health-food store, without knowledge or notice that it would be converted in his body to its proscribed metabolite GHB. The court on appeal held that there was nothing facially vague about Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1381(A)(3) but when applied to these facts it was void for vagueness. The defendant could not be held strictly liable for violating § 28-1381(A)(3) when, through a bodily process unknown to a person of average intelligence and common experience, that substance would be transformed into a prohibited substance. The fact that a violation of § 28-1381(A)(3) was a strict liability offense also influenced the court's determination that the statute failed to give defendant adequate notice such as to fulfill the requirements of due process.


OUTCOME: The conviction was reversed.

City of Tempe v. Outdoor Sys., Inc.


1 CA-CV 00-0242


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


201 Ariz. 106; 32 P.3d 31; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 142; 357 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 15



September 25, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 98-91511. The Honorable Robert H. Oberbillig, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; VACATED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city claimed the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) erred in granting summary judgment in favor of defendant corporation, a billboard owner, after concluding that Tempe, Ariz., Ordinance 808 was unconstitutional. The city also challenged the award of attorney and expert witness fees.


OVERVIEW: Defendants' billboard was a non-conforming sign under Tempe, Ariz., Ordinance 808. The city filed a declaratory action contending that repairs made to the billboard exceeded the permissible scope of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 9-462.02 and the ordinance. The ordinance's blanket prohibition against making any alterations to non-conforming signs could not be interpreted in harmony with the opposite mandate of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 9-462.02(A). Because the statute controlled over the ordinance, the conflicting language of the ordinance was invalid. The repairs fell within the permissible parameters of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 9-462.02 and the modified ordinance. The award of attorney fees pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988(b) was vacated, as that claim was not decided by the trial court. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by awarding expert witness fees.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment entered in favor of the defendants was affirmed. The award of attorney fees pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 was vacated, as was the trial court's finding that the ordinance was unconstitutional. That part of the ordinance prohibiting alterations was severed.

Kurti v. Maricopa County


1 CA-CV 01-0055


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


201 Ariz. 165; 33 P.3d 499; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 137; 113 A.L.R.5th 653; 356 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 37



September 20, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED April 26, 2002.
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by, Sub nomine at Avila v. Biedess, 78 P.3d 280, 2003 Ariz. App. LEXIS 173 (Ariz. Ct. App., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 2000-092802. The Honorable Robert D. Myers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff legal aliens sought review of a Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona) declaratory judgment in favor of defendant public health care officials. The aliens challenged as violative of equal protection guarantees certain limitations on health care availability contained in Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 36-2903.03, 11-297(B), 11-291(A) (Supp. 2000).


OVERVIEW: After the United State Congress enacted 8 U.S.C.S. § 1613(a), which placed limitations on availability of certain means-tested benefits to legal aliens for a five-year period after entry, Arizona's legislature enacted Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 36-2903.03(D), 11-297(B), and 11-291(A) (Supp. 2000), which limited such aliens' access to health care services, except for emergency services, forever. An alien couple challenged the statutes as violative of equal protection. The appeals court held that the statutes were subject to strict scrutiny, because the absence of a five-year moratorium made them more restrictive than federal laws. Looked at from that perspective, the State failed to show a compelling interest in the disparate treatment of legal aliens, so the statutes were unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded for determination of an appropriate attorneys' fee award.

 

548 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gross


1 CA-CR 00-0269


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


201 Ariz. 41; 31 P.3d 815; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 129; 355 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



September 4, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on January 8, 2002 by Arizona Supreme Court CR 01-0384-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 99-010161. The Honorable Thomas Dunevant, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE ENHANCEMENT VACATED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) convicted the defendant of two counts of forgery. The trial court sentenced the defendant to concurrent mitigated terms of three and one-half years in prison, then added two years on each count as required by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604(R), for a total of five and one-half years in prison. The defendant appealed the sentences imposed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the sentences imposed violated the Apprendi doctrine. Under Apprendi, it was unconstitutional for a legislature to remove from the jury the assessment of facts that increased the prescribed range of penalties to which a criminal defendant was exposed. Other than the fact of a prior conviction, any fact that increased the penalty for a crime beyond the prescribed statutory maximum was required to be submitted to a jury, and proved beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court held that absent waiver, the State had to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that the defendant was on pretrial release and a jury had to so determine before a sentence could be enhanced pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604(R) (2001). The additional finding by the trial court that the defendant was on release status exposed the defendant to a maximum sentence on each count which exceeded the statutory maximum for the offense. Therefore, the plain language in Apprendi required that the defendant's release status be submitted to the jury and proved beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court held the proper remedy was a remand for a new trial on the enhancement issue.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence enhancements were vacated. Because the State was not at fault for the need for a retrial, the case was remand for a new trial on the sentence enhancement issue.

 

549 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Andrews v. Willrich


1 CA-SA 01-0072, 1 CA-SA 01-0109, (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


200 Ariz. 533; 29 P.3d 880; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 117; 354 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 17



August 16, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on January 8, 2002 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-01-0334-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: MARICOPA COUNTY Superior Court. Nos. CR2000-094237 and CR2001-090825. Petitions for Special Action from the Maricopa County. Superior Court Cause No. CR 2000-094237. The Honorable Penny L. Willrich, Judge. Cause No. CR 2001-090825. The Honorable Robert Oberbillig, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated actions arising in the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona), petitioner juveniles argued that Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 8-302(B), 13-501(B) (Supp. 2000), which vested authority in the prosecutor to determine whether they would be tried as adults, were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The legislature enacted Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 8-302(B) (1999), 13-501(B) (Supp. 2000), which vested exclusive authority in the prosecutor to determine whether juveniles in specified circumstances would be tried as adults. Two juveniles argued that these statutes violated the separation of powers doctrine. The legislature did not exceed its constitutional authority by empowering the executive branch to select which sentencing scheme the court could use to punish a juvenile offender. The prosecutor's decision did not curtail the exercise of a court's discretion in choosing an appropriate punishment from among the legislatively authorized options. The legislature has not relinquished its power to decide the range of punishment available to the court. These statutes did not violate the separation of powers doctrine, or did they deprive petitioners of their due process rights.


OUTCOME: The challenged statutes were constitutional and petitioners' request for relief was denied.

 

550 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


In re Alex M.


1 CA-JV 00-0219


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


200 Ariz. 556; 30 P.3d 137; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 118; 354 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 13



August 16, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. JV 145949. The Honorable Janet E. Barton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A petition for revocation of probation was filed. The statute that the juvenile had pled guilty to was declared unconstitutional. The Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, vacated the judgment of delinquency, probation violation, and original plea agreement, and reinstated the charges that were previously dismissed. Upon reconsideration the superior court vacated the reinstatement of the previously dismissed charges. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile originally pled guilty to minor-in-possession of a firearm in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3111 (Supp. 1999-2000). The plea agreement contained a provision that if one of the parties was allowed to get out of the agreement, then the juvenile would again be considered accused of all the charges originally in the petition and any charges that were dismissed under the plea agreement. The appellate court found that the juvenile court erred in its decision of the motion for reconsideration because when the juvenile court granted defendant's motion to vacate his delinquency adjudication, it permitted him to withdraw from an agreement that he had not completely performed, and that triggered the provision in the plea agreement that reinstated all of the charges that were dismissed in the plea agreement.


OUTCOME: The juvenile court's order of reconsideration was reversed. The juvenile court's order vacating the plea agreement and reinstating the two charges that were previously dismissed as part of the plea agreement was reinstated.

 

551 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State Libertarian Party v. Schmeral


1 CA-CV 00-0335


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


200 Ariz. 486; 28 P.3d 948; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 119; 356 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 33



August 16, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Amended By Order Filed September 12, 2001.  [***1] Amended By Order Filed September 20, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 1999-03904. The Honorable Robert D. Myers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The county recorder sued to determine whether appellant conforming political party faction or appellee non-conforming political party faction was entitled to receive voter data. Appellee political parties intervened to challenge the constitutionality of statutes governing the selection of party leadership. The Maricopa County (Arizona) Superior Court entered judgment for the non-conforming faction, and the conforming faction appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the challenged statutes, Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 16-824 to 828 (1996), governing the selection of party leadership, were constitutional, but that the non-conforming faction needed to comply with them only prospectively. The appellate court held that because adherence to the challenged statutes was mandatory, not permissive, it could not avoid deciding whether the statutes were constitutional. The challenged statutes did not restrict the ability of political parties and their members to endorse, support, or vote for particular persons; they did not limit a party's access to the ballot; they did not determine a party's policy; and, while they affected a party's structure for some purposes, they did not regulate a party's internal governance. Therefore, they did not unconstitutionally burden associational rights under the First Amendment and the Due Process Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, but rather served the state's important regulatory interests. However, as the challenged statutes were passed in 1979, the non-conforming faction was aware of the law and the trial court erred in excusing it from complying with those statutes.


OUTCOME: That portion of the judgment upholding the constitutionality of the challenged statutes was affirmed. That portion of the judgment holding that the non-conforming faction needed to comply with the law only prospectively was reversed.

Simat Corp. v. State Health Care Cost Containment Sys.


1 CA-CV 00-0334


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


200 Ariz. 506; 29 P.3d 281; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 113; 353 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 13



August 7, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Plaintiffs-Petitioners' Petition for Review by the Supreme Court GRANTED as to Issue 1, 2, and 3, February 15, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 99-014614. The Honorable Kenneth L. Fields, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The plaintiffs doctors filed a complaint in the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) alleging that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 35-196.02 violated the Arizona Constitution. The superior court granted the doctors's motion for summary judgment and issued a permanent injunction prohibiting the enforcement of the statute. The defendant state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The statute prohibited state funding of abortions unless it was necessary to save the mother's life. The doctors argued that the statute was unconstitutional because it violated: (1) Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 8; (2) Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 13; and (3) Ariz. Const. art. 4, pt. 2, §19. The court of appeals held that the statute was not unconstitutional because: (1) there was nothing to suggest that the framers of the constitution intended the right to privacy under the state constitution to create a right of citizens to subsidized abortions to which they were not entitled under the United States Constitution, even if state citizens had a greater right to privacy under the state constitution; (2) the statute did not discriminate on the basis of sex, nor did the classification impinge upon the exercise of a fundamental right, and the statutory scheme was rationally related to a legitimate government purpose; and (3) eligible individuals were not special or exclusive simply because the state did not provide medically necessary abortions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the injunction was lifted.
