State v. Tschilar


1 CA-CR 00-0495


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


200 Ariz. 427; 27 P.3d 331; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 108; 352 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 4



July 17, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on March 27, 2002 by Arizona Supreme Court CR 01-0320PR. Petition for Review by the Supreme Court GRANTED January 8, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Navajo County. Cause No. CR 99-000165. The Honorable Thomas L. Wing, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted and sentenced for multiple counts of kidnapping and aggravated assault in the Superior Court in Navajo County, Arizona. Defendant appealed his convictions.


OVERVIEW: Among the issues defendant raised on appeal was whether the finding that his kidnapping victims were voluntarily released unharmed, a determination resolving whether the offense was a class 2 or a class 4 felony, was a factual decision for the jury according to the Apprendi rationale. The court of appeals held that: (1) the finding of defendant's kidnapping victims were voluntarily released unharmed was not a factual decision for the jury; (2) the superior court did not err in not finding that the teenagers were safely released for the purpose of reducing the charges of kidnapping from class 2 to class 4 felonies; (3) the consideration of the number of victims was not beyond the discretion of the superior court; (4) there was no abuse of discretion in the superior court's decision that there was insufficient evidence of a citizen's arrest to warrant giving a jury instruction regarding the law of citizen's arrest; and (5) the superior court did not err by not giving a jury instruction on the crime of unlawful imprisonment as a lesser-included offense of kidnapping.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed.

 

554 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Viramontes


2 CA-CR 00-0227


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


200 Ariz. 452; 27 P.3d 809; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 99; 350 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



June 19, 2001, Decided


NOTICE:

 [***1] THIS OPINION WAS VACATED BY THE COURT. 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review = GRANTED as to Issue F March 19, 2002.
Vacated, Remanded: State v. Viramontes, 2003 Ariz. LEXIS 1 (Ariz. Jan. 8, 2003).


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-67216. Honorable Michael Cruikshank, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Pima County Superior Court (Arizona), which convicted defendant of first degree murder and sentenced him to a prison term of natural life.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court erred by failing to apply the special sentencing procedures in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-703 to determine whether to impose natural life or a life sentence with the possibility of release in 25 years, and by considering natural life the presumptive sentence for first degree murder. Defendant also argued that the trial court erred by considering natural life in prison the "presumptive" sentence under § 13-703. The instant court found no reversible error regarding the conviction. However, because the trial court stated that natural life was the "presumptive" sentence for first degree murder, the instant court remanded for further proceedings regarding the sentence. The trial court's oral pronouncement of sentence did not mention the term "presumptive" but it did not negate the possibility that the trial court believed that the natural life term was to be imposed in the vast majority of such cases in the absence of an imbalance between mitigating and aggravating factors. If this were true, the trial court might have exercised its sentencing discretion improperly. Only the trial court could clarify its intent and correct the record if necessary.


OUTCOME: The instant court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence, but it remanded to the trial court for a period of 14 days so that it could clarify the ambiguity created by the use of the term "presumptive" in the sentencing minute entry and, if appropriate, make any necessary corrections, or, if necessary, order that it would resentence defendant without considering the natural life sentence the presumptive sentence.

 

555 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


City of Tucson v. Grezaffi


2 CA-CV 00-0172


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


200 Ariz. 130; 23 P.3d 675; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 201; 347 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 10



May 10, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. C20001372. Honorable Christopher C. Browning, Judge.
City of Tucson v. Grezaffi, 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 76 (Ariz. Ct. App., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant restaurant owner was cited on a civil infraction for having violated Tucson, Ariz., Code § 11-19(E)(2) which, inter alia, prohibited restaurant owners from allowing persons to smoke in restaurants except in a designated smoking area and from allowing smoke to diffuse or drift into a nonsmoking area. A city court ordered her to abate the violation. The Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) denied her appeal. The owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owner challenged the constitutionality of the restaurant smoking ordinance, § 11-19. The appellate court concluded that the ordinance was facially valid. The owner's contention that § 11-19 violated her First Amendment right to freedom of association bordered on frivolous. The owner's equal protection argument also was unavailing. She contended the ordinance constituted class legislation at its worst and unconstitutionally discriminated against her because it selectively applied only to restaurants, while excluding bars and bowling alleys. The owner did not claim to be a member of any suspect class and the law did not recognize any fundamental, constitutionally protected right to smoke in the same area in which one chose to eat. The appellate court had no difficulty concluding that the ordinance was rationally and reasonably related to furthering some legitimate governmental interest. Significant scientific evidence suggested that smoking or exposure to second-hand smoke posed serious and substantial health risks. The ordinance was a reasonable, legitimate means of safeguarding the general health, safety, and welfare of the community.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

556 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


In re Kyle M.


1 CA-JV 00-0179


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


200 Ariz. 447; 27 P.3d 804; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 98; 349 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 28



June 7, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. JV 525525. The Honorable Emmet J. Ronan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile challenged a judgment of the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) adjudicating him delinquent for threatening or intimidating in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1202(A)(1) (Supp. 2000).


OVERVIEW: Appellant alleged that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1202(A)(1) (Supp. 2000) required the State to prove that he acted with "wrongful intent," and that the State had failed to prove such intent. Appellant also alleged that the State failed to prove that he had uttered a "true threat" within the meaning of § 13-1202(A)(1). The appellate court affirmed the delinquency adjudication. Section 13-1202(A)(1) did not require the State to prove that an accused acted with "wrongful intent" by threatening to cause physical injury to another or seriously damage property. However, one violated § 13-1202(A)(1) only by communicating a "true threat." An accused expressed such a threat if, under the circumstances, a reasonable person would have foreseen that his words would have been taken as a serious expression of an intent to inflict bodily harm, and his statements were not the result of mistake, duress, or coercion. Based on the applicable standards, appellant had been proven delinquent under § 13-1202(A)(1).


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment adjudicating appellant juvenile delinquent was affirmed. Appellant violated the criminal statute prohibiting threatening or intimidating by expressing a threat which was objectively understood, under the circumstances, to be a serious expression of an intent to inflict bodily harm.

W. Maricopa Combine, Inc. v. Ariz. Dep't of Water Res.


1 CA-CV 00-0086


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


200 Ariz. 400; 26 P.3d 1171; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 93; 349 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 17



June 5, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied March 19, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 99-08176. The Honorable Barry C. Schneider, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation appealed a judgment of the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona) ruling that appellee private property owners' property rights trumped appellant's right to access to Central Arizona Project (CAP) water via the Hassayampa riverbed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant applied for a managed underground water storage facility permit. Appellee corporation and appellee town objected to the application. The proposed permit would have allowed appellant to move CAP water through six miles of the Hassayampa riverbed; approximately one and one-half miles of that riverbed ran through appellee corporation's property. Appellee corporation claimed that the section of the riverbed running through its property was its private property and could not be disturbed. The instant court held that the consent of streambed owners was not required before appellant could make beneficial use of an existing natural watercourse to move its appropriated water and for water storage purposes pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 45-811.01 (1994 & Supp. 2000). Appellee corporation's title to the land adjacent to the Hassayampa River was taken subject to existing water rights. Appellant's proposed diversion of CAP water was not a taking. The trial court's interpretation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 45-173(A) (1994 & Supp. 2000) and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 45-814.01 (1994) as requiring the consent of adjacent landowners before granting appellant's permit was contrary to law.


OUTCOME: Judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded with directions that the trial court enter summary judgment for appellant. Appellant was awarded its attorney fees and costs.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order of the Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, denying his request for an affirmative injunction requiring the Arizona Secretary of State to accept his late petition to appear on the November 2000 Arizona ballot as an independent candidate for President of the United States.


OVERVIEW: Appellant candidate requested an affirmative injunction requiring the Arizona Secretary of State to accept appellant's late-filed petition to appear on the November 2000 Arizona ballot as an independent candidate for President of the United States. State v. Farley


1 CA-CR 99-0870

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Yavapai County. Cause No. CR 98-0652. The Honorable William T. Kiger, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court in Yavapai County (Arizona) convicting and sentencing him for second-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant contended that Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-205(A) (West Supp. 2000), the affirmative defense statute, violated the Due Process Clause of the Arizona Constitution because it relieved the State of the burden imposed on it by the Due Process Clause to disprove the justification defense beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court rejected appellant's constitutional challenge to § 13-205(A) because appellant failed to demonstrate that the Due Process Clause of the Arizona Constitution, unlike its federal counterpart, prohibited the State from placing the burden of proving the affirmative defense of justification on a criminal defendant. Appellant also argued that the trial court erred in instructing the jury on the use of deadly force in defense of a third person. The appellate court found that a portion of the instruction subtly misstated the standard for the use of deadly physical force by impermissibly suggesting that only actual deadly force, and not apparent deadly force, could justify appellant's use of deadly force. However, the court declined to reverse because appellant invited any error by requesting the instruction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence.

Douglass v. Gendron


1 CA-CV 00-0409


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


199 Ariz. 593; 20 P.3d 1174; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 60; 344 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 20



March 29, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied October 5, 2001. Petition for Review Denied October 3, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Ariz. LEXIS 144.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 99-090527. The Honorable Robert H. Oberbillig, Judge. The Honorable David M. Talamante, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of the order of the Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, dismissing the citation of appellee landowner for violating appellant's regulation regarding the height of grass and weeds on his property.


OVERVIEW: Appellant city cited appellee landowner for violating appellant's regulation regarding the height of grass and weeds on his property. The superior court dismissed the citation. Appellant claimed that the court erred in its interpretation of the phrase "developed parcel" as used in Mesa City, Ariz., Code § 8-6-3(O). The appellate court agreed and reversed the judgment. In classifying a "developed" or "undeveloped" parcel, the appellate court held that § 8-6-3(O) intended that property be classified as a whole. Even though only one-third of the property was listed as a single parcel in the records of the county assessor's office, appellant's residential use of the property rendered the entire parcel a "developed" parcel. Because the ordinance was not vague, the matter was remanded for the entry of judgment for appellant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

562 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Town of Tortolita v. Napolitano


1 CA-CV 00-0437


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


199 Ariz. 556; 20 P.3d 599; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 61; 344 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 21



March 29, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied October 3, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Pima County. Cause Nos. C-322883; C-322969. The Honorable Michael J. Brown, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a proceeding regarding the validity of the incorporation of appellant town, a preliminary injunction was entered prohibiting appellant from exercising governmental authority, including incurring attorneys' fees. Nearly two years later, appellant moved to modify the preliminary injunction to be allowed to incurring attorneys' fees. The Superior Court, Pima County (Arizona) refused to grant the modification, and appellant town appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, appellant maintained that the trial court erred in refusing to modify the preliminary injunction and allow the appellant to obligate itself to pay an attorney. Appellant claimed that due process allowed it to pay an attorney even if its incorporation was found to be invalid. The court rejected appellant's arguments. The court held that no violation of the appellant's alleged due process rights occurred. Appellant's due process argument was not within the scope of a motion to modify a preliminary injunction. It did not stem from new legal or factual issues affecting the continuing propriety of the preliminary injunction but required a reexamination of the bases of the original ruling. Additionally, U.S. Const. amend. XIV applies to persons, not municipalities, and, therefore, the appellant had no Fourteenth Amendment right to assert. The court was satisfied that the appellant was and would continue to be adequately represented. Appellant's attorney provided representation for it in 13 separate lawsuits, and appellant took no action for nearly two years to obtain any relief from the restraint on its acquisition of debt for attorneys' fees.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

563 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


City of Tucson v. Pima County


1 CA-CV 00-0411


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


199 Ariz. 509; 19 P.3d 650; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 55; 343 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 24



March 15, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] ORDERED: Appellants' Motion for Expedited Consideration = DENIED.
FURTHER ORDERED: Motion for Oral Argument on Petition for Review = DENIED.
FURTHER ORDERED: Respondent City of Tucson's Request for Judicial Notice = DENIED.
FURTHER ORDERED: Petition for Review = DENIED April 26, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County. Cause No. 320926. The Honorable Nanette M. Warner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed an order from the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) concluding Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 9- 101.01 (1996) was not unconstitutional in requiring the consent of a proximate municipality before an area may incorporate.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff city refused to consent to allowing defendants to incorporate into new municipal corporations, as provided by state law. Defendants challenged the constitutionality of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 9-101.01(1966), which required plaintiff's consent. The court found the statute was constitutional because it did not violate equal protection, procedural or substantive due process, the right to self-determination or the First Amendment, nor did it have an adverse impact on the right to vote. There was no constitutional right to vote for municipal incorporation. Ariz. Const. art. 13, § 1, gave the legislature plenary power over the methods and procedures for municipal incorporation. The Arizona legislature granted the right to petition and vote for incorporation, but made an election contingent upon the consent of a neighboring municipality. Protecting the interests of existing cities concerning the formation of new political subdivisions, bore a rational relationship to a legitimate state interest.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

565 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Hobson v. Mid-Century Ins. Co.


2 CA-CV 99-0222, 2 CA-CV 00-0118 (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


199 Ariz. 525; 19 P.3d 1241; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 29; 342 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 26



February 27, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied October 9, 2001. Petition for Review Denied October 3, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Ariz. LEXIS 150.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause Nos. 332767 and 336267. Honorable Charles S. Sabalos, Judge, Honorable John F. Kelly, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed the ruling of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1023(C) did not permit an order compelling a workers' compensation lienholder to pay an equitable share of the attorney's fees and costs incurred by a claimant in a third-party tort action. Plaintiffs also appealed the ruling that the statute did not violate the separation of powers doctrine.


OVERVIEW: After two plaintiffs sustained industrial injuries, their employers' workers' compensation carriers, defendant insurers, accepted plaintiffs' claims and paid them benefits. Plaintiffs, through their attorney (plaintiff attorney), then pursued a third-party action, in which they settled. Defendants received payment of their workers' compensation liens. Plaintiffs then made claims against defendants for their share of what defendants received. Defendants refused to pay, and plaintiffs filed declaratory relief actions. The trial courts granted defendants' motions for summary judgment, and plaintiffs appealed. The appellate court agreed with the trial courts that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1023(C) did not permit an order compelling a workers' compensation lienholder to pay, from the amount it was paid on account of its statutorily prescribed lien, an equitable share of the attorney's fees and costs incurred by the plaintiffs in a third-party tort action. Also, that statute did not unconstitutionally violate the separation of powers doctrine by infringing on the trial courts' equitable power.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed. The lower courts did not have the statutory authority to compel defendants to pay plaintiffs an equitable share of attorney's fees and costs incurred by plaintiffs in their third party lawsuit. Further, the statute in question was not unconstitutional.

 

566 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Lawrence v. Jones


1 CA-CV 00-0301


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


199 Ariz. 446; 18 P.3d 1245; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 25; 341 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 16



February 20, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on May 23, 2001 by Arizona Supreme Court CV-01-0105-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 00-007066. The Honorable Susan R. Bolton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a special action, plaintiffs appealed a judgment of the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona), which denied their challenge to a City of Mesa zoning referendum and denied their motion for new trial and to amend the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sought to compel defendant city clerk to disqualify invalid signatures on a referendum attempting to overturn a zoning change on two grounds: first, because the attachment of a zoning map to the petition was insufficient to meet the requirement of a "legal description" of the property pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 19-121(E); and second, because petition signatures obtained by nonresidents of Mesa were invalid pursuant to state and local laws. The instant court agreed with the trial court that the requirement of a legal description was met by the inclusion of a particular zoning map authorized by the Mesa zoning code and attached to the petition. Nothing inherent in the context of § 19-121(E) required a "legal description" to be interpreted to mean a hypertechnical recitation of property boundaries having no meaning or relevance to the citizens considering the petition. The trial court also properly rejected the challenge to the validity of the referendum petitions based on the Mesa nonresidency of circulators who were otherwise qualified to register to vote in Arizona, as a local residency requirement for petition circulators would have been unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. The requirement of a legal description was met by the inclusion of a particular zoning map authorized by the city's zoning code and attached to the referendum petition. Signatures on petitions obtained by nonresidents of city were not invalid.

In re Leon G.


1 CA-MH 00-0004


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


199 Ariz. 375; 18 P.3d 169; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 21; 341 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 26



February 15, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION WAS VACATED BY THE COURT. 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] ORDERED: Petition for Review - GRANTED.
FURTHER ORDERED: The case shall be set for oral argument. The matter is consolidated for oral argument with CV-01-0063-SA, State of Arizona vs. Hon. Ehrlich et al/Walker.
FURTHER ORDERED: The parties may file simultaneous supplemental briefs, not to exceed 20 pages in length, no later than 30 days from the date of this Court's minute letter.
FURTHER ORDERED: The stay previously entered shall remain in effect pending final disposition by this Court.
Vacated: Arizona v. Ehrlich, 2002 Ariz. LEXIS 230 (Ariz. Dec. 16, 2002).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Yuma County. Cause No. SC98M00050. The Honorable Kirby Kongable, Judge.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Superior Court of Yuma County (Arizona) committing him to the state hospital as a sexually violent person following a jury trial conducted pursuant to the Sexually Violent Persons Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 36-3701 through 36-3716 (Supp. 2000).


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty to five counts of child molestation and one count of sexual abuse and was sentenced to prison. Appellant was required to serve at least two-thirds of his sentence before becoming eligible for release. Prior to his prison release, he was screened to determine his status as a sexually violent person. The screening psychologist opined that he suffered from a paraphilia that predisposed him to commit sexual acts to such a degree as to render him a danger to the health and safety of others and that made him likely to engage in acts of sexual violence. A jury found that appellant was a sexually violent person, and the trial court ordered appellant to be civilly committed to the state hospital. The appellate court reversed. Application of the Sexually Violent Persons Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 36-3701 through 36-3716 (Supp. 2000), to appellant was a collateral rather than direct consequence of his guilty plea; therefore he need not have been informed of this prospect at the time of his plea. However, the appellate court held that the act was unconstitutional, because the act did not require volitional impairment; thus it escaped a saving interpretation.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed, because the Arizona's sexually violent predator act was unconstitutional.

569 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Circle K Stores, Inc. v. Apache County


1 CA-TX 00-0002


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T


199 Ariz. 402; 18 P.3d 713; 2001 Ariz. App. LEXIS 17; 340 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 10



February 8, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Joint Petition for Review Denied October 5, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Ariz. LEXIS 198.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Arizona Tax Court. Cause Nos. TX 97-00378, TX 97-00413, and TX 98-00269. The Honorable Jeffrey S. Cates, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants contested a decision of the Arizona Tax Court granting summary judgment for appellees in appellants' action wherein they contended that they were entitled pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-280 to claim property tax exemptions for personal property located at each of their business locations.


OVERVIEW: Appellant corporations operating multi-location businesses throughout Arizona brought an action challenging appellee counties' decisions that appellants were entitled pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-280 to only a single, statewide property tax exemption in 1997 and 1998, rather than a maximum $ 50,000 exemption for personal property located at each of appellants' business locations. The tax court granted summary judgment for appellees and appellants challenged that decision. The appellate court affirmed. The appellate court was to interpret the term "taxpayer" in § 42-280 so that it conformed to the grant of authority set forth in Ariz. Const. art. 9, § 2(6). The term "taxpayer" in art. 9, § 2(6) and § 42-280 plainly referred to a person or entity that owned personal property used for agricultural, trade, or business purposes and who paid tax on such property. To the extent that art. 9, § 2(6) conflicted with the Uniformity Clause of the Arizona Constitution, Ariz. Const. art. 9, § 1, the specific authority granted by art. 9, § 2(6) controlled.


OUTCOME: Tax court's grant of summary judgment for appellees was affirmed. Word "taxpayer" in state property tax provision referred to person or entity owning personal property and paying tax on such property, such that appellants were not entitled to exemptions at each of their business locations.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his convictions and sentences for 2 counts of first-degree murder and 11 other offenses arising from the same shooting, in the Superior Court, Maricopa County (Arizona).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with two counts of first-degree murder in a drive-by gang-related shooting. The jury convicted appellant of all charges. Seeking review, appellant argued that the trial court improperly permitted the prosecutor to use a peremptory strike to remove a juror based on religion in violation of Batson and Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 12. The court affirmed, holding that although the juror's religious views were intertwined with other factors, including her employment by the Catholic Diocese, her religious membership was not the basis for striking her from the jury panel, and her opposition to capital punishment was a legitimate basis for exercising a peremptory strike.

Jackson v. Tangreen


1 CA-CV 99-0542


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


199 Ariz. 306; 18 P.3d 100; 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 183; 337 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 50



December 26, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied October 9, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 9518.
Petition for Review DENIED on May 23, 2001 by Arizona Supreme Court CV 01-0036-PR.
Record returned to the Court of Appeals, Division One, Phoenix, this 30th day of May, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Yavapai County. Cause No. DO 94-0203. The Honorable Robert M. Brutinel, Judge The Honorable Howard D. Hinson, Jr., Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged the order of the Superior Court in Yavapai County (Arizona) denying their petition to terminate appellee's visitation with their child.


OVERVIEW: Appellee had been judicially granted visitation with her grandchildren under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 25-409. Appellant wife's new husband petitioned to adopt the children, and the trial court granted appellee's petition for continuation of visitation. Appellant husband was allowed to adopt the children, and appellants petitioned to terminate appellee's visitation. The petition was denied by the trial court, and appellants sought review. Section 25-409 did not unconstitutionally infringe upon a parent's right to control the rearing of their child, was rationally related to the state's legitimate interest in fostering relationships between grandparents and grandchildren, and did not violate due process because it gave weight to the visitation decisions of the child's parent. The statute superseded the statute providing that, upon adoption, the adopting parent would have the same relationship with the child as if the child were born to that parent in lawful wedlock. The statute did not offend equal protection when it provided that all visitation would terminate upon the child's adoption but provided an exemption to this in the case of a stepparent adoption.


OUTCOME: The trial court was affirmed because the statute allowing appellee to continue to have visitation with appellants' children after the children's adoption by appellant father was constitutional, superseded the statute giving an adopting parent the rights of a natural parent, and did not impermissibly distinguish between two-parent adoptions and stepparent adoptions.

Andrews v. Eddie's Place, Inc.


2 CA-CV 99-0162


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


199 Ariz. 240; 16 P.3d 801; 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 185; 337 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 40



December 26, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. C-331803. Honorable Deborah Bernini, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment from the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), granting appellee's motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: Appellant filed a cause of action against appellee alleging it was negligent in selling intoxicating beverages to a motorist who was later involved in an automobile accident with appellant and her minor child. Appellee moved for dismissal, claiming the action was barred by the one-year statute of limitations in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-541. The trial court granted the motion, and this appeal followed. The court reviewed de novo the trial court's dismissal based on its application of a statute of limitations. Because appellant based her cause of action, in part, on that common law liability, the one-year statute of limitations in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-541(5) did not apply. The court therefore concluded that the two-year statute of limitations in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-542(1) applied to appellant's common law cause of action against appellee, rather than the one-year limitations period in § 12-541(5).


OUTCOME: The judgment of dismissal was reversed as to the cause of action and remanded the case for further proceedings. A two year statute of limitations was the applicable statute.

State v. Anderson

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction and sentences handed down by the Maricopa County (Arizona) Superior Court, for stalking, threats and intimidation, criminal damage, attempted aggravated assault, and aggravated assault.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of stalking, threats and intimidation, criminal damage, attempted aggravated assault, and aggravated assault. Appellant sought review, arguing that the stalking statute was unconstitutionally vague. The court of appeals affirmed in part and reversed in part, holding that the stalking statute, Ariz. Rev. Finally, the fact that appellant was shot while committing one of the offenses was not a mitigating factor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part, holding that (1) the stalking statute was unconstitutionally vague; (2) a hearing was required to determine whether appellant understood the consequences of admitting to prior felonies at sentencing; (3) the misdemeanor charges were properly heard by the jury; and (4) being shot while committing one of the crimes was not a mitigating factor.

In re Moises L.


1 CA-JV 00-0121


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


199 Ariz. 432; 18 P.3d 1231; 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 189; 340 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 14



December 12, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Redesignated as Opinion By Order Filed, January 29, 2001. As Amended February 8, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. JV 141935. The Honorable Eileen Willett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his adjudication of delinquency for failing to provide evidence of identity from the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) contending a suspect's verbal responses to identifying questions could constitute the evidence of identity required under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1595(B); and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1595(B) was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was stopped by a Phoenix police officer for making a left turn without using a proper turn signal. He had no driver's license, nor could he provide documentary identification. The statute did not expressly state whether evidence of identity needed to be documentary or whether verbal evidence could suffice. The court found the legislature required that an unlicensed operator's "evidence of identity" contain the operator's name, date of birth, address, physical description, and signature. The legislature was demonstrably attempting to require an operator who lacked a driver's license to provide a source of functionally equivalent identification. The court found appellant's argument that an operator could satisfy the statutory requirement by answering a series of questions and providing a signature made literal but not common sense. The statute contemplated a single, tangible, documentary piece of evidence whose contents satisfied the entire statutory list. Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1595(B) was sufficiently definite to provide notice to Arizona drivers that they must carry evidence of identity in a form comparable in content and reliability to a driver's license.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Evidence of identity needed to be documentary not verbal when motorist was stopped by police. Uncorroborated verbal responses did not satisfy the concern to provide a source of verification of driver's identity. Because a person of ordinary intelligence could understand the identification requirement, the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.

State v. Kessler


1 CA-CR 99-0988


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


199 Ariz. 83; 13 P.3d 1200; 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 164; 334 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 9



November 14, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Yuma County. Cause No. SC97C00879. The Honorable Thomas A. Thode, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a sex offender on probation, claimed the Superior Court in Yuma County (Arizona) erred in revoking his probation. He claimed the probation conditions violated U.S. Const. amend. I and denied him equal protection, and that the revocation of his probation violated due process.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was a participant in a sex offender supervision program. His probation was revoked because he initiated, established, and maintained contact with minors. He claimed that the probation regulations were overbroad and that they violated his constitutional rights. A reasonable relationship clearly existed between the requirement that appellant not have unsupervised contact with children and the goals of rehabilitation and protecting the public. There was no evidence of selective enforcement of regulations. State's alleged failure to pursue all violations was not a sufficient basis for a successful equal protection claim. Appellant's claim that it was fundamentally unfair for the trial court to conclude that he violated his probation when he had received permission to attend the retreat was rejected. Petition to revoke was premised on specific acts committed on the retreat.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Reasonable relationship existed between regulations and probationary goals. Appellant did not show that regulations were enforced in a discriminatory manner. There was no fundamental unfairness; revocation was based on specific acts that were not authorized as part of retreat.

State v. Welch


1 CA-CR 99-0324


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C

October 26, 2000, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Yavapai County. Cause No. CR 98-0183 The Honorable Raymond W. Weaver Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his convictions of manufacturing methamphetamine, possession of chemicals and equipment for the purpose of manufacturing methamphetamine, and possession of drug paraphernalia, in the Yavapai County Superior Court (Arizona), arguing that the convictions violated the Double Jeopardy Clauses of the state and federal constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted after being found in a methamphetamine laboratory and having a glass pipe found in his apartment. He appealed, contending that his convictions for possession of chemicals and equipment for the purpose of manufacturing methamphetamine and for possession of drug paraphernalia were lesser-included offenses of manufacturing methamphetamine. On appeal, the court vacated appellant's possession of chemicals and equipment conviction because it was a lesser-included offense of manufacturing methamphetamine because appellant could not have committed the offense of manufacturing methamphetamine under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3407(A)(4) without possessing the chemicals and equipment to do so under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3407(A)(3). However, the appellate court affirmed appellant's possession of drug paraphernalia conviction, as it was not a lesser-included offense, because the drug paraphernalia offense under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3415 contained elements not required under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3407(A)(4).


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed insofar as it convicted appellant of possession of chemicals and equipment because it was a lesser-included offense of manufacturing methamphetamine, and therefore conviction of both violated appellant's double jeopardy protections. Appellant's conviction of possession of drug paraphernalia affirmed because it was not a lesser-included offense of manufacturing methamphetamine.

SAL Leasing, Inc. v. State ex rel. Napolitano

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State appealed from a declaratory judgment by the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona), which held that the Consumer Lenders Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 6-601 to -638 (1999), did not apply to appellee company. Appellant State also appealed the trial court's dismissal of its counterclaim and denial of its request for injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: Appellee company provided money to customers in the form of a sale and lease-back transaction which required the customer to transfer title to his or her vehicle to the company and the company would have leased the vehicle back to the customer. Appellant State counterclaimed and alleged the transactions were usurious under the Consumer Lenders Act. The trial court concluded the transactions were not consumer loans within the meaning of the Consumer Lenders Act and that appellees had effectively shut down all operations shortly after the counterclaim was filed. The court concluded that appellees' transactions were consumer loans in which vehicle title transfers served as security devices, and not bona fide sales. The court further held that substantial evidence supported the trial court's denial of injunctive relief.


OUTCOME: The court found as a matter of law that the transactions constituted consumer loans, reversed the trial court's holding that appellees' sale and lease-back transactions did not violate the Consumer Lenders Act, affirmed the trial court's denial of injunctive relief, and remanded appellant State's claims for violations of the Arizona Consumer Fraud Act and the Organized Crime and Fraud Act for further proceedings.

State v. Donald


1 CA-CR 97-0551-PR


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


198 Ariz. 406; 10 P.3d 1193; 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 142; 331 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



September 26, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on March 20, 2001. Certiorari Denied October 1, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 5646.
Justice Martone voted to grant review.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 93-01516. The Honorable Frank T. Galati, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVIEW GRANTED; RELIEF GRANTED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a petition for review of the Superior Court of Maricopa County's (Arizona) summary dismissal of his petition for post-conviction relief, in a suit to determine whether petitioner's loss of a favorable plea bargain because of ineffective assistance of counsel inflicted a constitutionally significant injury upon him, since he had received a fair trial.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner sought review of the trial court's summary dismissal of his petition for post-conviction relief. Petitioner claimed that he had rejected a favorable plea agreement because his counsel provided ineffective assistance by failing to properly explain the relative merits of the plea offer in comparison with the potential sentence that he faced if convicted of the charges. The court held, first, that petitioner suffered a constitutionally significant injury when he rejected the favorable plea agreement as a result of his counsel's ineffective assistance. Second, petitioner's rejection of the favorable plea agreement was not relieved by his receipt of a fair trial. Third, the trial court could, without violating separation of powers, fashion a remedy for the deprivation of petitioner's right to effective assistance, including, if warranted under the circumstances, ordering respondent to reinstate the original plea offer. Consequently, the summary dismissal of the petition for post-conviction relief was reversed, and the case was remanded for a hearing on the merits of the petition, and if necessary, for the determination of appropriate relief.


OUTCOME: The summary dismissal of the petition for post-conviction relief was reversed, because petitioner had presented a colorable claim that his counsel's ineffective assistance caused him to reject the plea agreement and proceed to trial. The case was remanded for an evidentiary hearing regarding petitioner's ineffective assistance of counsel claim, and if necessary, for a further hearing to determine the appropriate relief.

 

582 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Alawy


1 CA-CR 99-0882


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


198 Ariz. 363; 9 P.3d 1102; 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 139; 330 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 5



September 14, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. LC 99-00145. The Honorable Daniel A. Barker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) that affirmed the judgment convicting him of violating Mesa City Code § 11-7-6(A), which prohibited the residential use of property zoned for an industrial purpose. Appellant asserted that § 11-7-6(A) was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted in municipal court of using the warehouse of his moving business as his personal residence in violation of Mesa City Code § 11-7-6(A). The trial court affirmed the conviction, finding that § 11-7-6(A) was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad. Appellant challenged that decision. On appeal, the court affirmed. Although the evidence was sufficient to conclude that appellant had violated § 11-7-6(A), which prohibited the residential use of property zoned for an industrial purpose, the trial court made no findings of fact, and thus the court was forced to address the facial validity of § 11-7-6(A). The court held that the language of § 11-7-6(A) clearly conveyed to the reader that the prohibition was that one could not set up a residence on industrially zoned property, and that a person of ordinary intelligence could distinguish at what point he had set up a residence from merely performing incidental activities that could also be performed in the home. Also, police officers testified that § 11-7-6(A) was necessary to ensure public safety. Thus, the court held that § 11-7-6(A) was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed; appellant violated the city zoning regulation prohibiting residential use of property zoned for an industrial purpose. The zoning regulation at issue plainly conveyed to the reader what activity was prohibited, that the regulation was necessary to enure public safety, and that the regulation was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad.

 

583 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wood


1 CA-CR 99-0896


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


198 Ariz. 275; 8 P.3d 1189; 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 134; 329 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 11



August 31, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on February 15, 2001 by Arizona Supreme Court CR-00-0492-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Coconino County. Cause No. CR 98-944. The Honorable Charles D. Adams, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State claimed that the Superior Court in Coconino County (Arizona) erred when it dismissed an indictment charging appellee father with custodial interference after finding that Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-1302 (Supp. 1999) required an ongoing court proceeding concerning custody.


OVERVIEW: Appellee took his son out of state without the mother's notice. Appellant State charged him with custodial interference under Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-1302 (Supp. 1999). The lower court held that this statute required an ongoing court proceeding concerning custody before a person could be charged with custodial interference. However, a common-sense reading of the language of § 13-1302(A)(2) compelled the court to hold that pending custody proceedings were not a prerequisite to a prosecution for custodial interference. By its own terms, the statute covered any act of custodial interference that took place before the entry of a court order regardless of whether there was a pending court action. Legislature intended to prohibit one parent from denying the other parent lawful contact with his or her children under all circumstances. Judgment reversed.


OUTCOME: Dismissal was improper. Trial court erred in holding that criminal interference statute required pendency of a custody proceeding before appellee could be charged with custodial interference. Statute covered any act of custodial interference taking place prior to the entry of a court order.

 

584 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Petrak


1 CA-CR 99-0730


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


198 Ariz. 260; 8 P.3d 1174; 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 133; 329 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 7



August 31, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Amended By Order Filed September 11, 2000. Petition for Review DENIED on March 20, 2001 by Arizona Supreme Court CR 00-0535-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Yavapai County. Cause No. CR 98-0068. The Honorable Robert M. Brutinel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction entered by the Superior Court in Yavapai County (Arizona) for misconduct involving weapons pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3102(A)(8) (Supp. 1999).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for misconduct involving weapons pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3102(A)(8) (Supp. 1999), contending that the trial court erred in failing to instruct the jury that the charge required proof that defendant possessed the weapons in relation to the underlying crime of possessing marijuana. Defendant also contended that the charging indictment was duplicitous. The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded for a new trial. In order to convict a defendant under the weapons misconduct statute, the State was required to prove that the defendant intended to use or could have used the weapon to further the felony drug offense underlying the weapons misconduct charge. On that basis, the trial court erred in instructing the jury pertaining to the weapons misconduct statute, and such error misled the jurors regarding the legal principles to apply in determining guilt. Also, the indictment inadequately defined the weapons misconduct charge and failed to notify defendant of what evidence would be presented against him, so as to handicap his defense.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed and case was remanded for a new trial. Trial court failed to properly instruct jury that in order to convict defendant under weapons misconduct statute State had to prove that defendant intended to use or could have used the weapon to further the underlying drug offense.

U. S.West Communs., Inc. v. Arizona Corp. Comm'n


1 CA-CV 98-0672


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


198 Ariz. 208; 8 P.3d 396; 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 125; 329 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 18

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] ORDERED; Petition for Review [Appellee Electric Lightwave] = GRANTED.

FURTHER ORDERED: Appellees' Petition for Review [Arizona Corporation Commission] = GRANTED.
FURTHER ORDERED: The case shall be set for oral argument.
FURTHER ORDERED: The parties may file simultaneous supplemental briefs, not to exceed 20 pages in length, no later than 30 days from the date of this Court's minute letter.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause Nos. CV 96-18667, CV 96-18668, CV 97-00157, CV 97-05563, CV 97-05564, CV 97-06427, CV 97-06428, CV 97-06429, CV 97-13774, CV 97-14801, CV 97-21835 (Consolidated). The Honorable Rebecca A. Albrecht, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the ruling of the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona), which upheld the decision of the Arizona Corporation Commission to grant certificates of convenience and necessity to appellees pursuant to Ariz. Admin. Code R14-2-1101 through R14-2-1115, and rejected appellant's argument that this violated equal protection.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, 11 telecommunications companies, applied to appellee state corporation commission for competitive certificates of convenience and necessity (CC&Ns) in order to enter the Arizona local exchange and "intraLATA" markets. Appellant telephone company intervened in each application. The appellee commission granted competitive CC&Ns to each of the telecommunications appellees without inquiring into the fair value of their investments in property held within the state and determining a reasonable rate of return on those investments, or imposing a carrier-of-last-resort obligation on them, as it did on appellant. The district court affirmed. On appeal, the court affirmed in part, because appellant had yet to apply for a competitive CC&N of its own, so its claim based on disparate treatment was not ripe for review. The court reversed in part and remanded, holding that appellee commission was required to ascertain the fair value of property owned by all public service corporations when setting their rates, under Ariz. Const. art. 15, § 14.


OUTCOME: The district court judgment was affirmed in part, because appellant's equal protection claim was not yet ripe for review. The judgment was reversed in part and remanded, because appellee commission was required by the state constitution to determine fair value rate bases for all public service corporations in the state before setting their rates.

Arizona Dep't of Revenue v. Care Computer Sys., Inc.


1 CA-TX 98-0003


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T


197 Ariz. 414; 4 P.3d 469; 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 114; 326 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 19



July 25, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied February 15, 2001, ASC #CV 00-0349-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Arizona Tax Court. Cause No. TX 95-00642. The Honorable William J. Schafer, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff agency appealed the summary judgment granted to defendant by the Arizona Tax Court, which held that defendant did not have a substantial nexus with the state warranting a transaction privilege tax under the Commerce Clause.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff agency, the Arizona Department of Revenue, assessed a state retail transaction privilege tax on defendant, an out-of-state company. Plaintiff agency appealed a summary judgment which was granted to defendant based on a finding that defendant did not have a substantial nexus with the state under the Commerce Clause. The appellate court reversed and remanded with directions to grant judgment to plaintiff agency. The substantial nexus was established by defendant's salespersons' and trainers' trips to the state which were intendced to, and did, result in additional sales of defendant's products. Since the tax could not be imposed on defendant's customers, the sales tax could be imposed by plaintiff agency on defendant.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment was reversed and remanded with directions to grant judgment to plaintiff agency. Because the tax could not be imposed on defendant's customers under constitutitional principles, plaintiff agency could lawfully impose the sales tax on defendant.

State v. Watson


1 CA-CR 99-0342


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


198 Ariz. 48; 6 P.3d 752; 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 102



July 3, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] ORDERED: Petition for Review = DENIED January 9, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. LC 98-00099. The Honorable David R. Cole, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona), affirming his Phoenix Municipal Court conviction for violating the City of Phoenix's neighborhood preservation ordinance due to the condition of defendant's premises. Defendant appealed pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22-375 (1990), alleging the unconstitutionality of the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued a Phoenix ordinance violated substantive due process. He invoked the fundamental right to privacy, identifying "the sanctity and privacy of the home" as the interest at stake. The court viewed defendant's request as seeking protection of a right to keep an accumulation of debris in his yard. A right that not only was not fundamental but did not exist. The court held safeguarding the general health, safety, and welfare of the community and protecting aesthetic values by avoiding visual clutter were proper goals for municipal government. The court found the ordinance adequately restricted its scope so as to target only conditions that the city could have legitimately regulated. Consequently, the ordinance's means of achieving its objectives were reasonable. The ordinance passed rational basis scrutiny and was facially constitutional.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because safeguarding the general health, safety, and welfare of the community and protecting aesthetic values by avoiding visual clutter were proper goals for municipal government. The ordinance's means of achieving its objectives were reasonable, passed rational basis scrutiny and were facially constitutional.

 

588 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


In re Paul M.


2 CA-JV 99-0064


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


198 Ariz. 122; 7 P.3d 131; 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 96; 325 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 37



June 15, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF COCHISE COUNTY. Cause No. JV99000073. Honorable Charles A. Irwin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minor appealed adjudication of the Cochise County Superior Court (Arizona), which found appellant delinquent for knowingly abusing a teacher or other school employee engaged in the performance of duties, in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 15-507.


OVERVIEW: The sole question presented on appeal was whether, by repeatedly telling a teacher's aide to "f--- off," appellant knowingly abused a school employee, in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 15-507. The court vacated the delinquency adjudication, disagreeing with the State's contention that the terms "insult" and "abuse" were essentially synonymous or that "to insult" was necessarily also "to abuse." The court concluded that the 1989 amendment to § 15-507, which expressly deleted "insults" from the statute reflected legislative intent that insulting words alone would no longer qualify as criminal abuse under the statute. Appellant did not call the aide names, did not make an obscene gesture, and did not intimidate her. Although appellant's behavior was insolent and offensive, his words did not attack, injure, disparage, revile, or denounce the aide personally. Therefore, trial court erred as a matter of law in finding appellant responsible for violating § 15-507.


OUTCOME: Adjudication vacated; trial court erred in finding that appellant knowingly abused a school employee where appellant, although he used vulgarity, had a rude attitude, and talked back to the employee, did not attack, injure, disparage, revile, or denounce the employee personally.

Graville v. Dodge

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. DR 97-90192 The Honorable Cheryl K. Hendrix, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parent challenged the contempt of visitation order from the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona), which found that he had violated an order providing for visitation between appellees and their two granddaughters.


OVERVIEW: Appellee grandparents' attempted to obtain visitation with their two granddaughters under Arizona's grandparents' visitation rights statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 25-409 (Supp. 1999). Appellant parent challenged the provisions of a visitation order appointing a doctor to supervise compliance and provide therapeutic intervention. Appellant argued that by invoking the statute to appoint the doctor, the trial court impermissibly gave statutory protections to appellees that the legislature intended only to extend to parents. The court disagreed. It found no reason why the legislature would allow the trial courts discretion to order supervision for parent visitation, but deny such relief for grandparent visitation. The court also found that the order was neither vague nor ambiguous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the contempt of visitation order against appellant, holding that the legislature intended to allow the trial court to order supervised visitation under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 25-410(B) in grandparent visitation cases.

Arizona Dep't of Revenue v. Dougherty


1 CA-SA 99-0084


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT C


198 Ariz. 1; 6 P.3d 306; 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 74; 321 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 35



May 18, 2000, Filed

FURTHER ORDERED: The case shall be set for oral argment.
FURTHER ORDERED: The parties may file simultaneous supplemental briefs, not to exceed 20 pages in length, no later than 30 days from the date of this Court's minute letter.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. TX 97-00075. The Honorable Bernard J. Dougherty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED, RELIEF GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Arizona Department of Revenue appealed an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), seeking special action review of a tax court ruling that certified a class action for taxpayers and ordered petitioner to bear the cost of notifying potential class members.


OVERVIEW: Arizona allowed a deduction from income for dividends received from corporations doing more than half of their business in Arizona. Respondent putative class challenged as unconstitutional the denial of similar deductions for dividends received from corporations not doing more than half of their business in Arizona during the same tax years. The trial court certified the class and petitioner Arizona Department of Revenue appealed, seeking to avoid the high cost of giving notice to potential class members and seeking appellate court jurisdiction because legal issues of statewide importance were involved. The court affirmed that taxpayers could bring a class action because Ariz. R. Civ. P. 23 applied to tax actions. However, class certification did not negate the requirement of Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 42-124, 42-129(E), and 42-1118(E), that each taxpayer must individually exhaust their administrative remedies by filing an individual refund claim.


OUTCOME: Class action suit was allowed because rules of civil procedure expressly applied to tax court proceedings, but the class was limited to those taxpayers who filed individual administrative claims, because the statutory requirement that each plaintiff exhausted his administrative remedies still applied.

State v. Cotton


1 CA-CR 99-0180


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


197 Ariz. 584; 5 P.3d 918; 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 73; 321 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 19



May 16, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] ORDERED: Petition for Review DENIED by Arizona Supreme Court CR-00-0370-PR December 5, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 97-09388. The Honorable Thomas Dunevant, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant with two counts of reckless second degree murder. The jury in the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) however, found him guilty of two lesser-included counts of reckless manslaughter. Defendant appealed, raising two issues.


OVERVIEW: The defendant accidentally shot his girlfriend, when she was eight and one-half months pregnant. Although she died shortly after arriving at the hospital, her daughter was delivered alive. But the fatal injury to the mother had so decreased the blood supply to the baby that the infant died the following day. Defendant's appeal raised an issue of first impression: whether a newborn child who died from injuries inflicted while the child was in utero was a "person" within the meaning of Arizona's homicide statutes. Defendant contended that because the injury was inflicted on a fetus, the victim was not a "person" within the meaning of the homicide statutes. The judgment was affirmed. Because the infant was undeniably a "person" at the time of her death a day after the shooting, it was irrelevant that the injuries that led to her death were inflicted while she was still in utero.


OUTCOME: Holding that Arizona's homicide statutes applied to the killing of a child born alive, even if the death resulted from injuries inflicted before birth and also that the trial court did not err in defining reasonable doubt as mandated by its supreme court, the convictions and sentences were affirmed.

 

592 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Preston


2 CA-CR 98-0524


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


197 Ariz. 461; 4 P.3d 1004; 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 71; 317 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



March 14, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. CR-60212. Honorable Richard Fields, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed conviction for drug charges in Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) alleging that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-206 unconstitutionally required clear and convincing proof of entrapment and unconstitutionally eliminated requirement for jury instructions concerning presumption of innocence and government's burden of proof.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of drug charges and alleged that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-206, governing the defense of entrapment, was unconstitutional since it required defendant to prove the defense by clear and convincing evidence and improperly limited jury instructions. The court held that the affirmative defense of entrapment was not of constitutional dimension and requiring proof of the defense by clear and convincing evidence was not unconstitutionally onerous since it did not lessen the government's burden to prove every element of the offense beyond a reasonable doubt. However, the presumption of innocence and the government's burden of proof were fundamental constitutional guarantees which were violated by requiring the court to instruct the jury only on the defense of entrapment, even where the defendant admitted every element of the offenses as required by the statute. The unconstitutional subsection of the statute was severable from the remainder of the statute, however, and did not require a finding of invalidity with regard to the entire statute.


OUTCOME: Conviction was reversed; requiring proof of entrapment defense by clear and convincing evidence was not unconstitutional but, even though defense required defendant to admit every element of offenses, defendant was nonetheless entitled to jury instructions concerning presumption of defendant's innocence and government's burden to prove offenses beyond reasonable doubt.

Brush Wellman, Inc. v. Lee


2 CA-SA 99-0124


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


196 Ariz. 344; 996 P.2d 1248; 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 35; 316 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 62

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employer filed a petition for a special action proceeding after respondent Pima County Court, Arizona, judge denied petitioner's motion for reconsideration of his decision to honor plaintiffs' notice of a peremptory change of judge in the underlying action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, former and current employees of petitioner, and their spouses filed complaints against petitioner alleging the employees had contracted chronic lung disease after being exposed to beryllium while working for petitioner. Plaintiffs filed a notice of change of judge pursuant to Ariz. R. Civ. P. 42(f)(1), thereby exercising their right to a peremptory change of judge. The case was reassigned to a new judge, who granted petitioner's motion for summary judgment on all claims. Summary judgment was reversed and the case was remanded. On remand, the case was assigned to respondent judge because trial court judge had retired. Plaintiffs filed another notice of change of judge. The case was again reassigned. On special action review, the court held respondent acted in excess of his authority in honoring plaintiffs' second peremptory change of judge. OUTCOME: Trial judge's order reassigning the underlying case to a new judge on remand was reversed; plaintiffs' could not peremptorily challenge a judge upon remand because they had already exercised that right before appeal and remand.

Stout v. State Compensation Fund


1 CA-CV 98-0652


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT B


197 Ariz. 238; 3 P.3d 1158; 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 21; 314 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 38



February 8, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petiton for Review DENIED on October 29, 2002 by Arizona Supreme Court CV 00-0418PR. Released for Publication November 25, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CV 97-12857. The Honorable Michael J. O'Melia, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) decision that, under Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23-1023, any settlement of third-party claims seeking recovery for medical expenses, wrongful death, and loss of consortium must be approved by appellee, State Compensation Fund, which had already compensated decedent's survivors.


OVERVIEW: Decedent died of complications from work-related injuries and appellee, Arizona State Compensation Fund, paid benefits to appellants, decedent's wife, child, and mother, and claimed lien for amount of workers' compensation paid. Appellants subsequently sued a product manufacturer, and sought judicial declaratory judgment that appellee's consent not required to settle lawsuit. Trial court held under Arizona law, any settlement agreement must be approved by appellee, equitable apportionment did not apply, and appellee's lien applied to amounts recovered for loss of consortium. Appellate court affirmed, reversing only with respect to decedent's mother. Equitable apportionment did not apply when third-party action in a workers' compensation setting was resolved by settlement, appellee did not breach its duty of good faith and fair dealing when parties agreed to a compromise on the lien and appellee failed to approve the proposed settlement. In addition, a workers' compensation lien against loss of consortium recovery was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Decision that under Arizona law any settlement of third-party claims must be approved by appellee affirmed. Equitable apportionment did not apply to case, appellee did not breach its duty of good faith and fair dealing in failing to approve proposed settlement, and workers' compensation lien against loss of consortium constitutional.
