Hilgeman v. Am. Mortg. Sec., Inc.


2 CA-CV 98-0236


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT A


196 Ariz. 215; 994 P.2d 1030; 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 16; 314 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 15



January 27, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PINAL COUNTY. Cause No. CV97045336. Honorable James E. Don, Judge. Honorable Richard L. McAnally, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; VACATED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Superior Court of Pinal County (Arizona) which denied defendant's motion to set aside a default judgment which awarded compensatory and punitive damages to plaintiffs on their tort claims.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs purchased a home secured with a mortgage from defendant. Shortly thereafter, defendant assigned the mortgage to a bank. Plaintiffs, claiming they did not receive notice of the transfer, sent their mortgage payment to defendant. Defendant negotiated the check and did not forward the payment to the bank. Plaintiff sued defendant alleging various tort theories. Defendant was defaulted when it failed to timely appear in the action. The trial court awarded compensatory and punitive damages. On appeal, the court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in finding that defendant corporation had been properly served with process. Further, the court affirmed the compensatory damages award. However, because the record was insufficient to evaluate the punitive damages award, the court vacated the award and remanded the case for a contested evidentiary hearing on the amount of punitive damages to be assessed against defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the compensatory damages award but vacated the punitive damages award because the record was insufficient for evaluation. Therefore, the court remanded the case for a contested evidentiary hearing on the amount of punitive damages to be assessed against defendant.

 

597 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Kerr v. Killian


1 CA-TX 98-0014


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT T


197 Ariz. 213; 3 P.3d 1133; 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 75; 319 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 28



January 27, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Amended Opinion Filed April 13, 2000. Petition for Review Denied December 7, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Arizona Tax Court. Cause Nos. TX 97-00119, TX 97-00131, and TX 97-00150 The Honorable Jeffrey Cates, Judge The Honorable I. Sylvan Brown, Judge Opinion Below Kerr v. Killian, 191 Ariz. 293, 955 P.2d 49 (Tax Ct. 1998).

Original Opinion of January 27, 2000, Previously Reported at: 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 14.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an award of the Arizona Tax Court of fees to attorneys who successfully represented taxpayers on a refund claim.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from an award of the tax court of fees to attorneys who successfully represented appellee taxpayers and those similarly situated on a refund claim. The factual background of the case concerned the pre-1991 exemption in Arizona from state income tax of the amount of money state and local government employees paid into retirement plans. In 1989, the United States Supreme Court invalidated a similar tax provision because no exemption was afforded federal employees. In that year, five taxpayers, who were federal employees and who were appellees in the case, sued defendant, seeking a declaration that the Arizona tax scheme violated 4 U.S.C.S. § 111. After years of legal proceedings, the Arizona governor ordered refunds. Appellees asked that their attorneys be awarded 20 per cent of the refunds. The tax court ruled that the common fund doctrine applied and that appellees' attorneys were entitled to an award of reasonable fees. The court was persuaded that the recovery at issue properly constituted a common fund for purposes of shifting attorney's fees under the common-fund doctrine, and it affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because the tax court did not err in awarding fees under the common fund doctrine, and the fee award was reasonable. Additionally, defendant did not have standing to assert the due process rights of the non-party taxpayers.

 

598 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Hispanic Broadcasters of Tucson, Inc.


2 CA-CV 99-0035


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION TWO, DEPARTMENT B


196 Ariz. 597; 2 P.3d 687; 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 15; 15 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1772; 314 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 24



January 27, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: A Petition for Review was filed and DENIED by order of the Arizona Supreme Court.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY. Cause No. 326242. Honorable Robert Donfeld, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged a Pima County Superior Court (Arizona) order granting summary judgment in favor of appellee employer on the grounds that appellant was precluded from bringing his wrongful termination suit pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1501.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sued appellee, his employer, for wrongful termination arguing a memorandum between them, which stated that appellee could guarantee a first year income to appellant of a fixed amount, constituted a one-year employment contract entitling him to sue under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1501. When appellant was fired he had neither worked a full year nor earned the specified amount. The trial court granted summary judgment for appellee, concluding that the guarantee clause could not reasonably be interpreted as a written commitment for a specified duration of time because it could be fulfilled in less than one year, and extrinsic evidence was not admissible to supply the required element. The court affirmed, holding that the trial court's analysis was correct. The agreement, even considering extrinsic evidence, concerned salary and could not be interpreted as a restriction of appellee's right to terminate the employment relationship.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment was affirmed. Appellee's first year income guarantee could not reasonably be interpreted as a written commitment for a specified duration of time because it could be fulfilled in less than one year, and extrinsic evidence was not admissible to supply the required element.

 

599 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


In re Juan A.


1 CA-JV 98-0253


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT E


196 Ariz. 183; 993 P.2d 1147; 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 5; 313 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 21



January 20, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. Cause No. JV-520812. The Honorable Thomas A. Jacobs, Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile challenged his delinquency adjudication in the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona) based on factual allegations that he failed to comply with the hearing officer's orders in a predicate truancy case in which he was adjudged an incorrigible child.


OVERVIEW: Adjudicated incorrigible, appellant juvenile failed to submit proof of compliance with the hearing officer's orders. Hearing officer, without notice to appellant, instructed Department of Motor Vehicles to suspend appellant's driving privileges. The state then filed delinquency petition alleging as a factual basis appellant's failure to submit proof of compliance in the incorrigibility case. The hearing officer testified to appellant's non-compliance, and that he advised appellant prior to accepting his admission to truancy only that he would be giving up his right to trial and his right to appeal and could be fined up to $ 150. The appellant was adjudicated delinquent, and appealed. The court, finding the record on appeal showed a high probability that substantial procedural defects existed in the incorrigibility case, suspended the appeal for 60 days, and remanded with directions to allow appellant a reasonable time in which to seek a delayed appeal in the incorrigibility case.


OUTCOME: The court ordered the appeal suspended for 60 days, and the matter remanded with directions to allow appellant juvenile a reasonable time in which to seek a delayed appeal in the incorrigibility case.

 

600 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Clary


1 CA-CR 97-0307


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT A


196 Ariz. 610; 2 P.3d 1255; 2000 Ariz. App. LEXIS 6; 313 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 3



January 20, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review DENIED on May 26, 2000 by Arizona Supreme Court CR-00-0037-PR.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County. Cause No. CR 96-91588. The Honorable Mark W. Armstrong, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his two convictions from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Arizona, for aggravated driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor, alleging his blood sample was illegally obtained.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of aggravated driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor. Defendant appealed these convictions alleging his blood sample, demonstrating an over the legal limit of alcohol content, was illegally obtained by force. The court affirmed the convictions. The court held that a warrant for the blood sample had been properly obtained. The court held that reasonable force was permissible to overcome resistance to execution of a search warrant for the removal of blood.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions, as reasonable force to obtain a blood sample was proper because there was a valid search warrant authorizing the procedure.
